After I completed this book for you, my Sons, which is the last on the science of medicine with its complement, and having reached an end in it through expositions of its contents and its declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you also with this Treatise, which is a part of operations, that is, surgery with hands.
Since the operation with hands is prostrate in our region and at our time, altogether lacking; until perhaps the knowledge of it has perished, and its trace has disappeared, except for some small descriptions in ancient books which have been altered by hand, and error and hesitation have occurred, until the intentions have been closed off, and the force of it has been weakened: It seemed to me that I should revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise in it according to the way from the positions, the declarations, and the abbreviations, and that I should come with forms of iron tools, and the rest of the instruments of work, through addition of declarations and proper use of what is necessary.
The reason why a skilled artist with his hand is not found in this present time, is because the art of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to exercise himself before that in the science of anatomy as Galen narrated, until he knows the remedies of members, their shapes, and their connections, and disconnections, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their number, their exits, veins pulsating and quiet, and places of their exit.
And for this reason, Hippocrates said that name with name is much, and with work it is little, and especially in the art of hands.
We have already said about him at the beginning of this book.
Whoever is not knowing what we have said about anatomy, may already fall into error, in which people are killed: as I have seen many of those who are formed by this science and boast about it without knowledge, and without experiment.
I have seen a foolish physician cut an abscess on a woman's neck, and he accidentally cut some arteries in the neck: therefore, blood flowed from the woman until she fell dead at his hands.
And I have seen another physician who presumed to draw out a stone from an old man, and the stone was large. Therefore, he came to him, and drew it out with a piece of bladder. Wherefore, the man died on the third day.
And indeed I was already called to draw it out; and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the man that he would die.
And I have seen another physician who received a stick at the court of some Duke of our land for his medicine: and there was a black eunuch with him, who sustained a fracture in his leg near the heel; and the physician, with his ignorance, pressed the fracture over an open wound with awls, iron staples, and strong ties, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he cured him according to his own devices. Then he dismissed him for some days and commanded him not to loosen the bandage; and he stood thus until an abscess formed on his leg, and his foot, and it came to ruin.
I was therefore called to him; and I hastened to loosen the bandage; and peace came, and he was freed from his pains.
However, corruption had already become fixed in the limb; and I could not restrain it.
Translation: Place therefore let corruption walk through the member until it perishes.
And I saw another physician who perforated a cancerous apostema: and it was healed afterwards until the evilness of its magnitude with its lord was revealed.
Because when it is a pure cancer from the humor of melancholy, then it is not necessary to approach it with iron entirely, unless it is in a member that can endure, so as to remove all of its extent.
And on account of this it is necessary for you to know that the operation is divided into two divisions: namely, an operation which brings salvation: and an operation with which there is danger in various dispositions.
And I have already awakened in all places of this book where the operation comes, where there is fear and dread.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of this and divide it so that fools do not find a way to speak and shameful things.
Therefore take the measurement with care and protection, and treat your sick ones gently and firmly, and make use of a better way leading by the grace of God to salvation and praiseworthy succession: and leave behind terrible illnesses difficult to heal: and remove from you what makes you fear, so that hesitation enters upon you in faith and comfort.
For it remains more to your glory, and higher in this world, and finally to your profits.
Galen has already said in some of his warnings. Do not treat an evil sickness, lest you be called a bad physician.
Now however I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters. ¶
First Chapter.
On the cautery with fire, and the cautery with sharp medicine, set out, arranged from head to foot, and forms of instruments, and ironwork of the cautery, and all that is necessary for the operation. ¶
Chapter second.
On cutting and perforating, on venesection and cupping, and on wounds; and on the extraction of arrows, and similar matters; and an entire chapter arranged according to the forms of instruments. (paragraph break)
Chapter third.
On restoration and dislocation, on the treatment of twisting and similar matters; arranged from head to foot, and according to the forms of instruments.
Before I remember the operation with him, it is necessary that I say the quality of his remedies and his harmful effects; and in what composition they are presented.
I say therefore, that the discourse on the quality of the remedy of the Cautery, and its harmful effects, is a long, subtle, scientific, and hidden secret.
Also there was a multitude of wise men who disagreed about it; and to me, at least, their many discourses are enough for me, fearing a prolonged debate.
I say therefore, that the Cautery applies universally to every composition, which is with matter and without matter; except for two compositions, which are a hot composition without matter, and a dry composition without matter.
In the hot and dry composition with matter they disagreed. Some indeed said that the Cautery is beneficial in this [hot and dry composition with matter]. And others said the opposite of this [that the Cautery is beneficial in hot and dry composition with matter], namely that the Cautery is not suitable for the sickness which is due to heat and dryness; because the nature of fire is heat; and it is inconvenient to heal a hot and dry disease, when heated by hot and dry.
And he who says the opposite said that by Cautery is beneficial for any hot and dry sickness which happens in human bodies; because when you compare the body of a man and its humidity to the composition of fire, you find the body of a man cold.
And I myself say by his discourse; because he has often revealed that to me in experiment.
Nevertheless, it is not necessary for him to come back to this, unless he who has already been tested and experienced in the last exercise of the chapter on Cautery, and knows the diversity of human compositions, and the disposition of diseases in themselves, and their causes, and accidents thereof, and the space of time of those diseases.
From the remaining body compositions, there is no fear for you: and especially in cold and moist illnesses. For it has agreed all physicians on these: and they did not disagree in helping with cautery in them.
And know, sons, that from the secret of cure by cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with medicine burning, is that fire is simple, whose action does not reach, unless to the member which is being cauterized: and it does not harm another joint connected with it, unless a small damage.
However, the action of medicine burning reaches to what is extended from members: and perhaps it causes illness difficult to heal in a member, and perhaps it kills.
Fire, however, because of its subtlety and goodness of substance, does not do that unless it is excessive.
Now we have understood that through an experiment, because of the length of service and study with art, and position on truth of things: and because of that I excuse myself from the length of speech.
And if it was not forbidden to this book of mine, I would give you the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies, by which it expels illnesses with a philosophical demonstrative speech, which would be understood by your minds.
And know, sons, that they themselves disagree on the time when cautery should be made, and put a better time for it with truth.
And I say that cautery is suitable in every time: therefore, because damage occurring due to the time is drowned in help, which is attracted with cautery. And especially if cautery is for pains from necessary pains, strong, pressing, which cannot endure delay: therefore because it is feared that what may happen from them is greater than a small damage which occurs due to the time.
And let not that thought enter your minds, O sons, that it is only the common people and foolish physicians who believe that there is not always a return for the sickness cured by cautery; and they assume this as a consequence, but the matter is not as they think: because cautery is not, except in place of medicine, which alters complexion, and extracts humidities which are the causes, wherefore pain arises.
However, cautery is superfluous over medicine due to the swiftness of its health, and the strength of its operation, and the power of its dominion: and it is possible that sickness returns at some hour according to the complexion of the sick, and the location of the sickness, and the virtue of the same: and what prepares in his body from an accumulation of superfluities within him: and what reaches him in acquiring it from foods, and similar things due to its causes, except for the sickness in which cautery is administered.
A subtle sickness in a member with few superfluities and humidities, such as the cautery of a tooth, because of pain and similar things, it is possible that that pain does not return in him. But this happens rarely.
However, the speech of the common people is again correct that cautery is the last medicine: not to what they intend in it: because they believe that there is no cure that confers with medicine, nor with anything after the fall of cautery.
But the matter is contrary to theirs and their intention, that cautery is the last medicine, is not, except when we administer modes of cure for a sickness and they do not confer with the same medicine: then we administer cautery at the end of things, and it confers: thence it happens that cautery is the last medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that a cautery with gold is better than a cautery with iron; and they did not say this, if not because of the equality of gold, and the loftiness of its substance; and they said, that it does not cause a place for pus at the site of the cauterization. That is not entirely true; because I have already proven it and found that it does not do this in certain bodies without others.
And a cautery with it (gold) is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you put fire to the cautery from gold in fire, it is not shown to you, when it burns according to the quantity that you want, due to the redness of gold; and when it rushes towards it (the gold) coldness, and if you add more fire to it, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls into this (mistake) due to it; and because of this, a cautery with iron is more quickly and closely made among us for the sake of the operation.
And I myself have already arranged this Chapter (on cautery) in the Cautery, according to chapters; and I have arranged it from head to foot, so that those who are seeking (information on cautery) may find what they want from it.
Chapter II.
Here is the cauterization for the dominion of humidity and coldness over the brain: these two are the causes of soda (seizures), and the flowing multitude of fluids from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and the multitude of sleep, and toothache, and throat pain; and universally all illness that happens due to coldness, such as paralysis, sodae, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
The method of cauterization is to instruct the sick person: first, that the head should be evacuated with a solution of medicine cleaning for three or four nights, depending on the strength of the sick person, their age, and their habit.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor. Then make him sit square between your hands so that he puts his hands on his chest.
Then put the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever your middle finger comes, mark that place with an uncauterized spot.
Then heat the cautery oil: this is its form.
Then put it on the marked uncauterized spot, descending with your hand to tighten it gradually, and you turn it. Then quickly withdraw your hand, and look at the place.
If you see that a piece of bone or quantity of pus has been discharged from the skull, then remove your hand. And if not, press your hand with the iron itself or with another tool, until you see the bones that I told you about.
Then take something from salt, dissolve it in water and soak the cloth in it, and put it on that place; leave it for three days.
Then place on top of it a wet cloth in butter, and let it remain until the burn is consumed by the fire. Then treat it with the four-ingredient ointment until it heals.
It is said that the larger an open wound remains, the more pus it discharges; therefore, it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the skin should be burned up to the bone; and the cautery should be held until it has heated something of the bone's thickness.
Then grind down what has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
Others say that when the cautery reaches the bone, it should make an impression on the bone for as long as the bone falls off, so that it becomes like the shape of a scorch mark; or they use an instrument that women put in place of the small alphabet: and they believe that vapors from the head will escape from this place; and let the open wound remain for a long time.
Then treat it until it solidifies.
But I do not see these two types of cautery at all except in some people according to the way of fear.
And let it be, in my opinion, it is better for his health.
For the head is weakened by the solution of its own continuity; as we have testified in other members: and especially when the head of a sick person is naturally weak: and the first species of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and I use it: therefore operate with it for his health.
Chapter 3.
When a chronic pain occurs throughout the head, and it persists in a weak person, and they use hyson (a type of tea), hot baths, bloodletting, massages with oil, and fomentation. And particularly if it has already been cauterized with one cautery, as we have mentioned, and none of the above helps him: then consider. If the head of a weak person is strong by nature and not frail, and it finds extreme cold: then cauterize it with another cautery, but sparingly. Then cauterize it on all the horns of his head with another cautery, but be careful not to penetrate the skin, and remove only the quantity of bone that we have mentioned. Cauterize it with one cautery on the occiput of his head, in the place which is called "was": and it is a place where pus collects: and clean out your medicine in this place, but do not remove bone. For the weak person finds relief from that intense pain, and it is different from the pain of all other cauteries on the head.
And I will say that this cautery is in its place: and it must be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the occiput more subtly with the cautery used for cauterizing the middle part of the head.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occurs on part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is treated with cleaning medicines, and further treatment is administered as I have said in the divisions of diseases, but it does not work completely: then cauterization is used in this case according to two methods: either cauterization with a burning medicine, or with iron.
The cautery with burning medicine is to take one clove of garlic, peel it, and cut off the ends from both sides. Then cut the painful spot at the time with a broad lancet until there is a place under the skin where a tooth can be captured.
Insert it (the tooth) into the same place under the skin until it is hidden; then press upon it with a suitable plaster and leave it for fifteen hours, then dissolve it and extract the garlic clove and let it be for two or three days; later, place it submerged in butter on the spot until pus forms; then treat the spot with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish to do this with certain burning medicines, as I wrote in the twelfth treatise on Medications that Burn.
But cauterization is performed in this manner (with iron). The form of the hot cautery is as follows: a cylinder of iron about the size of a finger, covered with a sheath of leather, and on both
It is called a claw-like cautery because its head resembles the shape of a nail, having something sharp on it and in the middle there is a small projection.
Then place it on the spot and hold your hand; and you rotate the iron slowly with speed; and the amount that is burned should be of the thickness of the skin, as the middle part of it. And lift your hand so that an artery below is not burned and there is no bleeding.
Then immerse the hot iron in water with salt and place it on the spot for three days; then immerse the hot iron in butter; later, treat the spot with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicania (half headache) with the tip of the second cautery (small knife-like instrument). Be careful not to cut an artery during this half-headache, not by the ancient method.
On the method of cauterizing in the old half-headache.
When you treat a half-headache as we have said in the treatment that follows, and what we have said in the division of diseases, and it does not help: and you see from the disease that it is not enough for us what we have said with the first cautery with medicine, or with the cautery with fire, then it is necessary to use a cold cautery, until it whitens after marking the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or about this much: and put your hand instead, and tighten it until you cut an artery, and reach as far as the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to be careful about the lower jaw area that moves during chewing, so as not to burn the side or the nerve that moves it, thus causing a spasm.
And take care and be careful about the flow of blood from the artery that was cut. For there is fear in its cutting, especially for those who do not know what they are doing and are not careful or experienced: and they abandon the operation first of all.
And I will come with a reminder about the management of the flow of blood that occurs from the cut artery according to its method and in its place in this book.
If you see from the disease that this cautery is not enough for him, and you see a weak body tolerating the cautery in the middle of the head as we have said, treat a wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cautery having two blades. Cauterization is indeed better in this way and more suitable.
On the method of cauterizing ear pain.
When cold pain occurs in the ear and it is treated with solutions, and the rest of the treatment as we have said in the division, and the pain does not subside, then cautery by fire: and that is what is called a puncture, whose shape is as follows.
Then the puncture is made around the entire ear, as it is rotated: or around both sides if the pain is on both sides. And elongate [the cautery] from the ear's root slightly after marking the spots with encaustum (beeswax): and let the amount of cautery be ten punctures on every ear, approximately.
Then heal the spots until they are healed.
In the manner of cauterizing in a strain (torture).
Chapter VII.
A strain that is treated with cauterization, is not anything other than those types which occur due to phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid cauterizing species that occur due to exhaustion and muscle spasm.
When treating this species of strain with hyssop, mouth washings, and gargles, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the weakened area with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the second slightly lower than its own time (i.e., below the earlobe), and the third at the junction of the two lips (labia).
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the weakened area. Since softening does not occur unless in the healthy part.
And the shape of the cauterization is to cauterize with the cautery itself, along the tip of the upper part of the ear near the head slightly, and another at the earlobe; whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. Place your hand with the cautery until it is burned to a depth of half the thickness of the skin.
This is the form of Cautery, and it is made of a knife whose shape is as follows: however, it should not be too thin as you can see; it is necessary that the knife in it has little extra thickness.
Then take care of the places with it until they heal.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for apoplexy (ancient).
When apoplexy occurs and your treatment does not help, nor does the patient have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every horn of his head, and a cautery in the middle of his head as previously stated, and a cautery in the back of his head according to what has been described; the method of cauterization should be as previously described.
Additionally, it is cauterized with a Cautery on the mouth of the stomach; this is more the final procedure.
Then it will be treated with what has been described before.
Chapter 9.
It is necessary that in drink there are firstly large quantities of hyssop, and pills cleansing the brain.
Then scrape the head of the sick person entirely, and place upon his occiput ointment described in the treatise on ointments, and place it repeatedly.
For this is the method of cauterization: and do that according to the same order as I said there.
If therefore he is cured by it, it is good. If not: then do three cauterizations on the back part of his head, which are descending from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye: and place between every cauterization a thickness of a finger.
Then take care of the cauterization, with that which preceded.
If however you wish an addition, and the sick person can bear it: then do a cauterization in the middle. What if you wish an addition: then cauterize him above both horns.
Then take care of him until he is cured: and let the cauterization be anointed according to the shape that was mentioned before.
[Chapter Title] On the method of cauterizing in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter X.
You should proceed with the cleansing (munda) of the head with hyson (hyeeris), and with what was said.
Then scrape the head of the sick person: afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery over all the horns of the head, and with a cautery over behind it, and three over the vertebrae of the neck.
If, however, you need for the softening (mollification) of the body to be done with more of these things, and the patient is weak and the disease is strong: then cauterize it with four cauteries over the vertebrae of the back, and the last one with a cautery, until the skin of most of it has been burned off, and wipe your hand. Then take care of him (the patient), until he is cured: thus cauterize with oil (Oliuare).
Chapter on the method of cauterization in epilepsy.
Epilepsy is not to be cauterized, unless that person's epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary to cleanse the brain of that person first with hyson (hyeris), and with the treatment we mentioned earlier: when the patient is very sick, or weak in accepting medicine.
If, however, the patient is a child who cannot tolerate medicine, then administer gargarisma, and cleansing mastication (masticationes) for the brain, before that for many days with good food.
Then scrape the head of that person, afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, as before (secundum quod praecessit in modo): and with another cautery on the back of his head, and over all the horns of his head with a cautery. If the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then cauterize him with the cauteries that were mentioned in the presence of paralysis, and the softening (mollification) of the body on the vertebrae of the neck and back: and let the cautery be oiled (Cauterium oliuare) as before.
If a child is sick, then place a subtle cautery in this manner.
On the method of cauterizing in melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize it with the Cauteries which we have mentioned in a person having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of declivities to melancholy and the body of the sick person is moist, then give him to drink what purifies his brain, according to what was mentioned in the division: then shave the head of the sick person, and make afterwards a well-made plaster made from linen, just like a circle.
Then place it on the middle of the head: and the sick person sitting facing all directions should be held.
Then bring a liniment. It is better from ancient sheep butter. And heat it over a controlled fire temperature that the finger can bear when it is inserted into it. Then evacuate it in the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools down.
Do this to the sick person once every week, with the rest of his good treatment regime, until he is cured.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small punctures in it, besides holding your hand with the cautery; it should be smelly.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with a certain quality.
Then put over it a cloth soaked in butter or goose fat.
On the method of cauterizing in water descending to the eye.
Book Thirteenth.
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared to you by the signs I mentioned in division, then begin and wash the sick person, with it to clean his head.
And keep him away from all moistness, and make him sit in a bath for several days while fasting.
Then command him to shave his head, and brand himself in the middle of his head. Then brand him with two cauteries on both temples, if there is an obstruction of water descending in both eyes at once: or from one side, if there is an obstruction of water in one eye: and cut with the cautery all veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauterizations be long in width equal to the temples: and avoid bleeding.
If you see something from him, then cut it off immediately with any medicine that is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and cutting them, and caution against bleeding.
And sometimes he should be branded on the neck, under two bones, with two cauteries that are pushed out to the utmost.
Chapter on the method of branding in tears (anciently).
When the tears of the eyes are old and constant: and they are on veins and arteries that are manifest on the outside of the head, it is verified that this is from superfluidities cold, phlegmatic: then brand with the same cautery as I mentioned in the obstruction of water descending, branding in the middle of the head, and with two cauteries on both temples, and with two cauteries on the neck under two bones. And if it is necessary to add, then brand him on all sides of the eye with caution, on the edge of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Method for Cauterizing in Nasal Foul Smell.
When you treat it as we have said in division, and the medication does not work: then hurry up, and give infirmocochia for three nights; afterwards, shave its head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, with an oil-filled cautery. Then cauterize it with a pair of cauteries, two cauteries, on both eyebrows under the hair.
And keep away from the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the claw-shaped cautery.
Method for Cauterizing in Softening of the Eyelid.
When the eyelid of an eye is softened by illness or moisture: then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, with this lunar-shaped cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it over both eyebrows with two cauteries in all places; and they extend from the two temples: and let the length of the entire cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow: and do not go beyond the end with your hand, rather according to the amount that is burned by the third eyelash.
Method for Cauterizing the Eyelid when the hair turns inward and pricks the eye.
Cautery is in it according to two modes: either cautery with fire; or cautery with burning medicine.
In cauterio with fire, command the patient to shave his hairs beforehand if he is among those who clean them, until they are extended and evened out. If however they prick him at its origin: then constrict his eyes with adhesive until they do not move until they grow (healing).
When they grow and are evened out, then place the head of the patient in your lap; afterwards mark on the eyelid of his eyes with encaustic (wax), mark what is second in shape to a myrtle leaf; let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a cotton soaked in egg white or slippery elm gum on the eye.
Then heat the cautery, which has this shape (circular or spoon-shaped).
Then cauterize on the shape marked by you gradually at many spots, until the surface of the skin that is like a myrtle leaf, completely visible, is burned.
And the sign of your health work is: if you see that the eyelid of the eye already contracts, and hairs are rising at the prick on the eye.
Then lift your hand at that time; and release him for three days.
Then place on it a cotton with butter until the scab falls off. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
If some hair grows back after an hour and the eyelid becomes soft: then repeat the cautery on that place as you did at first.
If however the hairs are on the lower part (eyelash area): then cauterize it until they rise to their own place and become even so that they do not prick the eye again.
It is to be ordered for the sick one, that he lets go of hairs until they grow out and become equal. Make from linen cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and unabsorbed lime each a weight of ounce I or about that, then crush them together well with good grinding, and make it quickly so that it does not get cold. Then spread the paste on the cloth that you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf and place it over the eyelid of one or both eyes. And put under the eye, an egg yolk immersed in white of egg; and let the head of the sick one be in your lap.
And place your forefinger on the medicine and press it a little. And you move it as often as the sick one feels pain from the medicine; because its pressure is like fire.
While this pressure, which he feels as pain, continues, then release the medicine and move it with your finger. When the pain subsides, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And then consider if the eyelid rises as it does when contracted with fire or incision, this is good; and if not, then repeat the application of the medicine on the place where the medicine does not press or blacken until your operation becomes equal and the eye contracts.
Then place over it the yolk of an egg with butter until the skin of the burn is removed. Then treat him with a diaphine ointment or another one until he is healed.
And it is necessary for you during the operation that you keep the last guard so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid becomes softened after days and something fights from hairs within the eye, then repeat the medicine on that place which becomes softened from the eyelid, as you did initially. Then cure it (the affected area) until it is healed.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And know that human eyes differ in size and smallness. Therefore according to that (knowledge), let your consideration be: and the path of righteousness for this art should not be hidden from you.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in the lacrimal fistula.
When you treat the fistula (lacrimal duct), and your treatment does not help as mentioned in the divisions of diseases, then it is necessary that you cauterize it using this method.
Command the patient to place his head in your lap and hold his head with one of your hands so that it is not moved or shaken along with his head.
Then place the cotton soaked in alcohol or slime of comfrey on his eye, then with a hot cautery whose shape is as follows.
Be concave like the shape of a goose feather quill from one end, with which the cautery is made: and if you want it to penetrate up to the other end, or if you want it to be extended upward, it should be thus shaped.
Nevertheless, this concave shape is better for your purpose.
Then open the fistula if it is open and remove the pus from it, and cut it (the affected area): and if it is not open, then open it and remove the pus.
Then place the hot cautery on it.
And hold your hand a little away from the cautery near the eye, by the nose, so that your hand does not slip or shake, and place the cautery on the fat of the eye and burn it.
If therefore you arrive at the beginning of your cautery until the bone, it will be well. And if not: then repeat the cautery once, or twice if necessary; and leave it for three days.
Then place a cotton with butter, and care for it with an incisive ointment, until it is healed.
What if it passes beyond forty days and is not healed: then place a sharp corrosive medicine on it until the bone appears; and shave it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is another way of cautery for a fistula, which some of the first said. Direct yourself to the place of the fistula, and pierce it; then put in it a fine cannula, that is, a thin cannula, whose shape is this. And pour into it a quantity of drachmas made from melted lead, and hold your hand with good retention on the cannula, and do not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run or reach its eye.
And it is necessary that you put a hot cotton on the eye of the weak person, either in egg white or in water.
For lead burns the place of the fistula and heals it with a marvelous healing.
If the fistula is healed with what we said from cautery and cure, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer a nostril hole, and lead the fistula to the nasal passage, according to what comes in its own place.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in fissures of the lips.
Multiple splits occur in the Lip, which are called Hairs, and especially in the lips of children.
When you treat these splits, as we have said in the division of diseases, and the treatment does not help, then apply small cautery with a knife, according to this shape.
And let its depression be according to the subtlety of the knife.
Then place it [the heated tool] quickly into these splits, until the cautery reaches the depth of the splits.
Then treat it with pitch, until it is healed.
[Title] The method of cauterization in the Fistula of the Mouth.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus and bursts; afterwards it becomes old, and pus runs, and a fistula is formed: then treat this fistula, and the treatment does not help in it, then it is necessary that you apply heat to the cautery according to its size, which can enter into the fistula. Then insert the heated tool into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand; until the iron becomes hot to its depth and end; do this once or twice.
Then treat it after that, as we have said about treatment, until it is treated.
If the pus is cut off and healed, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to remove the corrupted bone according to what comes out of its head.
[Title] The method of cauterization on softened gums and teeth.
When the gum softens due to moistures and teeth move, and care of it with medicines does not help: then place the head of the sick in your bosom.
Then apply fire to the cautery, whose form will come later, in such a way that you place the Cannula on the tooth and introduce into it the heated cautery quickly: hold your hand for a moment, until the sick person feels the warmth of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
Then remove your hand: then repeat the cautery several times as you wish.
Then let the sick person fill his mouth with water and salt, and hold it for an hour: then spit it out.
For the tooth moved hardens, and softened gums contract, and dryness sets in to corrupt moisture.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing tooth pain.
When the tooth pain is due to coldness or has coldness itself, or worms, and care with medicines does not help: then apply cautery in it according to two modes: either cautery with butter; or cautery with fire.
The cautery with butter is such that you receive fresh butter, and heat it in an iron cauldron or in a ewer. Then take the bag and turn it over the end of the wound. Submerge it into boiling butter and place it quickly on the painful tooth and hold it until it cools; then repeat this process several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
If desired, immerse wool or cloth in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth; then place a heated iron on it until the heat reaches the depth of the cavity of the tooth.
Cauterization with fire is to prepare a copper or iron tube (cannula). Let there be something bulky in the body so that the sharp heat does not reach the weak bone.
Then apply fire to the cautery whose form will come; place it on the tooth and hold your hand until it cools.
Repeat this several times, as pain will subside either on the same day or another day.
It is necessary to fill the weakened bone with good butter and hold it for an hour; then spit it out.
This is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with whatever shape you desire, provided it is possible; and this is the form of the cannula (tube).
Chapter on how to cauterize ulcers.
When worms are from phlegm, and from cold moistness, and do not obey digestion by medicines, and desire digestion quickly: then to a concave cautery, whose shape is this.
Having two open extremities, so that the smoke may leave at the other end of the cautery: and place it heated above the ulcer once, and a second time, if necessary, until it reaches the depth of the ulcer.
If the ulcer is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the ulcer.
Then let it be for three days, and place on it a cup full of butter heated, until what the fire has burned is removed.
Then care for it with tooth ointment, until the canal heals.
On the mode of cauterizing in swelling of voice, and constriction of breathing.
When moisture accumulates on the bronchial tube of the lung, and especially when it is accompanied by cold constitution, then it is necessary that the ill person first be evacuated with soluble medicines.
Then cauterize it at the nose at the root of the throat in a hollow place: and be careful not to reach with the cautery at the throat, nor on the skin, unless something of that part is present.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the junction of the neck near the last vertebra of that joint: and let the cautery be small according to the manner which was mentioned earlier.
Then care for it with what has been mentioned before, until it is healed.
On the mode of cauterizing in diseases of the lungs and cough.
When cough and lung disease are from cold moistness, and the ill person does not have fever, nor phthisis, and the illness is neither old: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the clavicle in hollow, loose, open places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cautery be a cannula as described before.
And if you wish your cauterization to be by pricking with the cautery called "Punctum", whose shape was described before in the section on ear pain: let them be pricks of about thirty, up to another.
Then treat it with that same thing as before, until it heals.
And now let the cautery have three branches: in this shape. Why should cauterization be applied with it, when you perform it with one of the three cauteries.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head is dislocated due to the cause of humidity, and it does not return to its place within an hour after its dislocation, until that has become its custom for returning, then it should be dislocated again from a slight movement, as we have already testified, then you must first reduce the dislocation. Then the patient lies down on his back or on his healthy side. Then clean the skin that is inside the tickle towards the upper part with your left hand fingers: and if it is a union that is dislocated towards the inner parts.
Then take the cautery with two openings (cannulae). Its shape is as follows:
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates through to the other side, and the figure of cauterization with four cauteries will come.
And sometimes a cauterization occurs with a cautery having three prongs, whereupon the figure of cauterization becomes six cauteries: and the prongs are according to the thinness of the tendon.
And this is the form of a cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one more is added to it, whereupon there are eight cauteries.
Then place over the cautery narrow strips of salted meat. Then make the patient remain still to avoid movement of the limb until it recovers.
And if a dislocation is upwards (rarely does this happen), then cauterize the same over the shoulder with an ironsmith's cautery or many puncturing cauteries.
For joints are strengthened and moisture is removed; and the sick person recovers.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When coldness and many humidities occur in the stomach until it is expelled from its composition and multiplied catarrhs are produced to it, and continuous methods of treatment fail, then the sick person must lie on his back, extend his legs and hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, an iron smith's cautery of the size of one finger at the sternum, and two cauteries below from the sides of one cautery, until a triangle figure of cauteries comes. And stretch them apart so they do not join when pus forms.
And the depth of the cautery should be the size of two finger-widths of skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be in this shape without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this shape, then let the cautery that is used for this cauterization be one in the shape of a circle according to this shape.
The stomach is to be cauterized by piercing it with a probe that frightens the patient from the cautery: and it is, as signs are placed on the stomach according to the quantity desired with wax: then cauterize it with the same cautery at the point pierced: then take care of it with the healing method that preceded until it heals.
On the method of freezing the stomach.
When pain arises in the stomach from coldness and humidity, or from thick vomiting until it has passed through its natural expulsion of excess, and the sick person is not cured by what was said, then the sick person should lie on his back on his neck, and signs with wax three cauteries according to this shape, and the same quantity below in the stomach near the hypochondriac region where the elbow reaches: and let the space between each cautery be as wide as a finger's thickness: and let the cautery be as long as the straight body: and do not press your hand too much with the cautery.
And let the quantity that is to be burned be taken from the thickness of the skin, but not increased in half: and let the sick person stand on his feet.
If he is not standing, then let him lie down, who has already stretched out his legs and raised his arms.
This is the shape of the cautery.
And it is possible for you to cauterize these cauteries with a surgical cautery, when subtlety and wisdom are present with you in the art.
And be careful not to advance too far in cauterization so that the entire thickness of the skin is burned, for the body is being burned entirely and it reaches the intestines; because the skin there is delicate, therefore know this.
On the method of cauterizing abscesses in the stomach.
When there is an abscess that needs to be opened, and you want to know if it is in the liver flesh or its sheath: then, if it is in the liver flesh, a weak pain and heaviness without sharpness will occur; and if it is in the liver sheath, with pain it will have a very intense sharpness; and you notice that the treatment of this abscess has exhausted the doctors.
Therefore, the weak person should lean his head back. Then shape the location of the abscess with the hot iron; then heat the cautery similar to a scalpel. And this is its shape. And cauterize it with the heated cautery until the entire skin is burnt and reaches the abscess cavity, until all pus is discharged; then treat the patient with the treatment of opening abscesses, until he is healed.
And this cautery shape should not be used, unless the person's interest in the art of medicine is prolonged; and through whose hands these diseases often occur with experience; then he may dare to perform such an operation.
But it is better for her to leave herself, in my opinion.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in pleurisy.
The ancients said that the cautery with the roots of Aristolochia should be applied to cold pleurisy in this manner. And you should take a dry root of Aristolochia with long roots; select the longest root from it, which is about the size of a finger. Then immerse it in oil and heat it over fire. Then cauterize it with one heated cautery in the area between the connection of the collarbone and neck, and with two small cauteries below slightly sloping cheeks on that side.
And with two cauteries also in it, which is between the fifth and sixth ribs sloping towards the back a little bit: and one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from the back: one in what is between the two scapulas: and two cauteries on both sides of the chest, the lower one being the one that is between the two scapulas.
And it is not necessary that you press your hand with the cautery, rather let it be in the open air smelling the skin.
And some ancient ones have said that there are men who use a cautery similar to a rod of iron, they heat it and put it inside what is between the ribs until they reach the abscess with it, and the pus comes out: as we said in the abscess of Epates.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is fear, that either the sick person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs at the place, which has no healing.
Chapter XXXII. On the method of cauterizing the Spleen Head.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, as we said in the division of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then there is cauterization in it according to three modes, which are all correct.
One of them is that you make three or four cauteries in a row along the length of the spleen according to the shape of the cauterizations of Epates, whose figure was previously mentioned.
And let the space between each cautery be the thickness of a finger, or more or less.
And let the mode of cauterization be equal to the one we mentioned in the cauterization of Epates.
And do not press your hand with the cautery, and let the sick person lie face down on his back.
Another method for cauterization is: hold a pair of cauteries, as we said in the chapter on dislocation of the humerus; and lift the skin, which is straight over the spleen, where the weak arm arrives; and let your elevation of the skin be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall according to the length of the body.
Then introduce two hot irons very deeply, until they penetrate the skin from the other side; then extract one of the cauteries; thus four cauteries are made.
And if you want to cauterize with a cautery having three hot irons.
Then take care of the cautery after you have released it to emit pus for many days; indeed, this is more effective than the rest which preceded from treatment.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for hydropsy.
The cautery does not fall in hydropsy, unless it is properly applied.
When you treat a hydropsy patient with the methods of treatment mentioned in division, and the treatment is not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize it with four cauteries around the navel, one on the stomach, another on the liver, another on the spleen, two behind the loins, one directly on the chest, and another directly on the stomach; and let the depth of the cautery be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then release the open cautery to emit pus for a long time.
And do not evacuate the weakened patient from treatment after cauterization with it; because two intentions must be assembled for him, and healing will hasten to him with the help of God.
The shape of the cautery with which the abdomen is cauterized should be clavicle-shaped; as its previous shape has been; and the one with which the back is cauterized should be olive oil-shaped, as its previous shape has been.
On the method of cauterizing feet and legs.
When the feet or legs are sickly or fractured and filled with yellow water (i.e., pus): it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot, which is between the big toe and ankle; and take the cautery in hand without twisting it; then take the hand away; and do not reapply it at all.
The yellow water will run out, and the cautery should be of this shape.
Then make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be with the point of a knife-like cautery; and let the cautery be along the length of the leg, one below the knee and the other lower about halfway down the leg; and over the hip make two cauteries: and leave the open cautery for a long time without treatment until some water comes out from it; then treat it as we have said before.

When the abdomen is malicious or: when there is a dissolution of the abdomen due to cold and moistness, until its powers of retention and digestion are weakened in the stomach and intestines; and it is treated with methods of treatment, but does not heal; and you see an infirm person tolerating a cautery with excessive power, then cauterize it with a large cautery over its own stomach, according to the method used in cauterizing the stomach with a circular cautery and four subtle cauteries around the umbilicus, with a small sharp cautery; and a large cautery or two large cauteries on the alcatin above the navel.
And if you see excessive moisture and the infirm person tolerating it, then cauterize it with a cautery over the breastbone and over the whole ilium; and perhaps add two small cauteries near the large one on the stomach.

On the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When in the anus there are many old hemorrhoids or one, and they consist of thick, cold, or corrupted fluids, and they cannot be cured by what has been said in the division; then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower part of the back slightly triangularly below the almeidatum, and with a cautery near the navel as if with two fingers.
And if you consider that its stomach is chilled and food is not digested, and you see the face turning pale; then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery as described before; also cauterize the liver and spleen of his with another cautery, along with a cautery on the kidney; and leave the open cautery for some time; then care for him until he is cured.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you cut (open) althelul, then heat the cautery similar to a rod. Then insert the heated (cautery) into the cut althelul: and hold your hand until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows; do this once or twice.
If there are many altheluls (abscesses), then cauterize each one with the cautery as I have said. Then take care of them (altheluls) with what you apply to them from ointments until they heal.
And if you cauterize it (the althelul) with a large cautery on the coal, it is more useful for healing.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter XXXVIII. (the thirty-eighth chapter)
If the patient does not obey the incision and operation as I have described at the place, and is afraid of it, he may heal with cautery.
When a fistula occurs and becomes chronic, pus flows from it, and the affected area is corrupted (putrid). Therefore, as is necessary, you should examine it with a probe of fine material. Then recognize the depth of it (the fistula) by probing with a probe.
Then heat the cautery that is similar to a rod. Then insert the heated (cautery) into the fistula and close the wound with a nail at the depth to which it was inserted.
And repeat the cautery over her (the fistula) until all the rotten flesh is burned away; do this once, twice, or three times according to your need.
And be careful not to burn the nerve or large vein if it is there; or if the fistula goes to the bladder or the intestine, then be careful about all these places.
And thou shalt not do that, except when the fistula is in a fleshy place: and consider, for it is not penetrating.
Then care for the place until it heals.
If the place is sealed and the matter is cut away from it, and it remains for a long time: then you shall know that it is healed completely.
And if the matter is not cut away from it, then you shall know that it is penetrating, or that the bone inside of it is corrupted, or as one of those (conditions) whose memory will come up in its place.

And perhaps we have cauterized it for the second time in the same almethenum (location). Why three lines will come. Therefore they will be more towards the benefit.
