Chapter on the method of cauterizing in sciatica.
When pain occurs in the ankle joint, and its cause is coldness and moistness: and the sick person is treated as we said in the division, but the treatment does not help, and it worsens: then it is necessary that you release the sick person from thick fluids with foul pills or artificial pills, or similar ones. Then cauterize him.
And the method of cauterization is done according to two methods: either cauterization with medicines advancing, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with fire, is according to many ways.
One of these is, to cauterize over the ankle joint itself with three triangular cauteries in this shape. And make a good or bad depth for them. And let the space be between every cautery of thickness of a finger's length: and let the cautery be to oil.
Occasionally, however, cauterization is made in the middle over the ankle joint itself. Why are there four cauteries?
If you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose shape precedes the ankle joint dislocation, one: so that it contains the entire ankle.
And burn the thickness of the skin all around.
This is the method of cauterization for sciatica, when the pain is adhering to the ankle itself, and it does not extend to the hip and leg.
If it extends to the hip and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the hip, at the place where the sick person indicates, where there is pain, and your cautery four fingers on the side of the forest part: and let the cautery be a knife.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the sick person indicates that the pain extends to near the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where he indicates with a cautery of points, three, or four, or more if needed.
And if he indicates that the pain is turned towards the leg from the foot, then cauterize it there with a single-pointed cautery.
And be careful with every cauterization in your work, so as not to burn the nerve or a large artery, and thus attract harm upon the sick person or constriction.
I myself have seen one and another of those who cauterized above the hock, and burned too much in cauterization, and the leg swelled so that the tumor reached the foot, and it was perforated all over, and the entire foot rotted; then there followed rupture of the abdomen, and death after that.
If the pain is in two parts at once, cauterize both according to this method.
And some wise men have said that in cauterizing the ankle, this method of cautery should be used. Make a small iron rod similar to the thumbnail in size and thickness; and within its opening, there should be a third of that small iron.
And the space between each small iron should be as much as the knuckle of the thumb; and let the small irons have openings on both sides; and let their height be like a knuckle, or two knuckles; and make handles of iron well-suited for the small irons.
Then it (the small iron) is heated in fire until it turns red and emits sparks; then it should be placed on the box of the ankle on the sick person lying down on the healthy side. Cauterize him with three round irons at once.
Then let him go for three days. Afterwards pack it with butter: and let the open wound heal for many days. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis says, in this manner of cautery, we have not been often employed, because of the fear of its appearance: and therefore, few are found who wait upon it.
Nevertheless, it is one of the good cauterizations for him who endures it, and finds a place for it.
The cautery with stimulating drugs is, that you should make two pieces of silk having a perforated thread, into which descends the key of his gate from brass or iron, the length of the wall: whose knots in their height are two, or as if they were themselves.
And let there be the space which is between both of equal thickness to a finger, and let them be open below and above: and let it hold together on either side, according to this form.
Then place it upon a box of an oar, a weak one lying upon the healthy side. And press your hand much upon the box of the oar. Then pour between the two circles from warm water, which is heated slightly with fire and hold it for an hour's time: and let the weak one endure its biting and burning, for he himself finds the biting as if by fire, until the biting ceases.
Then wash your hand with the instrument and clean the oar with warm water together with sweet water: then let it go for three days.
And place butter upon it until the blackness of the burning is removed: and let it go for some days, and let pus run out from it. The remedy is at last in help.
Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg: make a setting in it that contains water, as you did with the ankle, equally.
And this is the method of hot water: and I have already written it in the treatise on the correction of medications. Take equal parts of lime and unburnt chalk; grind each one separately, and put them in a new pot whose lower part is perforated with a small hole, according to the quantity that will be added to it; place another earthenware pot underneath; pour on top of the lime and chalk from sweet water, so that they are submerged by a finger's depth; when you have compressed them with your hand, let it stand until the water descends in the lower part of the earthenware pot.
Then gather that water altogether and pour it over another lime; cook until it returns.
For indeed, it will then be very strong for sharpness, which is used in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of other body parts. Because it performs the action of fire itself.
And among the medications are those with which anchors and also stitchwort, walnut honey, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed. [The rest of the sentence is missing.]
And Galen indeed reported the cure of a certain man from ancient times, who was cured of pain in the anchor and sciatic vein; he praised it very much. And he said that it did not need any other cure, and because he was cured from the first application, until he reported that perhaps he himself had entered a bath carried there, and came out already healthy from it.
And it is to be taken from green seedage; and if no green seedage is found, dry ones should be gathered, recently; they must be ground thoroughly with some fat, and placed on the anchor where there is pain, or leg, or hip: and tied, and left for three hours' quantity, or until the patient feels relaxation of burning. Then insert him into a bath (or tub).
When his body becomes hot, insert him (the instrument) into the bed (of fire or coals). Pain retreats and it heals.
And know that no one should use cautery with these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides says that goat dung, when cauterized with it on the sciatic vein, brings this about: and it becomes a cautery in this way. Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on a deep place that is between the toe of the foot and the heel, and closer to the heel.
Then take dry goat dung and heat it in fire until it becomes coal.
Then place it on the wool and let it rest until it is extinguished. Repeat this again. Do not stop doing that until sensation reaches the ankle through the intermediary and pain ceases.
And this method of cautery is called the cautery of goat dung.
Section on the Cauterization of Back Pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back from various causes, either from falling, striking, excessive evacuation, and similar ones, or from the infusion of cold and moist matter: and cautery does not fall except in this single case, which is made by the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after evacuation of the sick with fetid pills, and similar ones, they should be made over the back where there is pain, three lines according to the width of the almud itself, after signs have been made with wax in every line, five or more cauteries according to the quantity that comes from the tolerance of the sick person: and let the cauterization be done with a cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries, together with the middle claw-shaped cautery, according to this shape.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in the swelling of the Hump (Gibbositas).
Often this illness occurs in small children.
The sign of its beginning in children is that it happens on him constriction in panting during lifting and movement: and you find at the end of the vertebrae of the back and nodes of it, which has already begun to protrude above the other vertebrae.
When you see that and wish to do it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery shaped like this.
And let the cautery encompass all parts of the vertebrae equally: and if you wish, cauterize around the vertebrae with a pointed cautery two or three lines, and let the points be close to each other.
Then care for the place until it is healed as we have said.
And beware not to administer cautery on a hump that occurs due to muscle spasm.
On the method of cauterization in gout, and the pains of the joints.
When the pains of the joints are caused by cold and moist humors spreading to any part of the body, and when the pain is in the feet, it is customary among physicians to call this gout properly.
Since, therefore, when gout caused by cold is treated with means of treatment and the pain does not subside, then a cautery removes them.
And it is to be cauterized with him after evacuation around the joint of the foot, with many cauteries; and let the cautery be Olivar.
And if you need to prick the sole of the foot, then do so with a cautery for pricking. If the pain ascends to the knees or other joints and this often occurs, then cauterize it over the entire knee with three or four cauteries from all sides, using the same cautery as Clavius.
If more cauteries are necessary for you, then cauterize it. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, rather let it be about the thickness of the skin.
If the pain ascends to the knees and back: then administer what was said concerning cautery in its own chapter.
If the pain is only in the hands: then prick around the nails as two lines are rolled.
If some of the pain remains in the fingers: then prick them all over each nodule and on the back of the hand.
If the pain ascends after several days to the elbows or shoulders: then cauterize both from all sides.
And do not evacuate a weak person from good diet and medicine intake. If good care is taken and phlegm is evacuated, healing will be aided by the help of God with this cautery.
On the method of cauterization for ruptures.
When there is a rupture in the groins and the intestine or scrotum descends, and it begins close by: then it is necessary that you advise the sick person to abstain from food on his own day. He should use purgatives, so that he may pass stool from his bowels.
Then he should lie down on his back before you, and you should command him to hold his breath until the scrotum or the intestine appears.
Then you should reduce him with your fingers and make a mark with hot wax at the rupture on his chest, with a sign whose end is similar to half of a circle above the body.
Then apply cautery with this shape until it becomes white and expels pus. Then reduce the intestine or scrotum into its hollow. Then the assistant shall place his hand on the place so that the intestine does not come out; and you have already opened between the legs of the sick person, and you have placed a pulley under him, and one servant above his thighs, and another above his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on the mark, with your hand holding it straight. And hold him until you follow the bone with it; or replace him with another if you do not reach the bone with it the first time until the bone.
And be careful to observe the exit of the intestine during your cautery operation, lest you burn him, and a great evil or death come upon the sick person through it.
And know that when you do not follow the bone with the cautery, the operation does not help.
It is necessary that the cautery be small for children, according to their measure.
Then care for him with ointments until he is healed.
The patient lies down on his back for forty days until the wound is healed.
It is necessary that you place food for him in accordance with the duration of his cure, to soften his stomach, so that the intestine does not come out during surgery or evacuation.
Then, when he wants to perform surgery after forty days, then administer a well-made ligature and hold it for forty other days.
Let him be reduced by work, let him be filled with food and drink, and let him be silent with strong voices.
For when using this regimen, he will heal with complete healing.
And I say the treatment of ruptures with incision in its own chapter.
When ruptures occur in the rest of the abdomen, and they are starting and want to be added, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautionery in accordance with its size: and let that which is burned from then on be like a third of it. Then take care of him, as I said before: do not add anything.
And some have said in the beginning: that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautionery in this shape.
After it is signed with a hot iron and a line is placed which is across the width at the top of the rupture, and another line down below. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery tongs.
But the first cauterization is easier and better.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in pain due to rupture or injury.
Chapter 48.
When there is pain in some parts due to rupture or injury and the pain persists for a long time and does not cure with medicine, then it is necessary to cauterize with a puncture cautionery.
And let the cautery be for each member according to its size and its own smallness and weakness, and also according to its strength, and its location of twisting, and pain from it.
If he is cured by the first cautery, it is well. If not: then repeat the cautery upon him.
Because it is a custom for these pains that they are changed from one member to another which is closer to it. Therefore, you must pursue them with the cautery until the sick man is cured.
Chapter on the manner of cauterizing in Leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes helped by a great extent by cautery. And especially the species of Leprosy which arises due to corruption of phlegm and melancholy: when therefore you wish to cauterize it, consider this.
If leprosy is beginning and you have treated it as we said in the division, and it does not abate nor stabilize: then fear for the sick person, lest corruption spread over his entire body; then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, and the second lower toward the forehead near the end of the hairs, and two over the two horns, and one behind over the nuchal bone.
And the last [cautery] press your hand slightly with the cautery until it makes an impression smaller than a finger, and the scales will be dislocated from it; so that the expiration of gross vapors from it is relieved, and cauterize also the spleen with the cautery according to what preceded.
If leprosy is already spread over the sick person and is manifestly apparent: then it is necessary to cauterize with these cauteries which we said in the head, and a cautery on the tip of the nose, and two cauteries on the cheeks, and two cauteries on the shoulders, and six on the spondyles of the back, and one large one over the alhahosos near the greater trochanter and one above it in the same almeidat: and two over the ankles: that is, over every ankle with one, and two over the knees, and two over the elbows, and two over the wrists, and two over the tendons of his breast; and cauterize him over all the joints, from the joints of his fingers of his hands and feet, and cauterize over all the calcanei of his feet, and the soles of his hands.
Beware not to burn the nerves that are above the last calcaneus (heel bone).
Whenever cauterized with a cautery on the chin, and another on the breast, and another on the epigastrium (upper abdomen).
And know that as much more you add cautery, it is more beneficial and more effective.
And know that the sick do not feel pain in cautery as healthy ones do, for this reason, because his body is already numb.
Cauteries should be of different sizes and shapes according to the limbs and joints; this depends on the type of instruments that preceded.
Then, treat the cautery with flour from a plant mixed with honey, and the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Section on Cauterizing in Epilepsy.
When a limb is numbed and treated with medicines, oils, plasters, and yet it does not heal, then the affected limb should be cauterized with cauteries, according to the size of the limb or its smallness.
And let your cautery go in slightly deeper than the skin's thickness. Then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
Whenever a cautery is applied for numbness that occurs in the hand or foot, at the joints of the back near the nerve exits that move that limb, the numbness is removed.
But do not presume to apply it unless you are wise about the anatomy of limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
Chapter LXI.
When Albaraz becomes gangrenous and no medicine is applied to it: then cauterize over the affected area with a deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the white disappears and its color changes.
Then care for it with a mixture of barley flour and lentils with rose oil, arnoglossa leaves, dove blood, and heron blood. Each ingredient should be an equal part. Mix all these together, soak the cloth in the mixture, and apply it to the affected area until it heals.
Chapter on the method of cauterization for cancer.
When a cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it: then cauterize it with a circular cautery around its circumference, as it rotates.
The wise have said that it should be cauterized with the ultimate cautery in the middle.
That does not seem good to me, for I fear it will burn: and I have already seen that happen several times.
It is more correct to cauterize around its circumference with a circle, as we said before: or with many cauteries.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in adubelation.
When someone has adubelation and it slows in maturation, either due to excessive matter causing it or because the person is old and weak with few blood vessels, or because of time and a desire to hasten the maturation of adubelation: then cauterize around its circumference with many small puncturing cauteries. Then let it go. For it will hasten when it matures.
If you wish to make a perforation with the cautery: then heat the cautery in fire, and this is its form.
And place it in the middle of the adubelation until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be weak after that, to alleviate the course of the purgatives.
Then care for it until it is healed.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in a rotten wound.
Chapter LIIII.
Corrosion is not unless it is walking corruption in a limb, and it consumes itself: just as fire consumes dry wood.
If you see a corrosion in a place that can bear cautery with fire, then apply much cautery, small and large nails according to what suits the place where the corrosion is present.
Then cauterize it from every part until you eradicate the entire corrosion, and no part of it remains deep within.
Then let it rest for three days and put over the cauterized places finely ground sulfur with oil until all scabs are removed and the entire corrosion is eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments that promote flesh growth.
If after three days you see new flesh growing healthy, without any corrosion, it is good.
And if not: then apply cautery again to the remaining parts of the corrupted places.
Corrosion is sometimes treated with an acute medicine. It arises where cautery was applied.
Nevertheless, cautery with fire is quicker in help. And I have already said that the cauterization of it with an acute medicine is useful in division; take it there when you need it.
Chapter on how to cauterize nails and warts.
Chapter 50.
It often happens that this sickness occurs in the lower parts of the feet and it is a serious condition, filled with pus, which damages the foot.
Cauterization is done in these cases in two ways: cauterization with fire and cauterization with hot water.
As for the cauterization with fire, it is done by heating a concave cautery similar to a vulture's feather, made of iron according to the size needed to hold the nail from all sides; and the edges should be thin.
Then place the hot iron on the nail. Then turn the hand with the cautery around the nail until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail; and leave it for three days until it begins to emit pus. Then plaster it with malves from the forest, crushed with salt; and leave the plaster on it at night. It will be uprooted by its roots.
Then care for the place with a gentle ointment until it heals.
If they are not converted and occur frequently on the surface of the body, particularly in hands and feet; then administer cauterization with hot water: and it is that you receive a cannula from brass, iron, or from an eagle's feather; and place it on the nail, or the sore. Then pour a small amount of hot water into the cannula: hold your hand and turn it with a slight compression to print the edge of the cannula on the root of the nail, and let the hot water find its way deep to the root of the nail; and let the weak person wait a little while for the biting of the hot water for an hour.
Then leave it, for the nail will be uprooted with its roots.
Do this to each one separately, until you come upon all that are in the body.
Then care for them after they have been uprooted, with what generates flesh from ointments.
\*\*On the Method of Cauterization in Tremor.\*\*
When trembling occurs in a person due to cold in the nerve, or quartan fever, or something else: then it is necessary that you cauterize it with four or five cauteries on the dorsal spine, and between every spine with a cautery, and in its chest with a cautery, and over its stomach with a cautery.
For trembling quiets with the cauterization of oil, and hastens the health of the cold illness.
§ On the method of cauterizing Albathir.
Head LVII.
At times, foul matters called Albathir (boils) are expelled from the body; these boils arise from corrupted thick substances.
Therefore, when they appear, it is necessary to cauterize the entire head of each boil with a fine cautery and myrtle wood, whose tip has been ignited with fire. Or, if with a long root of Aristolochia (Snakeweed). Or with a concave cautery.
And sometimes, the cauterization of ademeanol (a type of abscess) is done at the beginning of its expulsion according to this method; they do not increase and the excess is broken causing them to discharge pus, from which they heal.
However, it must be done after evacuation with phlebotomy (bloodletting).
Chapter on the method of cauterization during blood flow from an artery in a wound.
It often happens that blood flows from an artery, which has been cut near a wound, due to external causes or during the incision of an abscess, or cauterization of a limb, and similar cases; it is difficult to separate it.
When this happens to someone, then quickly place your hand at the opening of the artery and put your index finger on it; press it tightly until the blood is contained under your finger and nothing can be expelled from there.
Then place a small olive oil-coated cautery in the fire and many more of them; blow on it until they are lit very well.
Then take one of them, small or large, depending on the wound and the location where the artery has been torn; place the cautery over the vein and then remove your finger quickly; hold the cautery until the blood is cut off.
If it is expelled with the finger from the opening of an artery, and the cautery is extinguished, then take another cautery hastily, from those that are prepared in fire.
Therefore do not cease to do that (the procedure) one after the other, until the blood is cut off.
And beware lest you burn the nerve which is there, and another harm befalls the patient.
And know that when blood flows from an artery, then it is not possible to cut it (the artery); especially because the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or with a cautery, as we have said. Or with extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it (the artery) is drawn out, the ends are contracted, and the blood is cut off. Or it is tied with a strong thread. Or medicines of the property for cutting off blood are placed upon it (the artery), and it is squeezed with a proper ligature.
Whoever administers the cutting off (of the artery) with a ligature and compression with a cloth, or placing of burning things and similar items, does not completely restore him (the patient), unless rarely.
If that (the procedure) should happen to anyone and the physician is not present nor medicine: then let him begin with the position of the index finger over the opening of the vein itself, as we have said, and with very strong compression, until the blood is obstructed from the superior part of the wound, and on the artery. And let the finger not be removed from above it (the artery) with cold water of violent coldness always, until the blood is frozen, thickened and cut off.
And meanwhile let him consider in it (the wound) what requires a cautery or medicine.
On Incision, Perforation, and Phlebotomy in Wounds, and Such Like Things.
As we have said in the first chapter, every illness where cautery with fire and burning medicine is suitable, its occasions, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries.
And I set there chapters from the neck down to the feet.
And I shall proceed in this chapter along the same path, so that what is sought may be clarified for those who seek it.
And before I begin that (discussion), you sons must know what is in this chapter from the fear which was mentioned in the first chapter about cautery.
And for this reason it is necessary that there be a greater caution in this, because in the operation which is in this chapter, evacuation often falls with blood, with which life stands at the opening of a vein or incision on an abscess, or the opening of a wound, or treatment of wounds, or extraction of arrows, or incision on a stone, and such like: from all of which is associated tremor, fear, and death occurs in many cases.
And I warn you that it does not happen to you what is hesitant, for sometimes men of this art fall into your hands like weak ones. For there is one who gets angry with his illness, and death is easy for him because of the intensity he finds from weakness and the length of his wickedness. And when it comes from fear, it signifies death.
And there is one who gives his guaranty and pays you along with it, hoping for health, but his illness is fatal.
Therefore, it is not appropriate that you agree with him who comes to you from those whose method is such. Let your caution be more intense than your greed and rapacity. And do not presume about anything from it unless after certain knowledge which verifies at your place the successful outcome.
And in treating all your sick people, make prognosis and indication concerning that which is appropriately healthy.
For there is help for you in the acquisition of fame and glory, as well as memory and praise.
May God inspire you, O sons, with His understanding, and may He not remove from you guidance and inspiration, for that is in His hand.
And I myself have arranged this chapter by dividing it into sections according to what preceded in the chapter on Cautery, from neck to feet: so that you may be relieved of what is sought from it and what you need.
Chapter on Treating Water That Gathers in Children's Heads.
Section I.
Know that this weakness frequently occurs in children during childbirth: or when the midwife tightens the child's head without ease.
And it sometimes happens due to an unknown cause which is not known.
And indeed, I have not seen this illness in others than children; and death approached every one of them whom I saw from them; therefore it seemed to me that the operation should be avoided in it.
And indeed, I have seen a child whose head was full of water and his head grew great every day until he could not sit on himself due to the size of his head; and the moisture increased until he died.
And this moisture, indeed, either collects between the skin and bone; or it collects under the bone above the brow ridge.
And the operation on it, if there is moisture between the skin and bone, and the abscess is small, then it is necessary to make a fissure in the middle of the head, one opening wide; and let the length of the fissure be like two knuckles, until the moisture runs out.
And this is the form of trephining (spatumilis).
If therefore the moisture is more increased, and the abscess is larger, then place two fissures, according to this form (trephining).
And if the moisture is under the bone, and there is a sign of it, which you see that the joints of the head are open everywhere; and water sinks when you press it with your hand to the inside, and it does not hide from you; then it is necessary to make three fissures in the middle of the head, according to this method.
And after the incision, extract all the moisture. Then tighten the fissures with bandages and lints. Then pour oil and wine over it until the fifth day.
Then cut the ligament, and care for the wound with sutures and ointments.
And do not let the head be bound equally. Feed the sick man with dry food of little moisture until the limb recovers and heals.
Another method of incision is to consider where the size of the abscess appears, and collection of water.
Because sometimes it is more in the skull, or in the forehead, or on the right, or on the left.
Therefore, with the incision, go where you see the abscess and filled water: and cut it as much as possible for you.
And observe that you do not cut the artery and cause a blood flow, and let the sick man die from this flow along with the evacuation of moisture.
[Section heading] On incisions of arteries after the ears.
Chapter II.
When someone suffers from catarrhs on the eyes or chest and it becomes chronic and does not improve with medical treatment: then the final cure is more in him, incision of these two arteries.
Therefore, when one wishes to make an incision there (on the affected area), let him shave his head. Then rub the place with a rough cloth, so that the arteries appear. Then let him tighten his neck with any of his cloths. Then observe where the vein pulses. And these places are places that are depressed behind the ears: and they are rarely hidden except in some men.
Then mark both with pitch (or wax): and make an incision on both sides with a spatula or sharp tool, the incision reaching the bone: and let it be done along the width of the head.
And if one wishes, introduce the spatula under the artery, and make an incision upward with the incision.
Let the length of the incision be like two fingers joined together.
For when an artery is cut, blood comes out with a pulsating flow, which leaps to the interior with frequent jumps.
If, however, the artery does not appear to the senses, then it is necessary that measurements from the ear determine the size of three fingers' space. Then mark both with pitch (or wax) and make an incision up to the bone.
And what must be released from the blood is about 6 ounces, and you may possibly release more or less from it. All of this according to the quantity that appears to you from the strength of the disease and the filling of its artery.
Then observe at the wound. Then if there remains any of the flesh at the bone, then cut it so that a hot abscess does not occur: then tighten the wound with linen rags.
Then care for him with an ointment until he is healed.
On the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
Chapter III.
When an old hemiplegia or acute catarrh due to acidic humoral excess and heat in the neck muscles, or an old sclerosis, violent, and similar conditions occur in a man, and it is treated with methods of medication, but there is no improvement: then we have experience in dealing with such diseases by extracting arteries from the neck or cauterizing them, as we have said.
The method of operation for extracting them (arteries) is as follows: shave the sick hairs that are on the neck, and stretch to the visible artery in the neck. It is indeed evident to you by its pulse and rarely hidden except in a few men or in case of violent coldness.
If it is hidden to you, then let the sick person tighten his head with any cloth of his own and then rub the place with a rough cloth. Or apply heat to the place with warm water until it appears clearly to you. Then take the spatula that I have prepared earlier. Then scrape the skin with it (the spatula) easily until you reach the artery. Then plunge a hook into it (the artery) and pull it upwards until you extract it from the skin, and make it escape from all sides from the layers beneath it.
If the artery is fine: then insert the tip of the hook into it. Then cut off that portion according to its length where the ends are extended and contracted so as not to cause bleeding. For if it is not cut and not separated, blood does not rise deep inside.
Then evacuate the blood to six ounces up to three-quarters.
If the artery is large: it must be tied in two places with strong double thread, silk or catgut, or with a twisted linen strip, so that decay does not occur near it before the wound heals and bleeding occurs.
Then cut the excess, which is between two ligaments. Do this at that hour, or after another hour.
And if you wish, cauterize it with a cautery up to the bone, with a small cautery: until its ends are cut and it remains in place for that same operation.
It is better work unless if the patient has fever, or has a warm constitution. Because the cautery is from those things that help to end moisture. Therefore it is better treatment.
And after the removal of the artery, it is necessary that the place be filled with cooked clay from ancient times; and little balls made of clay should be placed on top of it.
And after the solution, it will be cleaned with dry medications that promote growth of flesh, and with linen cloths until it heals.
If during the operation bleeding occurs from the artery, then hasten to cut it with a cautery, or to fill the place with wax; and press your hand until the blood stops flowing. If nothing from these is present to you, then place your finger on the place until the blood freezes. And pack the place with water of intense cold, until the pain subsides and it is tied as necessary.
And because the vein is lighter and easier to remove, it is to be cauterized with this cautery having two small blades; and the sharpness of the two blades should resemble a lancet. Nevertheless, they are much less sharp than two knives. Because if they are sharp like two knives, cold is needed for both of them; and they do not cut flesh with speed. Since there is a certain thickness in them, heat from fire must be held within them and the flesh is cut quickly; therefore this work is better than any other, and lighter, and easier.
And this is the form of the cautery.
And let the space between two knives be the thickness of a finger, after you mark two places with hot iron; and place both heated ones until they reach the bone, and cut the vein in two places: so that what is between its ends can be removed. They do not coagulate completely with this cautery.
Chapter IV.
Chapter on the care of sharp, frequent epiphora from the eyes.
When the tears are frequent and the flow is from veins on the outside of the skull; and no medicine for their cure is applied to them with medicines; and you see the face of the sick already reddening, and he feels a wandering in his forehead like the wandering of ants; and his eyes are weakened, wet, so that the hairs of them have already been corroded by corrosion; and the eyelids have been heated by the acuity of the tears: then the ancients used this operation for their cure, and they named it treatment with the sword.
And it is to be ordered that the sick person should shave the hairs on his forehead. Then make three cuts in the forehead, equal in length to the forehead; and let the length of the cut be about two fingers, and one cut should be in the middle of the forehead, and the second, a little below the movement of the arms, and the third on the opposite side: and avoid cutting the arteries that are on both sides; and extend your hand from the continuation of the lower jaws, and let the entire length of the cut be the size of three connected fingers: and prepare for yourself a piece of sponge or dry cloth with which to squeeze the blood.
Then insert a double-ended probe (spatula) with sharp tips, which follows its shape immediately. From the first incision that is on the side of the temple, until the second incision: and excise with it all the skin that is between the two incisions, along with the sifak (sinus frontalis) that is above the eye. Then do the same from the central incision until the second incision. Then extract this probe and insert into the first incision another tool called a sharp scalpel, blunt on one side but not on the other. And this is its shape.
And position its sharp side towards the attached flesh with skin and its blunt side towards the bone; push it in until it reaches the midline, and cut with it all vessels that descend from the head to the eyes, except where the incision continues until it appears on the skin.
Then do this along the midline up to another fissure (incision).
And when an equal amount of blood has flowed out, squeeze the places from the clotted blood fragments.
Then put a linen cloth soaked in old oil (or wine or vinegar) into every incision and cover them with small pieces of wool soaked in water, oil, or vinegar. And be careful not to cause a hot abscess (infection).
On the third day, loosen the bandage and administer a large infusion with warm water. Then treat it with basilicon ointment and the other ointments used to heal wounds until it heals.
Chapter 5.
Chapter on the treatment of acute tears (eye discharge) and catarrhs of the eyes from within the skull.
When someone experiences acute and intense catarrhs or tears that are persistent, you see their eyes weakened, small, and their appearance is already debilitated; and their eyelids are ulcerated, hairs fall out from them, and there is a sharp pain deep within the skull, which causes sneezing; then take action on these symptoms when this happens, because those substances and catarrhs do not come unless from many veins.
A better treatment for them is this. And it should be ordered that the sick person shave his forehead. Then make one incision in the middle of the forehead, or slightly to one side, and begin with the incision from the left temple to the right temple; let the incision go as far as the bone; and move your hand away from the temples which move during chewing, until the bone is exposed; then dry up all the blood with a sponge.
Then separate the fissure between the two lips with a spatula or with flax from linen. Then bind it above with thread; and dip the threads in wine and oil, so that no hot abscess occurs.
And when you release it, and see that the abscess is about to burst; then it is necessary to fracture the bone, until flesh begins to grow in it.
Then treat the person with a drying regimen that makes flesh grow; as if you were to take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony; and prepare a plaster from them, and administer it for the growth of flesh in these wounds.
Chapter 6.
Chapter on the care of an ear wound.
Everything that falls into the ear is one of four kinds: either a mineral stone, or something like a stone, such as iron and wood; or it is from a plant, such as chickpeas and beans; or it is fluid, such as water, vinegar, and similar substances; or it is some animal.
When a stone or something like a stone falls into the ear, which does not grow in the ear, lay open the ear; if you see the stone, then pour some oil of roses or sesame into the ear. Then administer the extraction and make it cause sneezing with powder, and insert oil at the nostrils during sneezing; after you place in the ear's edge fragments from cloth or wool, and stretch the ear upward.
For many times, it goes out with this care.
If it does not come out, then administer the extraction with Geppi, that is, finely-powdered pigeon droppings; whose shape is as follows.
If therefore it comes out with Geppi, it is good.
And if not, then administer the extraction with a finely-sharpened blind hook in small doses.
If therefore it does not come out by that, then make a cannula of bronze and insert the end of the cannula into the ear's hole as much as possible; and insert what is in the circumference of the cannula with softened wax mixed with oil, so that there is no path for wind but the cannula; then draw it out with your strong attraction of wind.
For many times, it comes out by what we have said. If it does not come out by this method, then take from helkalimbat or from vinegar (that is, prepared gluten), a small amount; and place it at the end of the radius after you have placed a well-centered piece on top of it; then insert it into the ear's hole with ease, after you have removed the ear from humidity.
If therefore it does not come out by all that we have said, then hurry to cut it before a hot abscess or spasm occurs.
And the method of cutting is that a lancet is applied first to the head; and draw blood from it according to its power. Then make the patient sit between your hands, and turn the ear upward, and make a small incision in the base of the ear near the fat in a depressed place; and let the incision be crescent-shaped until you reach the stone; then remove it with what is possible for you using instruments.
Then, open your wound at your hour (time) with speed, and care for it until it heals.
If something falls into the ear from among the grains that grow and swell, then administer its removal (extraction).
But if it does not obey your attempt to come out, then take a thin, fine pledget, shaped as such.
And administer with it the removal of that kind (species) of grain from those that fall into the ear and do not come out; and do not do this when you believe that the grain is already moistened by the moisture of the ear, until you place many fragments (pieces) thereon: then remove it with tweezers, or with a thin stick, or with suction, as we said, for its extraction will be facilitated.
In water that enters the ear, it is necessary for the sick person to use sneezing with incision at first; and already his ear has been filled with some warm water; and there lies on top of it (the water) the ear. If therefore it comes out through that (opening), it is good.
And if not: then take many small, soft stones (pebbles), and warm them slightly with fire; and the sick person shall insert one of these into the ear's opening; and let him spit on one foot from that side, and strike with another stone upon the stone that is in the ear. Therefore, he should not cease doing it with stone and stone until all the water comes out.
And now the water comes out in such a way that you shall take one from parchment or reed and insert its end into the ear; and you shall light the other end with fire until it is burned much of it. Then take another reed and do this repeatedly until all the water comes out; and remove it with a syringe according to what was said about the stone.
In the extraction of an animal entering into it [the wound], if it is small like a louse, and similar to it, care should be taken as I have said in division.
But if it is of a large body, which appears to the sense: then administer its extraction with forceps and tweezers; and its removal is easier for all who are required to pull it out from the ear.
In the extraction of a worm generated in the ear, when you care for it with what I have said in division, and in treatment of distillation, and your care does not help: then it is necessary that you look at the ear in sunlight. If therefore something appears there [in the ear] of worms, then extract it with forceps, or with fine tweezers.
But if nothing appears there [in the ear], then take a cannula whose form is constricted below and wide above; and insert its fine end into the ear according to the quantity that the sick person can bear; then suck with strong suction. Do this often until all worms come out.
If they do not obey you for exiting, then surround the head of the worms with a cannula and beeswax, as I have said in stone [a chapter about treatment with ointments].
If they do not come out with what I have said, then administer the distillations that were experienced by the ancients in killing worms; and you will find it in treatment of distillation.
And let your flow be with oil and medicines into the ear with this tool, whose shape is depicted here. Make it [the instrument] of silver or brass, constricted below and wide above, with a small hole.
Let the pressing part which is on the concavity of the cannula be made of well-made brass. And if you wish, take the radish, and insert it into the ear opening with a suitable lining: then pour oil, or juice, or whatever medicine you prefer into the cannula; let it be in gold: then insert the radish with the cooked [substance] on top, and press it gently with your hand until the oil is driven into the hollow of the ear, and the sick person feels it inside: and whatever is poured into the ear, let it already be heated slightly with fire: and take care that no substance which distills very cold is put in it; for medicines do not tolerate that.
Chapter 7.
On the Care of Ear Blockage (Auris).
When some infants are born from the wombs of their mothers without perforated eardrums.
It also happens to some people that ear blockage occurs in the cavity of the Ear due to a wound or flesh born in it.
And this blockage sometimes occurs deep within the Ear's cavity, which is not visible to the eye; and sometimes it happens near the outer part of the cavity, which can be seen by the eye.
Therefore, that which occurs deep within the Ear and is not apparent to the eye, is difficult to cure in many respects.
And in that which can be seen by the eye, one must place the sick person's Ear on the sun and observe it; then if you see the blockage appearing, open it with a fine spatula whose shape is as follows: its end should have a small notch, part of which is sharp; and the rest of the spatula should be flat on both sides so as not to injure the Ear.
If the blockage is due to flesh born in the Ear cavity: then hold it with a fine hook and cut it out gently but powerfully until all the flesh is removed.
If there is an opening in the deep part of the ear: then take subtle radium, leno, and heat it slightly with fire; afterward send it into the ear's flesh.
If you find that the patient is weakened by illness with hearing difficulties, try to open it (the ear) easily; and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear.
Then place linen in the ear according to the size of the opening you made, wrapped in Egyptian ointment; do this for several days until you are sure that the wound has healed.
Or take linen and soak it in rose water, sprinkle powdered alum over it, and use it (as a poultice).
If you see that the ear is already suppurating: then it is necessary to remove the linen and allow it to be covered with another piece of linen, wrapped in a cerotto made with rose oil, until the warm suppuration settles; then take care of it until it heals.
If there is bleeding (occurring): then immerse sponges or cloths in cold water and place it on the ear; and use the rest of the treatment that removes the mentioned bleeding in the section on distillations.
Chapter on Altheli's Treatment for Eyes (Eyelids)
Chapter VIII.
These are the Althelils that occur in the eyelids, which are sometimes wet and are sometimes dry.
Therefore, you must hold them with forceps or tweezers: or with a hook, and cut them at their roots with a spatula. Then place it over the place of the bite, grinded.
If blood flows from them, then cauterize them with a thin lentil-shaped cautery.
And it is better to cauterize them after the incision. They often return when something remains from their roots. And when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
Chapter on the care of the eyelids of the eye.
Chapter IX.
It often happens in the eyelids that something similar to a crab occurs, which is hard and tough, and because of this it is called a crab; and it is an accumulation of thick moisture on the upper eyelid, and the lower eyelid.
Therefore, the procedure in them is to examine if there is a crab emerging from it, which appears on the eyelid, and they move around in all directions, and its substance is soft.
Find a split on her (it) in width. Then scrape it from all sides easily, until it comes out. Then hang it with a hook and cut off the pouch.
But if its removal is not prepared for you unless after you pierce the eyelid with a small cut, then it harms the weak in some way.
If the split is large: then bring it together with stitches: and take care of it until it heals.
And if it is small, no harm will come to you from it. Ointment indeed restores and fleshes it.
And if the sand is turned towards the inner parts of the ear with the surface facing inside, then turn the eyelid inward and hang the sand grain with a hook: besides requiring a cut, press it from all sides.
If the eyelid is stretched out by an incision, no harm will come to you from it.
Then wash the eye after the sand grain incision with salt water: and care for the place where it is until the weak heals.

Chapter XII.
§ On plucking painful hairs from the eye with a sharp instrument.
The operation is that you take a subtle point and insert a fine silk thread into it gently. Then gather the ends of it and knot them both with a very subtle knot, and let the length of the threads be one palm [width].
Then combine another fine thread beneath it in a short distance, and knot its ends if you wish.
Then place the weak head of the patient on your lap and bring it close to the sun so that the operation may be clearly seen, because the operation is subtle or delicate.
Then insert the fine point with the scissors into the root of the eyelash and make it penetrate the eyelid quickly until you pull out the natural hair from above.
Then draw the hair up to the scissors and insert the scissors into the hair; if it is one, or two, or three, do not take more than that.
Then draw your hand with it until the hair comes out of the eyelid along with the plucked hair.
If the scissors are pulled out without the hair coming out of the eyelid along with it: pull the scissors downwards with the thread that you have prepared in it until the scissors come out from the upper opening and are visible to the eye; then, when you pull the scissors and the thread, draw both of them out, close the eye and let the closed eye heal for two or three days until the hair adheres to its place and new flesh grows over it.
If the hair is short, then either bind a long hair from natural hairs with it and lift it up together; or leave it alone until it grows out a little, and then lift it up.
Chapter XIII.
When this Alzacter's condition occurs in the eye, it is called Leporina.
And Alzacter's condition is either natural or accidental.
Therefore, the accidental form arises from the consolidation of a wound, a cut, a cautery, and similar things.

And it is not necessary to use in the treatment of this condition things that dry and tighten, for if you do so, Alzacter's condition will become worse than it was; rather, use soft things such as flaxseed: and embrocation with water, in which althea has been boiled, linseed seed: and ointment of djaquilon, which has been made liquefied with some oil: and wrap it with linen, and treat it with it.
And your treasure of healing is to strive with all your skill so that it does not consolidate again in its original form.
And this operation that we have mentioned is not other than a correction of Alzacter's condition, so that it does not return to its original form entirely.
On the care of Alzacter's condition that occurs in the lower eyelid, and is a ridge or contraction upward towards the right and left.
Chapter XIV.
This Alzacter's condition that occurs below is properly called Alzacter's condition. And it is natural, and it is accidental.
From wound, or fracture, or cautery, and similar things it becomes accidental.
The way of the operation in it is that you receive the needle, on which there should be a double thread, and you dye it in flesh, and you make it penetrate from the left tear duct to the right tear duct, until the thread reaches both ends of the flesh.

And if not, take radium, and place it in the fissure, and turn the eyelid with it; and make two fissures on the inner side of the eyelid, and let their extremities be from the two angles of the incision, until they converge and form an angle: until when they come together a figure is formed, and it is a Greek letter lambda.
Then remove that flesh to the extent of its sharp lower part, from what follows the eyelid. Then join the separated parts; or sew it with a woolen thread.
Then take care of them with what I said, with softening medicines and linen cloths, until they heal.
And if the Alxatratus happens from the fissure or stitching or cauterizing: then it is necessary to make a flat wound under the eyelashes, even as it was before. Then separate between two lips with linen cloth, as I said.
The summary of the discussion on treating Alxatratus, whether it is above or below, is that the treatment should be performed according to the preparation for the form of Alxatrati.
For indeed it has many diverse forms; and the skillful craftsman prepares his talent with whatever means is possible for him, until he brings back the figure to its natural form or close to it, and himself who is ill, according to what suits him from the operation and instruments in various positions.

Chapter on the adhesion of the eyelid with the conjunctiva or cornea.

Chapter on incision of nail and protrusion of skin around eyelashes.
Chapter XVI.
Know that the nail is of two kinds. Or it is nervous: and is similar to horn, but delicate. It is not a nerve, similar to the consistency of frozen white moisture; when iron touches it or one tries to grasp it with a forceps, it is torn away and the forceps do not take hold in it.
And neither of the kinds begins except from the greater tear duct, up until it gradually reaches the eye, until it fills the sight, and prevents light, and movement of the eye.
The method of operation in its incision is: that the sick person places his head in your lap. Then open his eyes, and lift the eyelid with your hand. Then collect a few double-spaced claws with forceps and extend them upward. Then take a spear and insert a horse hair or ox or sheep hair into it, let it be a thread, and slightly double the end of the spear point, and fix it in the middle of the claw; penetrate it with the spear and tie it with the thread to the claw, and extend it upward; peel off the side of the claw following the pupil as if you were holding it with the hair up until the end of it.
Then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with a thin spatula or small forceps; let the natural tissue of the tear duct remain, so that no persistent flow of tears occurs due to its incision.
And sometimes the claw is extended with forceps alone; or with a thread, as we said. Then it is scraped with a soft spatula, which has this form.
And be careful that the soft spatula does not touch the corn layer and cause a break there, and pierce the pupil.
Then after the incision, throw something crushed salt or made from chalk into the eye and let it stay until another day. Then take care of him with what is required, until he is healed.
If the nail is not sensitive and you cannot insert a probe into it nor apply a clamp to it, then repeatedly treat this kind of nail with medications, and it will heal as I have described in the division.
If you wish to cut it, then open the sick person's eye and take a thin, soft, weakly sharp probe of this shape. And shave the nail from above with delicacy. If you see that it becomes rarefied and crushed, and press a razor into it, then drip from your hour (urine) into the eye made from seif or from ziniar, or from red seif ground fine: and keep the eye closed until another day.
Then repeat the operation on it until the entire thing is removed. Unless a hot abscess appears in your eye, then leave it alone and treat the abscess until it is healed.
Then repeat the operation on it with delicacy, until it is healed.
The growth of the flesh on the eyelash, if it causes great harm to the eye, is to be suspended with a clamp and cut off that part of it; not too deep so as not to disturb the flow of tears.
Then drip red seif or seif made from ziniar into the eye until it is healed.
Chapter on Incision of Albucasis and growth of flesh in the eye.
Chapter 17.
Sometimes in the eyes of men there grows red flesh composed or laid on top, covering the pupil or approaching it, or pressing against the eyelids and perhaps turning the eyelids toward the outside; and it resembles a balustrade rose.
The operation in it is also to place the sick head in your armpit. Then open his eyes and collect the entire flesh with suitable hooks to it; hold it with a single forceps or tweezers.
Then cut the flesh first, until you finish it all with a knife. Take care not to touch the eye during the operation; make your cut be such that it is made as we have described in the incision of the nail, or with tweezers like those used for asbestos, according to the shape it will take after this chapter.

And similarly do with any flesh that happens to be present in the eye of this kind.
Nevertheless, any weakening of the eye from a natural or accidental cause must be treated by cutting with iron; and do not insert your hand into any of these operations until you see that the member is able to withstand this treatment.
Chapter on removing asbestos from the eye.
Chapter XVIII.
Asbestos are veins of red color that cover the eye and impede vision; they weaken the eye day by day.
Therefore, first you must consider if the eye in which asbestos is found is strong and there is no other illness except for asbestos; then collect the asbestos of it.
And it is that you command the sick one, that he places his head in your bosom.
Then suspend those veins with one or two needles according to your judgment: and let the needle be fine of double fold, according to this shape, or let there be two needles graduated in one body, according to this shape.
Then collect with fine forceps those veins and remove the blood by the hour, until you see the veins removed from the eye and resolved: and be careful not to hurt the eye with the tips of the forceps.
And let your work be at noon before the sun, and be very firm in your work: so as not to cut except those veins.
And when you have finished, then distill into the eye green or red: so that with its own acidity it burns what remains from the scalpel.
If it is not possible for you to collect all of it in that hour, then plaster the eye with that which soothes the pain of the eye: and leave it for some days until the pain subsides: and bind it with warm poultice: then again repeat over it according to the same method until it heals.
And this is the form of the forceps.
Chapter on reducing Arissatas (nasal polyps) to the nose.
Chapter XIX.
The surgeon is called Arisatha, and he treats the Fistula, which he cures with a cautery or with a medicine burning sharply, according to his narrative that has gone before.
If it is not healed, then there is no skill in this case, except to open a boil at its birth and remove all the moisture that is in it and the pus, until the bone appears.
When the bone is exposed, and you see in it corruption or blackness, then grind it with an instrument of this form.
And it is called Asperga for the head.
Make it from iron and round its head like a needle, pierced by the grinding of a file or a finely-pointed aliskilfer; place it on the corrupted bone.
Then turn it over between your fingers and press your hand a little, until you know that the corruption has been ground away; do this repeatedly.
Then restore the place with very dry ointments.
If the place consolidates and flesh grows in it, and the flow of pus is stopped; and forty days have passed, and it does not break open again, nor develop an abscess, nor does anything else happen in it; then you know that it has been healed.
If not, then there is no skill in this case, except to lead the fistula back to the nostril, according to this shape.
And it is to be exposed from the second bone with iron or with a sharp medicine; when the bone has been exposed, then take a gimlet according to this shape, its tip being made of iron, triangular: and let the wood of it be a pyramid extended to the end, as you see.
Then place it on the bone itself; let it be near the tear duct; and extend your hand slightly away from the eye. Then turn your hand with the lancet until it penetrates the bone and feels it weak; by this you will find wind coming out of it when you hold your hand over his nose.
Then restore the place with medicines that dry (or stop bleeding), as I have taught you.
When the flesh grows and the place hardens, then what was flowing out to the outside returns to the nose; therefore it is lighter above the weak one.

Chapter 20.

Chapter on the incision of the eyelid.
Chapter XXI.
