[Title] On the cure of Alcomnat.
Chapter XXII.
This disease called Alcomnat is not other than pus that accumulates in the eye, similar to descending water, and it is not itself.
And the method of operation in this case is that you make the sick person sit on a prepared chair or straight-backed one.
Then take hold of his head with your hands from both sides and move him until you see the pus reach the lower parts of your eyes. Then it is shaped, and does not fall down, and the vision is cleared; and the sick person sees as he saw before: and if it does not fall lower, know that it is water.
If however the descent of pus is not prepared as we said, then make the patient sit between your hands. Then take a thin probe and pierce it through the cornified panniculus continuous with the cornea at the junction with the tunica cornea in the corona, until the pus is expelled.
When it comes out, then pour warm water into which you have mixed honey over it; or hot water in which you have already boiled fennel and honey; then treat it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter on the care of water that falls into the eye, or cataract.
Chapter XXIII.
We have already said the type of water in division and which is suitable for perforation in speech declaring and explaining it, then take the same according to its health.
Then it is necessary that you make the patient sit with your hands facing each other, opposite to the eye, near the sun; and tie the healthy eye, and squeeze it very tightly; then close the eyelid of the affected eye with your right hand, if the water is in the left eye; or with your left hand, if the water is in the right eye.
Then take your right hand with a large spoon, if the eye is the left; or your left hand with a large spoon, if the eye is the right.
Then place the almadga near the corona proximate to the apparent lachrymal of the smaller eye-socket; then push the almadga with force, and you will roll your hand together with it, until it penetrates into the white part of the eye; and you will feel that the almadga has reached the empty space.
And it is necessary that there be a measure for the journey of the almadga to the depth, a measure of the space from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and this is the corona of the eye. For indeed you will see it in the pupil of the eye itself, due to the clarity of the cornea coating.
Then place the almadga up until where there is water. Then press it downward once after another.
If therefore the water descends immediately, then the sick person sees immediately whatever opens his vision, and the almadga in his eye.
Then rest for a little while. If therefore the water descends, then put it down in the second place, beyond which the almadga emerges.
When it is clogged and does not rise, then extract the almadga with ease; and you roll your hand slowly.
Then dissolve something from salt in water of the gemma, and wash the eye with it. Then place over the entire eye all wool soaked in rose oil or linen and the white part of the eye; and bind it with a clean bandage.
We and those who are in our time place over him camphor powder with the white part of the eye.
If the almadga does not obey you in entering the eye due to its hardness, since it is from a man whose eye is very hard; then it is necessary that you take Spatholea (Alberid), whose form is as follows:
Perforate only the connecting tissue and not the final joint; and it is not to be done except to make a passage to a subtle place.
Then introduce almagda, as we have said.
Prepare for your procedure a well-made bed for the sick person in which he may sleep on his back in a dark room; and keep him free from movement, coughing; and put food for him that soothes his nature; and do not let him turn his head to either side at all.
And let the ligament remain according to its position until the third day.
Then dissolve that in the dark room and test his sight; and make him see things. Then bring back the ligament until the seventh day.
It should not be done during the hour of cure or immediately after cutting; rather it should be done by others because water rises quickly through a vehement heat.
If, however, an abscess occurs that is hot: then it is necessary to dissolve the eye before the seventh day; and rectify that with what calms the abscess until it is calm; then remove his sight from him and place on his mouth orally whatever regulates his sight during several days, while he remains in that dark room.
Then leave the house gradually and change into your clothes.
And know that a student is not allowed to be absent from view often; then he dares at the operation.
Now someone from those of Alayrach has arrived who said that a large perforation was made in Alayrach where water flows out.
Therefore I have not seen anyone in your country who has done that; nor have I read it in any old books; and it is possible that it is new.
These are the shapes and appearances from the hand, so that they may stand upon him who knows them not.
Make from bronze: and let their extremities have the same subtle triangular shape, and the extremity be sharp.
Chapter XXIV.
Treatment for the born flesh in the nose.
Sometimes in the nose are born diverse fleshes added, of which there is something similar to the many-footed scorpion; and from it there is a cancerous flesh, stony, dark colored; and from it there is one that is soft flesh, not dark colored.
In the one that is among these fleshes soft, not fraudulent, nor cancerous, you must make the sick man sit facing the sun, and open his nostrils, and thrust the hook into those fleshes; then draw them out to the exterior, and cut what you have grasped with a subtle spoon-like instrument sharp at one side, until you know that all the flesh is removed.
If anything remains from that one whose removal is not possible; then shave it with a subtle instrument with ease until nothing remains from it. If blood dominates you, or a hot boil occurs; then oppose it with the necessary remedy; or if it is among the malignant boils, then hurry to cauterize him, until the blood is removed and all fleshes are removed.
Then vinegar, or water, or wine is thrown into the nose after the incision. If the nostril opens and moisture proceeds to the palate, then you know that he is well.
If moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you know that there is born flesh within the upper nasal bones, to which the instrument did not reach with the incision.
Then it is necessary that you insert a thread of linen with some thickness and many knots; and place between every knot an amount equal to a digit or less; and make the sick one send out one end of the thread into his nose with a probe, or as he can do after he has done this, similar to the aze; and pull the scented substance until it reaches the cavity, and exit on his throat.
And indeed many times boys do this which is similar to that of Attomus in schools; and it is easy for him who desires it.
Then place two ends of the thread, one which exits on the nose and the other that remains in the nose. Then as a servant, sew together the flesh with knots that are in the thread. Do this until you know that the flesh is now with the knots of the thread.
Then pull out the thread; and put linen in the nose after bloodletting which you have soaked in Egyptian ointment; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has completely corroded what remains of the flesh.
Then at the end, put a tube of lead into the nose for some days until it heals.
If however there is need for treatment to dry it, use that.
For the purge to be made with oil and other medications into the nose, make it of silver or copper; it should be like a small lamp, open as a shell and its opening similarly.
And if you wish to make a closed tube, like a tube.
And the shell instrument for the purge should be full, pierced; to which there should be a handle at the end of it, with which you hold it when heating oil or what you wish from juices and flowable things in it.
Chapter XXV.
Many times is born at the end of the nose, Thelul, and it swells, and grows larger with days, until its appearance becomes foul.
And because of that, it is necessary to cut it at the beginning of its appearance and to remove all of it. Then place on the spot either cautery or medicine burning in its place.
If the cutting of it is delayed until it swells, then consider if it is hard, stone-like, dark colored, and with few senses; then do not touch it with iron because it is a cancerous boil.
For often I have seen that one cuts a boil, and great evil comes upon him who has it.
And if the boil is soft and not dark colored, and you see that it can be cut completely, then evacuate the weak, and cut it without fear, without dread; and take care of the place where it was with the remedy to draw it out and constrict it until it heals.
Chapter 26.
Section on the stitching of the nose, and lip, and ear.
Know that when there is loosening of continuity in one of these cartilages, the operation does not help much unless in certain men.
Therefore, when something happens to anyone from it, you should consider if it is a recent wound with its blood; and then gather together two strips of the wound with suture; then take care of it until it heals.
And if the loosening of continuity of the lip has already separated and each part is healthy; then it is necessary to remove all the edge from its visible skin until it bleeds. Then gather together the two lips with suture and bind them; then sprinkle over it the powder of dragon's blood and pulverized olibanum; and put on top of the powders a piece of an emollient plaster and any other consolidating plaster; and let it be bound for two or three days. Then dissolve it (the suture), and change the medicine: and let it be until the threads are separated by themselves. Then treat it with ointment, until it is healed.
The method of suturing is to gather the solution of continuity with needles, as we have said in abdominal sutures: or gather the solution with thread, as I have told you.
Chapter 27.
Chapter on the removal of neck nodes.
Many men occur, and often in the inner parts of their own lips, hard ulcers similar to grains of grain: and some of them smaller, and others larger.
Therefore, it is necessary that you turn the lip, and cut on top of every node of it, and hang it up with a hook, and cut it from all sides.
Then you shall fill the place after the cut with lime until the blood is separated.
Then it is scraped with vinegar, and the place where there is hardening is rubbed with it, until the wounds heal.
Chapter XXVIII.
Chapter on the incision of the flesh of a newborn on the gums.
Often flesh grows over the gum, which the ancients called abscesses.
Therefore it is necessary to hang it up with a hook or hold it with forceps and cut it at the root, and let the pus run out, or blood.
Then put on top of the place lime or other healing powders, drying.
If that flesh returns after treatment, which often happens, then cut it again the second time and cauterize it; for it does not return after cauterization.
Chapter XXIX.
Chapter on filing of teeth with iron.
When the teeth accumulate on their surfaces from inside and outside, and between the gums rough, dirty, and sometimes they turn yellowish or greenish, until corruption reaches the gum and the teeth become foul through it.
Therefore it is necessary that you make the sick person sit between your hands, and put his head in your lap, and file the pulp and tooth, where the gums appear, and it is like sand; until there remains nothing of them, and similarly do for yellowish, greenish, blackish, and others, until they are cleaned.
If therefore that which is in them at the beginning of reason is removed, it is good: and if not, then apply reason to them on another day, second, and third, until finally study reaches what you desire.
And know that the tooth requires variously shaped razors of many shapes; according to which it is prepared for your operation: therefore, because the razor with which the tooth is scraped from below is different from the razor with which it is scraped between the teeth, according to other forms.
These forms of the razors should be prepared by you, which you see.
Chapter XXX.
Chapter on the extraction of tooth pain.
It is necessary that you cure Tooth from its pain with all your skill, and be not hasty in its extraction. There is not another to take its place when it is extracted: because it is a substance that rises high: until there is no excuse for its extraction, then if one who is sick must extract it, it should be made firm, and the tooth in pain should be certified by you.
Often pain deceives the sick man and believes that there is worm in tooth and extracts it himself: then the pain does not subside until the diseased tooth is extracted.
We have already seen that from phlebotomy. (referring to bloodletting)
When the tooth in pain is certified by you, then it is necessary that you make an incision around the tooth with a spatula containing something of virtue, until the gums are loosened on all sides: then move it with your fingers or with delicate forceps first slowly, until you shake it.
Then place the large forceps in that place with a good grip, and hold the head of the sick one between your knees: for what you have well held, so that it does not move: then pull the tooth according to its straight line, so as not to break it.
If it does not come out then take one of those instruments and introduce it below it from all sides with ease, and try to move it as you did at first.
If the tooth is perforated or worn away then it is necessary that you fill that hole with a cloth and tie it with the end of a delicate radius so as not to break it during your constriction above it with the forceps.
And you must be careful when making an incision around the gums from all sides a lot.
And guard your strength so as not to break it and a part remains of it and returns to the sick one from that mischief which is greater than its initial pain.
And beware, lest you do what ignorant phlebotomists do in haste, and because of their arrogance in excision, except for what we have mentioned.
For many times they bring on great afflictions in men, which are difficult to break, and the roots of it remain all or some: or that they extract it with certain jaw bones: as we have often testified this.
Then it is to be anointed after excision with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
If bleeding should occur from the places (for it often happens), then rub something from beeswax and fill the place with it: and if not, cauterize it if you do not have beeswax.
The handles of fine forceps with which the molar is moved should be long at the ends, short at the grip, thick, so that they do not split when pressed upon the tooth: as you see, those of the thick handles, until when you tighten them, they do not slip and do not split: the tips should be short and made of hard iron or well-made copper, pointed tips: and in their tips there should be teeth, some of which enter into some and hold tight with a decent constriction, strong.
And sometimes the tips are like the shape of a bird's beak, which is called a ciconia, and they are strong in constriction.
Chapter 31.
Chapter on Extraction of Teeth and Removal of Fractured Jaw Bones.
When something remains after the extraction of a tooth that is breaking, then you should place hot cotton over it for one or two days until the place softens: then insert algaster or forceps, whose tips are similar to the beak of a bird called ciconia. This form is forceps.
The ends of them (forceps) are made like a plane's edge, or as an aliskilfeghi (a type of forceps).
If therefore it (a part of the body) does not come out with these forceps, then it is necessary that you be careful on the root and expose the whole flesh and introduce an instrument which is called a small Palanca, whose form is this.
Let the end (of the forceps) be short, thick somewhat less: and let it not be filled with liquid, so that it may not break.
If therefore the root comes out through this (instrument), it is good: and if not, it is necessary to aid with these other instruments whose forms are these.
The form of the first triangular end, in which there is some thickness.
The form of the subtle triangular end.
And with other instruments and tools which have been mentioned in the ratio of teeth.
Also aid with this instrument similar to a large nail, whose form is the triangular twisted end with some thickness, so that it may not break: and let it not be filled with liquid.
And know that the instruments for teeth are many: and similarly other instruments are not accounted, and a skillful artist, subtle in his art, finds for himself an instrument according to what is signified by the operation and the illness itself.
Because from illnesses there are those for which the ancients did not find an instrument, due to the diversity of their forms.
If however the bone breaks from the jaw, or from other bones of the face, or it rots: then to investigate on it (the tooth) itself in its place with that which suits it from among instruments and forceps which I have said for extraction of roots, and aid with gesti whose form is this.
Place something of some thickness in it [the wound], gradually so that a bone can be held or tied to it, and it does not escape and move away, until the bone comes out: and restore the place with appropriate medications for it.
If there is a small rottenness in the bone, then shave it off from its rot, and treat it until it heals.
Chapter XXXII.
On the setting of protruding teeth above others.
When teeth protrude not according to their natural course, an ugly shape arises from it; and this occurs particularly when it happens in women and girls, that is, in those who menstruate.
Therefore you should consider. For if a tooth is born after another tooth and does not settle or can be set, or its removal or trimming is not possible; then uproot it: and if it is attached to another tooth, then cut it with this tool whose form is as follows.
It resembles a small beak and is made from iron with a very sharp tip.
And your cut should be such that you make the incision over many days and because of the hardness of the tooth so that another tooth is not disturbed.
If it is protruding and exposed to trimming; then trim it with a file made of iron whose form is as follows.
It should be made entirely of iron and the handle small with numerous sharp points like a file used to make a needle; with which you can trim the tooth gradually over many days with ease, so that another tooth is not disturbed and it falls out: then smooth it gently, in the end shave it off with certain rasps.
If it is a tooth that breaks off and injures the tongue; then it should be filed down until the roughness of the break is removed and leveled: and smoothed, so as not to injure the tongue nor corrupt speech.
Quid autem de extractione dentes in quibus
On the twisting of teeth with threads of gold.
In the case of teeth that have been struck or jolted due to blow or accident and the patient cannot hold what he eats without it falling out; and treatment with medicinal poultices has failed; then it is appropriate for them to be threaded with a gold wire, because silver turns green and rots after days, but gold never changes.
And the thread should be of medium thickness and coarseness according to its quantity that it may fit between the teeth.
The shape of the twisting is that you take the thread and insert its double between two healthy teeth; then wind it with its two ends between the moving teeth, whether one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side with the needle. Then wind again to the part from where you started; and hold your hand with delicacy and wisdom until it is completely removed; and your pressure when threading the wire should be at the roots of the teeth so that it does not escape.
Then cut the excess ends of the thread with scissors; and join both, and turn them towards each other; and hide these under the healthy tooth and the moving tooth so as not to hurt the tongue; then release it when tightly fastened.
If it loosens or breaks, thread them with another wire and it will remain in place for the whole time.
And this is the form of teeth and the shape of twisting two healthy teeth and two moving teeth, as you see.
Sometimes a tooth or teeth return to their place after an accident, and are held as we have said, and remain; this is not done unless by an experienced craftsman who is both wise and skilled.
And sometimes a bone from a cow is made suitable: and it is formed like a tooth and placed where the tooth is protected and tightened, as we have said; and it remains and serves for a long time.
Chapter XXXIIII.
Sometimes this ligament that occurs under the tongue is natural, with which a man is born, or accidental, from a healed wound.
The operation in this is to open the weak mouth of the patient in your chest, and lift the tongue; then cut that nerve ligament across its width until the tongue is released from its holding.
If there is something hard and knotty in it, and it is from the consolidation of a wound; then thrust a hook into it and pierce it across its width until you cut the ligament, and the knot is released.
And be careful that there is no opening in deep flesh, and do not cut an artery there and let blood flow.
Then it is washed with rose water or vinegar or cold water.
Then place a flannel of linen under the tongue for the patient to hold at all night so that it does not harden again.
If blood flows out, then place onion paste over the place. If the blood resists you, then cauterize the place with a flat cautery that is suitable for it; then care for it yourself until it heals.
Chapter XXXV.
Sometimes a boil occurs under the tongue that resembles a small frog, preventing the tongue from performing its natural function; and perhaps it swells so much that it fills the bone.
The operation in him is, to open the weak bone in the sun's presence: and examine the boil.
If you see him of dark or black color, hard, which does not have a weak sensation, then do not touch it because it is cancer.
And if it is hollowed out towards whiteness, in which there is wetness, then throw a hook into it and cut it with a delicate spatula and free it from all sides. What if blood presses you during your operation hour, then place upon it a piece of zinc until the blood is separated; afterwards return to your operation until you draw it out with its entirety.
Then cleanse it with vinegar and salt; care for the rest of the treatment as suitable to that until it is healed.
§ On the cure of two boils, the Molar teeth.
Chapter XXXVI.
When sometimes they happen near the throat, that is, the glands which resemble the goiters, which appear outside; and they are called the two Molar teeth: when you treat them as we said above in division, and they do not heal, then examine.
If it is a hard boil of dark color with few sensations, then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is of red color and the root is thick: then do not touch it even with iron, fearing blood flow; rather let it be until it matures. And then either you will pierce it or it bursts by itself.
And if it is of white color, round and the root is subtle: then it should be cut.
The operation on it is, to examine it before the operation itself, if the boil has stopped being hot and quieted completely or has decreased slightly: then let the patient sit in the sun with his head in your lap; open his mouth, and take a servant between your hands and press his tongue downwards with an instrument of this shape.
Make it from silver, or brass, that it may be as delicate as a scalpel.
When therefore you press with it your tongue, and the boil is shown to you, and it falls upon the same (boil), then take a hook, and fix it in the boil, and pull it out as far as possible, except that you pull something along with it from the tunics.
Then cut it (the abscess) with the instrument which has the following shape: The forceps are to be made similar: however, the tips of it should be curved, so that the opening of each of them is directly opposite the other's sharp point: therefore, care should be taken that it is made of iron or brass coated with lead.
If this instrument is not present, then cut it with a pair of scissors having such shape. Let one part be sharp, not the other.
And after cutting one almond, cut the other according to the same shape of the incision.
Then, after the incision, the sick person shall rinse with cold water, or with vinegar and water.
If bleeding occurs, rinse with water in which the peels of pomegranates have been boiled; or leaves of myrtle, and similar things from willow bark, until the bleeding stops; then take care of him until he is healed.
And sometimes boils other than almonds may occur in the throat. Therefore, cut them as I said for the incision of the two almonds equally.
And I myself have been cured of a woman who had a boil that was born in her throat, which dragged her to asphyxia, with few senses, which almost closed her throat; and the woman breathed through a narrow mouth, and she had already prohibited food for herself, and drink of water: and it was about to reach death, if it had remained one or two days.
The boil had risen only so much that it discharged two branches, until they came out through the two nostrils.
I approached quickly and fastened one of them with a hook. Then I pulled it, and a large piece came out.
Then I cut it where it was seized from the nostril.
Then I made that which came out through the other nostril hole.
Then I opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; then I fastened a hook on the boil; then I cut off part of it, but nothing else ran out except a little blood; therefore, the woman's throat was healed, and she began to drink water immediately, then ate food.
I did not stop cutting from the boil for a long time; and the boil grew in place of what I was cutting until it became too prolonged and with her, [it seems that] I have made it worse.
I made an incision and burnt the boil at her throat.
Therefore it stopped growing; then I went away from there, but I did not know what God did with her after me.
[Section on the incision of a boil in the throat.]
Chapter XXXVII.
When the catarrh descends to the throat and becomes a boil that is long; then it is called perpendicular; and if it is thick and round in the lower part, then it is called uva.
When it is treated with what I have said in the division, and there is no improvement; and you see that the boil has become warm and thin; then it should be cut.
And what has gathered around it is round and not long, and it is red, dark or black, and there is no sensation; then it should be cut off. For there is fear over the sick person.
Therefore, when you see it according to the manner I have said from whiteness and length, let the sick person sit facing the sun; then press his tongue with the instrument whose description has preceded; then fasten a hook in the boil, and pull it downwards; and cut it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of two tonsils.
It is necessary that you not cut from it, unless what is added exceeds the natural limit without addition.
If you cut more from it, you harm the voice and discourse.
Then, after the incision, use what we have said concerning the incision of two tonsils and take care of it until it heals.
If the sick person is afraid of the incision, then it is necessary to use skill in cauterizing it without fear and cowardice.
The method of cauterization is not anything but with sharp water and it is, to place the head of the sick person in your lap. Then press the tongue with the tool that we have said. Then take water from the water that I have told you in the chapter on cauterization and melt with it an unquenched lump of chalk and do not make it thick or thin, but fill the hollow of this tool with it, whose shape is as follows:
Let the concavity at its end where the medicine is placed be concave like a conch shell's radius.
Place the tool with the medicine on the wound itself: let the sick person lie on his side so that the saliva from his mouth runs out through the internal medicine, so that something does not descend from it to his throat and harm him.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. Then you apply it to the wound for the first time with a quantity of half an hour, until you see it darkened and the pain of the medicine subsided.
And if you want to take a piece of cotton and wrap it around the end of the radius, and pour the cotton with the medicine over it, and insert the radius into the canal above it until the cotton sticks to the wound.
Do this repeatedly until you achieve what you want from the cauterization of the vein. Then let it go: indeed it dries up and falls off after three or four days.
If you need to apply medicine again, apply it again: and after cauterization, wipe around the area with a cloth soaked in butter and clean it with that which is in the surrounding area from the medicine: and pour cold water over it.
It shall be treated externally with plasters and internally with poultices until healed.
Therefore this method of treatment is healthier than surgery and less to be feared.
And sometimes the ulcer is treated with a method that is more subtle than cauterization and surgery: it is treated with fumigation, according to this method. Take calamus, hyssop, origanum, ruta, sassafras, chamomile, abrotanum and similar herbs: mix all of them or some of them in a pot, and submerge them with vinegar, and boil them: the pot should be coated with clay properly: there should be a hole in the middle of the pot, over which an instrument concave according to this method is placed.
Make it from silver or bronze: and insert the end, where there is a grain, into the sick man's nostril, until the vapor reaches the ulcer through the tube, until the ulcer is covered with a lot.
Then apply it many times over it until it dries up.
And beware not to perform this treatment at the beginning of the abscess's arrival. Usually pus is added to the abscess: and it should not be done unless at the time of the abscess's decline towards heat.
If this instrument is not available to you, then take a cannula and make a layer of ox horn at its end so that the sick man's bone is not burned: because the ox hide prevents the vapor from burning the bone: and this is a good treatment with safety.
On the extraction of thorns and bones from the throat.
Item, si quid in gutture positum inveniri sit,
Also, if anything found in the throat is bone or fish spine, or something else...
Therefore, whatever appears visible from among them [bones or fish spine], that must be extracted after you press the tongue with an instrument near the sun, and when it is made clear to you that it is in the throat...
And whatever is not visible and hidden in the throat, you should make a gentle vomit before the food is digested in the stomach... Perhaps it will come out attached through vomiting.
Or the sick person swallows a piece of nutmeg or radish root, or a piece of dry bread crumb; or he may take a soft piece of sponge dried and bind it, then swallow it... When the place where the spine or bone is reaches, and it is extracted, it comes out.
If it does not come out with what we said [vomiting], then use an instrument made of lead in this shape...
Let it be larger than a finger joint, and at its end, let there be a hook, which can easily be inserted into the throat; and it should have a head raised upward...
And be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that it does not cause coughing and push the bone or spine with it, or a doctor may insert his hand...
But what the sick person inserts is better [for extraction], since he has knowledge of the place where the thing is attached; and he should push it down or pull his hand with the instrument upward, all according to the size that is prepared for him until it comes out...
On the extraction of leech.
Head, XXXIX.
When the leech (sanguisuga) is treated as I mentioned in the division of cure with medicines and it does not help, then consider if there is a problem in the throat of the sick person in the presence of sunlight, or after the sun if you press his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
If therefore your sight falls on the leech (sanguisuga), remove it with a small hook or with fine forceps carefully.
If it is not possible with them (small hook or forceps): then take a concave cannula and insert it into the throat of the sick person as far as the throat; then insert into the concavity of the cannula hot iron with fire. Do this repeatedly, and let the sick person refrain from water for the entire day.
Then let him take a vessel full of cold water, and open his mouth in it; wash his face with it, and swallow nothing from it; move the water one hour after another with his hand. For the leech (sanguisuga) immediately when it feels water falls off.
If it does not come out with what I mentioned, then fumigate the sick person with bedbugs or with asa with the instrument that I told you about for fumigation of the ear.
Do this repeatedly, because it will fall off by itself.
And the method of operation in fumigation is that you take a pot, in which there are live plums with fire; and let the pot be covered with a lid, through the middle of which there is an opening; and arrange the end of the instrument in it.
Then throw the fumigation, and let the sick person place his mouth at the end of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the fumigation does not come out, until you know that the fumigation has reached the leech (sanguisuga). The bloodsucker falls immediately.
If it does not fall, then repeat multiple fumigations.
The sick man endures thirst, eats salt and other things, but drinks no water.
Therefore, it is necessary that he goes out with this regimen.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the bloodsucker is drawn from the throat when it falls upon the same eyesight.
It resembles forceps, as you see; but it has this curvature that is inserted into the throat. And the end of it resembles the beak of a bird called ciconia, in which there is roughness like that of a file; when it grasps something, it does not let go of it entirely.
[Title: On the opening of abscesses, and their section, and care in general.]
Chapter XL (40).
The species of abscesses are many, according to the remembrance of them, that is, one and one in this book; and they are diverse in their perforation, and their section from two modes.
One of them is of the kind of abscess within itself and because it contains moisture.
The second method is concerning places where it occurs from the body.
Because an abscess occurring on the head is different from an abscess occurring in the anus; and an abscess occurring in a fleshy place is different from an abscess occurring in joints: and each of them has its own judgment by operation.
And among abscesses there are some that should not be pierced unless after the maturation of pus in them and its completion; and there are some that should be pierced while they are raw and do not mature according to its completion.
As abscesses which are near joints.
Because when an abscess occurs near a joint and prolongs itself, until it becomes putrid perhaps the tendons or nerves of that joint are corrupted; therefore it is the cause of closer contraction of that member.
Or it is an abscess near a main member; because if you delay the piercing of it until it matures, it will harm either itself or through the main member.
Or it is near the anus, pierce it when it is immature; and it should not be pierced, if the abscess is raw, not completed digestion, unless it is near the anus, so that it does not become putrid deeply, and reaches the interior of the anus, and becomes a fistula, or becomes at its end which does not heal.
It is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is matured according to its completion; and this is in sedation of pain, decrease of fever, and diminution of redness, and pulsation, and sharpness of the head of the abscess; and the remaining signs.
And it is necessary that you make the same perforation in the lower part of the abscess and with greater prominence: and the perforation should extend along the length of the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of hands and feet, and in the regions of shoulders, and tendons, and nerves, and arteries, and finally in all places without reflection.
In those which are reflected, go with the perforation according to that limb.
When the abscess is in fleshy places: then it is better to leave the perforation of it until its digestion is confirmed, as we said according to the completion.
Because if you perforate it before that (time), the course of the virus from it is prolonged, and there are many dirt and foulnesses, and perhaps its lips harden, and its depth increases.
And some abscesses are perforated according to the width of the body due to necessity, or according to that limb which requires it.
And it is necessary that you make a small perforation for small abscesses and a large one for large abscesses, or numerous cuts according to the size of the abscess.
And there are abscesses in which the skin must be concaved: and it should be cut when it has become like cloth, and made into a form that is already dead: such as what happens with boils and buboes.
And there are some which are to be cut through a section having three angles. And from it is cut in the form of a myrtle leaf (figure).
As an inguinal abscess.
And from it is administered a round cut and a crescent-shaped cut, and similar ones: such as those from cuts.
The thing which has no head, such as are soft ulcers on the surface, should be perforated with a shallow perforation, or only a flat one.
When the ulcer is large and already has collected much pus, and you have perforated it, so that it does not burst out and you extract all the pus at once: rather, extract a part of it from it. Then, remove the ulcer up to another day. Then, extract something from the pus again.
Do this often according to its progression, until it comes out: especially if the person is weak in strength, or a woman who is pregnant, or a small child, or an old man who has decayed: for the animal spirit is often resolved with the exit of pus: and perhaps the weak one dies, and you do not receive payment.
Be careful then, this chapter requires great caution.
After your perforation, which you make for these ulcers, it is necessary that you clean the wound and consider. If then the wound of the ulcer is small, or if it is a plain incision, then apply linen cloth or old cotton. If the ulcer is large and there are many perforations of the fissures, then you should insert linen into each fissure until they meet.
If you have cut off a piece of skin from the ulcer, or if you have hollowed out its circumference: then it is necessary to fill it with old cotton, or as when a cloth is sewn together, or made into linen yarn without moisture: and tighten it for three days.
Then throw it away, and care for it with whatever is necessary from the ointment until it heals.
If it should happen that there is a flow of blood during your operation, then administer cold water and vinegar after the linen cloth has been soaked in them: and place it on the site of the blood flow many times.
If the flow of blood persists, then it is necessary to administer a regimen, treatment, and powders which I have described in many parts of this our book, and according to division.
If it is winter time and the place of the boil is many nerves: then it is necessary to pour warm powders with wine and oil, and place them on those areas.
And if it is summer and the areas are fleshy: then it is necessary to place warm powders soaked in water, oil or wine and oil, and all that cold. Until the third day, as we said, then it is necessary to dissolve the boil, remove it, and administer treatment for its healing until it heals.
This is therefore what is necessary universally for the knowledge of treating boils.
According to the way of distinguishing it, I have already said about every boil, how is the path for its healing chapter by chapter individually.
Chapter 41.
Chapter on the cutting of boils that occur on the head skin.
In the skin of the head occur small boils, which belong to the species of nodules that are contained by bags, which are like they themselves have been sucked by a hen.
And their types are many.
From them are the fat ones: and from them are those that contain moisture similar to mud: and from them those that contain moisture similar to frozen slime and powders: and of such like, and from them are the hard stone-like ones.
And in cutting all of them, and their removal there is no fear if there is no contradiction to the artery in their sectioning.
And the operation in cutting them is that you try it with the instrument, whose form comes after this, which is called intromissum, until you know what it contains.
If it contains moisture, then dry it by section along its length using a surface incision: according to this form.
And start by making an incision from line b to line g. When moisture is evacuated, then scrape off the cyst that contains this moisture, and do not leave anything inside it.
For many times it returns if something remains from it.
Then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment if it is present; and if not, in water and salt. Fill the wound with this mixture, and leave it until another day. The remaining part of the cyst corrodes itself.
Then apply Egyptian ointment to the wound again on the second and third day, as often as you need it, until you are sure that no part of the cyst remains, then treat the wound with ointment until it heals.
If an abscess contains a thick knot, then cut it according to this form, making the incision in the shape of a cross; insert forceps between the sections and scrape off the entire mass; and try your best to extract the layer containing it.
If it interferes with an artery, then do as I will tell you later.
And the same is to be done for an abscess that contains a stone, by cutting it out and treating it in the same way as described before.
The incision on an abscess containing a stone is easier because there is less blood and moisture. Sometimes there are such abscesses located on the head of certain individuals where there is no moisture inside them.
This is because I have made an incision on an abscess on the head of an old woman and found an abscess that was as hard as a stone, rough, white and unbreakable; if someone hit it with a blow it caused injury.
In other kinds of boils occurring on the head, except for boils that occur on children's heads and around the roots of ears, a section of them all should be a superficial incision.
Always make a perforation from the bottom part of them so that the flow of pus is directed towards lower parts.
Then care for it with what suits it from the healing process.
§ On the incision of goiters on the neck.
Chapter XLII.
These boils often occur on the neck and under the shoulders and groins; and sometimes they occur in other parts of the body.
And above the boils that occur on the neck, there is one and many; and they are generated one after another; and every goiter among them is within its proper tunica, as it is in nodes and boils of the head, as we have said.
The forms of these goiters are many. For they are stone-like; and some contain moisture; and there are also malicious ones that do not obey the healing process.
Therefore, when you see a good one among them, which has a good color close to the skin and moves towards all parts, and is not attached with the neck muscles, groin or artery, nor deep, it should be incised superficially from the upper part of the body to the lower part, along the line b to the line g. Peel it off from every side. Spread two layers of skin with a scalpel or several scalpels if necessary, as we have said for boils on the head, and extract it gradually.
And it is advisable not to cut an artery or nerve.
Let the scalpel not be very sharp; so as not to injure your hand during the incision or disturb the sick one, and cut what is not necessary.
If you cut a vein or artery, then stop the operation, then place in the wound alum powder or certain powders which coagulate blood, and suture the wound, and leave it, until the sharpness of the lancet subsides and the wound softens: or if it begins to rot.
Since the blood has been coagulated, return to your operation until you are finished.
Then ask with your index finger if there remains anything from the Strophulus or other small ones: if so, cut and clean them.
If there is a large vein in the root of the Strophulus: then it must not be cut from its root; instead, it should be tied with a double strong thread and left to fall out naturally without harm.
Then fill the wound with old linen that you have already soaked in Egyptian ointment. Then take care of it.
If the entire Strophulus is cut off, then it must be gathered with two pieces of wound edges: and sew it immediately, after you see that there remains no superfluity.
If you see that there remains some superfluity due to the size of the Strophulus, then it must be intended for cutting its root and pulling it out; and administer the suture as we have said.
And what contains humidity from the Strophulus, perforate it with a superficial perforation: so that you may see its maturity; and place the perforation below, as we have said.
Then administer after perforation linen with ointment and similar things, so that it corrodes what remains from the corruption, until when you see that the wound is clean; then take care of it with ointment for regenerating flesh, until it heals.
Title (Roman numeral): Chapter XLIII.
"On the section of the epiglottis due to strangulation within the throat.
"The ancients said this section was performed on the epiglottis, and I have not seen anyone in our land who has done it; this is their writing.
"However, in those with synanchema (a condition where the epiglottis is stuck to the back of the tongue), it is necessary to perform the section on the epiglottis; because there will be no help through this procedure, as all veins and lungs are weak.
"In those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, throat or both tonsils, when there is no illness in the nostril, it is necessary to use the section on the epiglottis, to prevent the loss that occurs due to strangulation.
"Therefore, when we want to perform the section on the epiglottis, it should be performed under three or four rings of the epiglottis with a small section across its width, in that area between two rings, because the section should be made at the sifac (a cartilage at the base of the epiglottis), not in the cartilage; this location is suitable for the section as it lacks flesh and blood vessels are distant from it.
"If the physician is afraid, then he should stretch the skin of the throat with a hook. "Then he shall incise the skin until he reaches the nostril; he should drain the blood vessels if he sees any.
"Then he shall perform the section on the sifac as previously mentioned; it is noted that from the mucus that comes out of the nostril, when it is ruptured, and with the loss of voice.
"And leave an open wound for some time.
"When the hour comes when strangulation is feared, bring together two lips of the wound skin and only the skin itself (without cartilage).
Then administer medications that cause flesh to grow, until it heals.
Says Albucasis. In conclusion of the story we narrated, there is no explanation unless they see that one of these abscesses has already opened in the throat of the sick man: and he was raised up above death, and desired to be cut: they go to cut the Epiglottis, so that the sick man may breathe over the place of the wound with a certain breathing and save himself from death: and for this reason they ordered to leave the wound open, until the malice of the disease is consumed, and the malice of it lasts three days, almost as if it were itself: then they therefore commanded to suture the wound, and to care for it until it heals.
And what I myself have seen is that a maidservant took a knife and sent it into her own throat, and cut a piece of the trachea of the lungs.
And I was called upon for its treatment, and found her to groan, just as is the groaning of the dead.
Therefore I uncovered the wound, and found blood which had come out from the wound to be little. So I was reassured that she herself did not cut a vein or an artery: and air was coming out from the wound.
I therefore approached the wound and cared for it until it is well: and nothing happened to the maidservant except a cough in her voice: and she returned after days to a better state of health.
Therefore I say: that there is no fear in cutting the Epiglottis.
Chapter on the section of the hernia of the throat.
Chapter XLIV.
This abscess is called hernia of the throat, it is a large abscess, according to the color of the body: and it is much more common in women.
It is according to two modes: for it is either natural or accidental.
Certainly, there is no skill in the natural.
The accidental is according to two modes; one of which is similar to fatty knots. And the other mode is like a gangrene that occurs from the knotting of an artery. There is fear there, and it should not be presumed with the iron, unless in what is small; and you prove it, and examine it with the probe. If you find it similar to a fatty knot and not suspended with some veins: then cut it, as knots are cut; and draw it out with what contains it from the cavity, if it is in the cavity; and if not, then search the whole of it. Then take care of the place with that which is needed for treatment, until it heals.
Chapter 45.
Section on the cutting of knots.
There are many kinds of knots, and I have already said all their species in division; and it is necessary that here the difference between a knot and an ulcer be explained, since there is doubt about it.
Therefore, I say that when an ulcer is heat and fever and violent pains until the effervescence of the superfluity subsides and the putrefaction is completed, then the fever and heat cease.
But a knot is not heat or fever, nor pains; and it contains them within the body cavity or a sac which is proper to them; and it is closed like a pea or a gourd, and it forms like a bulging tumor, and it is major or minor.
And there are two kinds of them: either fatty; or containing moisture. The colors of moisture are many, according to what I said in the division.
Therefore, when you arrive at the treatment of a knot, it is necessary that you examine it and inquire about it first with the instrument called Intromissum, according to its form as described in the chapter following this one.
The method of examining boils and all knots is to take this instrument and insert it into the moist place that you find in the boil; then move your fingers slowly with it until you know that the instrument has penetrated the skin. Then, lay your hand on it according to the measure of the size of the boil.
Then remove the Intromissum and observe what comes out with it.
If what comes out running is moisture of any color, then cut it off with a surface incision as I have said in the treatment of other boils.
If no running moisture comes out of the Intromissum, then know that it is fat; so cut a cross-shaped incision over it as I have told you, in this shape, just as I taught you; and peel off the skin from all sides easily; and keep a container over it if possible to extract the pus with the knot.
If the container breaks during the operation and it is not possible to extract the pus, then extract it roughly until there is no more left of it.
For if there remains a little or much, the knot returns most frequently.
If it overpowers you and there remains a little of it, then fill the wound with certain corrosive powders; bind up the wound, place hot compresses on top of it where the boil sits, and take care of it with the rest of the treatment until it is healed.
If therefore it is a large knot, then its two folds [should be] cut and care should be taken of it along with that which has grown together.
If it is a pulsating vein that is opposite to you, or not pulsating: then go near, and fill the place with soft wax, and leave it compressed for two days, or three, until the wound rots and the boiling of blood subsides: then return to cut what remains of the knot.
Chapter XLVI.
Chapter on External Instruments for Cutting and Perforating.
Of these (instruments) are the shapes of Intromissors, and there are three types.
One is large, one is medium, and one is small.
Make them from iron with square ends properly so that they can enter easily into the opening.
These are the shapes of Experientials, and they are named piercing instruments, and one of them is called Beris, which means piercing: and there are three types.
From these there is great, and middle, and small.
They meet so that they may be treated by lancing, excision, fistulas, and abscesses from the bone that is among them.
And some become rounded, smooth, blunted, like the tips of large needles which are placed on handles, namely, from jasper or brass or iron or silver.
The better ones of them are those that become from jasper.
And also experience is made from black lead which meet so that they may be tried for fistulas, the concavity of which are reflections, so that they may return with their smoothness to those reflections.
And there are again three kinds. Because from them are long ones, medium ones and short ones, according to the quantity of the width of the fistula and its narrowness.
The form of uncions (uncini), and they are of many kinds.
Because from them are simple ones, namely those with one curvature: and they are of three kinds as you see, large, medium, and small.
And from them are blind uncions (uncini): and they are of three kinds.
And from them are uncions having two curvatures, and they are of three kinds: and from them are uncions having three curvatures, and they are of three kinds: and all these are necessary in their place.
And these are the forms of knives (scalpels), which cut and scrape nodules, and abscesses: and they are of three kinds: because from them is great, middle, and small.
The ends of them that make the cut are sharp, other ends are not sharp: and they are placed thus only so as to provide help in scraping nodules near the fear of incising veins or nerves: and so that he who is ill may be cured by it, and find a little tranquility from burning which he finds during the scraping of abscesses.
They are made of copper and resemble a radio, from which alcohol is made: at the end there is a hole called Spatumilis, which can be opened to allow it to run both internally and externally as desired, as you see.
The form of Spatumili that are hidden among the fingers for the perforation of abscesses: the weak do not feel them; they come in three species, large, medium, and small.
The forms of Ventosari with which the flow of blood is cut off: they come in three species, large, medium, and small.
Make them out of copper or citron, round, slightly shorter than you see, and be delicate.
And these species of Ventosari should be large and small at your disposal, so that you can cut off blood quickly when needed, and then when there is no medicine present for you.
However, do not use them to cut off blood in every part of the body, and do not use them except in fleshy parts: such as thighs, hips, arms, breasts, abdomen, groin, and similar places, from fleshy, moist areas.
And sometimes they are made into small instruments similar to the gourd, according to their shape: with which blood is cut off when it flows from the site of phlebotomy or incision of a vein or artery; and sometimes they are round in this shape.

Chapter on the treatment of human breasts resembling female breasts.
Sometimes the breasts of some men swell during sleep (that is, when they start to become dirty while sleeping), until they resemble female breasts; and abscesses remain filthy.
Who therefore shrinks from it, it is necessary to cut across the breasts with a crescent-shaped incision, according to this shape from line 'b' to line 'g'. Then scrape off all the fat. If however the breast hangs downwards and softens due to its size, as happens in women: then it is necessary to make an incision in its two upper sides with two similar crescent-shaped cuts, of which one contains the other at their ends so that the larger encloses the smaller, according to this shape from line 'b' to line 'g'. Afterwards scrape off the skin between the two lips and remove the fat, and administer what I said about suturing and powders, which is necessary for the healing process, until it heals.

Chapter 48.
These abscesses that occur under a tumor are of the types of hard ones containing cysts and those containing moisture.

Chapter XLIX.
Chapter on the incision of boils that happens due to an Artery and a Vein.
When an artery bursts and the skin above it consolidates, it often happens that a boil forms there; similarly, this also happens with veins so that a boil and swelling occur in them.
And the signs by which it is known that a boil and swelling are due to an artery or vein are: because when a boil is due to an artery, it is long and aggregated in the depth of the body; and when you press the boil with your fingers, it feels as if there is a grating sensation.
And that which is due to a vein, is round in visible parts of the body.
And incision over this boil is an error, and especially when it is under the armpits, groins, neck, and in many parts of the body; and it is very great. Therefore, its care should be avoided with the iron, and if there are any of these also in the extremities or in the head, it should be avoided.
Therefore, over that which is due to the swelling of the artery opening, make a cut in the skin lengthwise. Then open the incision with scissors, then the artery; and release it from the tunics until it is exposed.
Then insert a pointed instrument under it and make it penetrate to the other side, and tie the artery with double thread at two places, as I taught you in extracting two arteries which are in the temples.
Then pierce the place which is between two ligaments with a lancet, until blood that is within it all comes out, and the abscess dissolves.
Then administer a cure that produces pus until the ligaments fall off: afterwards care for it with suitable ointments until it heals.
If the abscess is due to a cut vein, then it is necessary that you hold with your hand as much as possible of the abscess along with the skin from it. Then introduce a probe under the place that you held with your hand, and make it penetrate: and there should be a double thread in it, until you draw it out from the other side. Then tie the abscess with a good ligament: as I told you before, on the ligament of the vein, at two parts with two ends, with two threads.
But if you fear that the thread will be drawn out, then introduce another probe with another thread under the whole abscess near the incision: press and bind your threads in four places.
Then cut the abscess in half, until when it comes out what is within it: then cut off the excess skin, and release that which is bound from it.
Then place a poultice made of wine and oil over it. Then administer a cure with linen cloths and suitable ointments until it heals.
Chapter L.
Chapter on the abscess that happens from the twisting of nerves.
As it happens with an abscess in an Artery and Vein, similarly it happens with an abscess in Nerves: which happens to them by a blow, or happens from excessive labor, and similar causes: and it occurs most often in places of joints, or the heel, and in every place where the connections are moved: and it is a heavy abscess.
Its color is similar to the rest of the body, and it is found in several positions without pain: and when it is pressed with violence, one feels weak, similar to faintness.
And it is not an abscess gathered deep within the body, rather it is under the skin, and it moves to every part, and does not reach forward or anteriorly, nor backward to posterior areas.
Therefore, what is in the joints, should not be invaded with iron. Perhaps contraction will occur.
However, in what is in the head or forehead, puncture the skin with a lancet. If it is a small abscess, then hold it with forceps and cut it off at the root.
And if it is large, then hang it with a hook and scab it; then remove it and close the wound with stitches: care for it until it heals.
Chapter LI.
Section of abscess, which occurs in the abdomen.
Occasionally, in some men's bellies, and in their other bodies, there appear growths called Fungalia, which resemble mushrooms in nature.
Their root is subtle, and the head of them is thick, and their lips are turned inwards. And there is a small one among them, and there is one that can be enlarged greatly.
I myself have already seen a man, and in his belly there were two growths, which were more like mushrooms than other things: there was no difference between them, white, with fine roots, and their lips were turned inwards, and they festered, and moisture always flowed from them.
I then cut them and found one to weigh approximately X VIII ounces and the other about VI ounces. The operation for cutting them is as follows: consider if the patient is weak or sick, and the growth is white, moist, and fine-rooted; then cut it with a broad spatula, and have cauterization irons ready in your presence.
For often much blood is expelled during the cutting; therefore, be careful if you are overcome by blood, then cauterize it.
If you see a weak, fearful, and timid person from the cutting with iron, then take a properly made lead thread, and bind it with it; the method is as we have said, and leave it for two days.
Then add lime to the lead stringing. Therefore, do not cease to bind lead, whenever it is pressed into the growth, until it is cut off and falls away without effort.
If the growth is large-rooted, then there is some fear and dread in its cutting; particularly since it is in the belly.
It is possible to cut the middle of it. Then cauterize it, so that it does not return.
Then heal it, until the wound heals.
And beware not to cut what is of dark purple color, with few senses, foul appearance; for it is a cancerous boil; and I will come again after this, when I remember the Crab.
Chapter LII.
Chapter on the treatment of hernia of the umbilicus.
A protrusion of the umbilicus arises from various causes. It comes out either through a hernia of the scapula (what is above the abdomen) and that is called an umbilical hernia or it comes out through the intestines, according to what happens in other ruptures. It comes out either from blood flowing from a vein or an artery, as has been mentioned earlier. Or it comes out due to a constipated gas there.
If it is due to a hernia of the scapula and it protrudes like a tumor: then its color is similar to that of an abscess or body and it is soft, without pain: and it appears in various positions. And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestines, then its position, as we have said, is of a more violent diversity. Therefore, when you press it with your fingers, it is hidden; then it returns and possibly there is a sound; and it swells greatly at the entrance of the bath and causes severe pain.
If however it is due to moisture, it is soft; then when you press it with your hand, it does not hide and it is not compressed nor does it increase in size.
If it is due to blood, then with these signs appears an abscess that turns black at the root.
If it is due to flesh born (caused): then it is a heavy, large, hard abscess and it festers according to its size.
But if it is due to gas, then when touched, it is soft.
The procedure for this is to consider whether the protrusion of the umbilicus is due to blood from an artery or vein or gas; then it is necessary to prevent its treatment. For there is fear and dread, as I have taught you in the chapter where I said that abscesses due to an artery or vein are dangerous.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to an intestine or hernia: then it is necessary that you command the sick one, so that he holds his breath and stands extended and still. Then mark [the area] with hot wax around the entire navel. Then command him to lie down on his back under your hands. Then encircle with a broad bandage around the navel over the place you marked with hot wax. Then extend the middle of the incision upwards with a large spoon. Then bind him around firmly with thread or with silk cord: and the knot of the ligature should be a square knot.
Then open the extended incision above the ligature. If you then find it [the hernia] already caught by the ligature: then extract the hernia sac, and insert your index finger into it, and push the intestine towards the interior of the abdomen: and if you find a hernia, then take it with the spoon, and cut off the excess.
If however it is an artery or vein [affected]: then bind it much. Then return to your operation. And take two needles and insert into them two strong threads: and insert the two needles into the circle you made around the abscess in the shape of a cross, which you make to penetrate.
Then tie the abscess in four places on the needles: and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the place until the rotten flesh extends: and falls by itself; or cut it when it becomes soft and rots.
Then care for him with what is necessary from ointments until he is healed.
If the protrusion of the navel is from a soft flesh or moisture in him: then hollow out the abscess as we have said. You shall draw out blood or moisture that you find in it.
Then take care of it with what solidifies the place.
Chapter LIII.
Chapter on treating Cancers.
We have already stated in the division of Cancer's species and the way to treat it with medicines: and beware when treating it with iron, lest it ulcerate. We also said that cancer is generated in the matrix, and warned against cauterizing its treatment.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer is at a place where it can be eradicated. Such as cancer that is in the breasts or hips and similar limbs, which are to be extracted entirely when possible: especially when it is beginning small.
But when it becomes ancient and large, one should not approach it.
For I was unable to heal anyone from it; nor have I seen anyone before me who achieved that.
And the operation on it, when it is placed as we said, is to precede and dissolve a patient from black cholera several times. Then, if you find phlebotomy itself with obvious fullness.
Then prepare the patient with a preparation in which the operation takes place.
Then throw hooks that fit into the cancer. Afterward hollow out the cancer from every side with skin, as examined, until nothing remains of its roots; and let blood flow, but do not cut it quickly, rather press the areas, and remove all thick blood with your hand or if possible there with tools.
If however the flow of thick blood from an incision of the artery or vein opposes you; then cauterize the vein until the blood is cut off. Then care for it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
[Section on the Cure of Hydropsis]
Chapter LIV. We now discuss the division of hydropisis species and how water accumulates; and the signs for each species and its treatment along with medications.
And that which is cured with iron is not but the asclitis species alone; it does not approach iron for the timpanitis species; nor deeply for the hyposarca species, since it is lethal.
When you have already been treated for this hydropisis species of timpanitis with medications and the treatment did not work; then consider. For if the patient has already become weakened or there is another illness besides hydropisis; such as if there is coughing or looseness of the bowels, and similar cases; then beware not to treat him with iron because it is dangerous.
But if you see the patient overflowing with strength and no other illness besides hydropisis; and he is neither a child nor an old man; then there is room for operation on him, that you lift up the weakened person standing between your hands, and afterward, the attendant presses his abdomen with his hand to force water downward toward the lower part of the breast.
Then take a thorny spoon in this shape: Let it be of two sharp parts, long, and sharp-pointed at the end like a spoon. However, there should be something short in it to prevent you from passing through with it during the operation as far as the intestine and damaging it.
Then consider. For if hydropisis generation is from the intestines, then it is necessary to extend with a section from the navel a length of three fingers downward directly above the breast.
But if hydropisis generation is due to liver illness; then make the section on the left side from the navel a length of three fingers.
And if its generation is due to the spleen, then let there be a section on the right side: and it is not necessary that there should also be a section on the side towards which the sick person wishes to lie, so that superfluities do not flow to that weak place.
Then perforate the entire skin with an instrument. Then insert your hand into that section, and scoop it up with a spatula between the skin, and scoop out, as if you are peeling it; let the quantity scraped off be the size of a fingernail or about that.
Then pierce the spatula until the spatula reaches an empty place: and that is where the water is. Then extract it, and insert the instrument into the opening, which has this form. And it resembles a cannula: it is made of silver, or copper, or brass, linen, cleaned; on the lower part of it there is a small opening, and on its sides there are three openings, two on one side, and one on the other; and the tip of it is slit, according to the way of cutting a reed, as you see: at the upper end of it there is a band.
For when the instrument reaches the water, then it immediately descends upon the instrument; therefore let out a moderate amount of water by the hour.
For if you let out more than is needed from it, perhaps the sick person will die by resolution of his vital spirit; or a syncope occurs which approaches death.
However, let out from it according to its potency, and according to the signs given to you by the pulse of the sick person, and the quality of his condition.
Then remove the instrument, and retain the water.
That is because it is retained immediately due to the skin which holds the opening that is on the spatula; about which I told you to pierce it in that way.
Then repeat the instrument on the second day, if you see the patient able to bear it; and also remove a small amount from water.
Probe it for a few days without fear, and be careful to avoid error; until there remains only a little in the water.
If you fear for the patient and let out much water; then care for him with warm sand, many sweating in a bath and sun, and wait for his thirst; and care for him with most drying medicines, until he is cured; and cauterize over the stomach, spleen, and liver, after removing the water; as I told you in what preceded.
Chapter on the care of infants born in places where their urinary tracts are not pierced.
Chapter 50.
When anyone of the infants comes out of his mother's womb, and the head is not pierced by a lamb's forceps, or the opening is narrowed, or it is not in its proper place.
Therefore, help him by immediately piercing with a thin spatula such as Spatumili.
Then place a thin nail made from lead into the wound and tie it; and hold it for three or four days.
When he wishes to urinate, remove it and mix [something] with it. Then bring it back.
And if you do not place lead, it is now possible that the urine which flows upon the area does not allow the wound to close.
But if his wound is narrowed, he is treated with lead as we have said, for many days until it is enlarged.
But those in whom the wound is not in its proper place are harmed. This is because the wound is at the end of the spine of the one who is born; therefore, he cannot mix it with urine towards the front until he raises the spine with his hand to the upper parts. Nor is there generation in him, because the semen cannot reach the womb according to the correct direction; and it is a very foul illness.
The method of operation in him is that he lies down sick on his back. Then extend the spine of his head with your left hand with a strong stretch, and cut off the head of the spine from the location of the glans, with a pointed or sharp spoon-like instrument; like cutting a reed, or as you radish something, so that the middle comes out similar to the head of the spine: and so that the wound falls in the middle according to what is necessary.
And beware of yourself during your operation from bleeding. It often happens that this occurs. Therefore oppose him with what causes the bleeding and care for the wound until it heals.

Because, in cleansing with a new scalpel, the skin often escapes. Chapter LVIII.
On the extraction of a retained bladder stone.
Retention of urine in the bladder, occurs from a blockage made from stone, or frozen blood, or pus, or flesh born, and similar things from what we have said in modes of treatment, in division.
If the urine does not flow and you see that its retention is due to a stone which is already in the neck of the bladder: then it is necessary that he who is ill be laid low on his knees. Then his feet should be placed upon his back, and he should stretch out his belly from the upper part of his back, and he should contract his breath as much as possible for him. Therefore, when the neck of the bladder is compressed to expel the stone, the urine flows out.
If it does not flow as we have said and a severe situation is over the ill person: then it is necessary to administer extraction of it with an instrument which is called syringe, whose form is like this: It should be made from silver, and be fine, soft, concave like the reed pen of a bird in fineness, long like the palm of one hand and a half: let there be a fine cannula at its tip.
And the method of urine outflow through it is, that you take a double thread and tie a wool or cloth, or good ligature at its end: and insert the end of the thread into the lower part of the syringe: and cut with scissors if there is too much from the wool, but introduce into the cannula with force, like pulling.
Then anoint the syringe with oil, or with butter and egg white: and make him sit on a chair, and warm the bladder, and his own member with moist oils, and olive oil, and warm water.
Then introduce the syringe into the vein with ease, until it reaches the root of the vein.
Then fold it over at the upper part of the navel.
Then push the syringe into it until it reaches the bladder and feels it weak as it enters the empty space: this is not done according to this order unless because the pathway where it goes has a tortuousness.
Then gradually extend the thread with wool. The vein follows the wool.
Then draw it out, and let the vein run through the way of urine: and continue to do this, without stopping, until the bladder is emptied, and the weak relief is found.
