Chapter 60.
§ On the Extraction of a Stone.
We have said about the types of stones, their treatment with medicines, and the difference between a stone generated in kidneys, bladder, and urinary tract, and its signs; we have also mentioned the operation on the stone with hand or section: this is properly a stone in the bladder; it is the one that hardens in the rod; I am telling you about this with clear explanation and abbreviation.
Therefore, I say that a stone generated in the bladder most often occurs in children.
And among its signs is that urine comes out from the bladder like water in its fineness; and there appears in it white sand, and the sick one rubs his rod, and labors with it, and often hangs down. Then it is erected, and exits with it in many of them.
And the healing of children is easy until they reach fourteen years. It is difficult in the elderly. In young people it is moderate, since it is between that which heals quickly and that which requires a longer time to heal. However, in the one whose stone is larger, the cure is easier; but if the stone is small, the cure is more difficult for that one.
When we reach the cure, it is first necessary to clean the sick person with an enema, which extracts all feces that are within their intestines; for it sometimes prevents the discovery of the Stone during investigation.
Then let the sick person be taken with their feet, shaken and moved towards the lower parts; so that the Stone may descend into the deep bladder or rise from a high place several times.
Then let him sit between your hands, and his hands be beneath his buttocks; so that the bladder is entirely relaxed towards the lower parts.
Then examine him, and touch him externally.
If you therefore feel the Stone in a space, then immediately approach with section over it.
If it does not fall with your touch at all, then you must anoint the index finger with oil of the left hand if the sick person is a child; or the middle finger if he is an adult full-grown; and insert it into his anus; and search for the Stone until it is beneath your finger; and turn it slowly towards the neck of the bladder.
Then press upon it with your finger and push it outwards against the place of the incision; and command the attendant to press the bladder with his hand; and command another attendant, to lift the testicles with his right hand towards the upper parts; and with his left hand, to remove the skin that is under the testicles in the part where the incision is.
Then insert a probe cutting, whose form is as follows. Find within him what is between the anus and the testicles, not in the middle, to the side of the left: and let the section be made above the stone, and your finger be in the anus: and let the section be transverse, so that it is a broad section externally and narrow internally, according to the quantity in which the exit of the stone from there is not larger.
Perhaps the finger compresses the stone that is within the anus at the incision point and exits easily.
And know, that from the stone are those angles and margins, wherefore its exit is difficult on account of this.
And it is soft, similar to a gland, and round; and its exit will be easy.
To that which has angles and margins, add in the incision.
If it does not exit in this manner, then it is necessary to fissure above it; or to tighten upon it with a device whose tip is like the moon that tightens on the stone and does not slip away from it; or to introduce below it an instrument with a curved tip.
If you cannot do this, then widen the opening slightly. If something prevents you from doing it with blood, cut it off with a lancet.
If the stone is larger than one, then push first and foremost on the bladder bone. Then cut upon it. Then push a little after this; and do likewise if there are more than two.
If it is very large, then it is ignorance to cut above it with a great incision. Because it happens to the sick one of two things, either death or continuous flow of urine; therefore, because the place is not consolidated at all.
But administer its expulsion until it exits; or fissure its fracture with forceps, until you extract it piece by piece.
When you have completed your operation, then fill the wound with tar, aloe, and dragon's blood; tie it up, and place upon it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or rose oil, and cold water; to let it sit and heal the hot abscess.
Then turn the sick one on his neck, and do not undo the bandage, until the third day. When you undo it (the bandage), apply balm to the place with much water and oil.
Then care for him with dyafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until he is healed.
If a hot abscess or ulcerous eruption arises in the wound, and it becomes corrosive, as if blood congeals in the bladder and urine is prevented from passing: this is known to be when blood comes out with urine. Insert your finger into the wound, and draw out that blood. For if it remains, it encourages decay of the bladder and its rotting.
Then clean the wound with vinegar, water, and salt; and apply to it all kinds of things that agree with healing until it is healed.
And it is necessary during the entire healing period to bind two thighs together and apply, because of the medicine placed on the site.
If the stone is small and it is in the neck of the bladder and it obstructs the passage of urine, then care for him with what I have said before you reach the incision. For many times you are excused from this treatment during the incision, now I have proved that.
And you should take a perforator made of iron, its shape is triangular, sharp and fixed to wood.
Then take a thread and tie it to a rod under a stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
Insert the piercing iron into the rod easily, until it reaches the point of the stone; and you turn the piercing iron with your hand in the stone gradually; and compress the piercing to make it penetrate from the other side.
The urine is discharged immediately.
Then press your hand on what remains of the stone from the outside part of the rod. It is broken and comes out with the urine, and heals the sick man.
If this treatment is not prepared for you because of something that prevents it from being done; then tie a thread under the stone, and another thread above the stone. Then cut the rod over the stone between two bindings. Then remove it (the piercing iron or stone). Afterwards untie the knot and clean off the frozen blood that forms in the wound.
And the knot of thread under the stone is not necessary unless it prevents the return to the bladder; and another knot above, unless when the string is untied after the removal of the stone, the skin returns to its place and covers the wound; and this requires you to raise the skin over when you tie the upper string so that it returns to the incision and covers the wound as we have said.
Chapter LXI (61).
Chapter on the removal of stones in women.
Not much stone is generated in women.
If a stone happens to one of them (women), then the treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden because of the numerous procedures involved.
One of them may be that she is a virgin.
And the second reason is that you do not find a woman who will expose herself to the doctor when she is a virgin or married women.
Thirdly, because you do not find a woman well versed in this art, especially in surgical operations with the hand.
And fourthly, distance from the place of the stone: for it requires deep incision, and this entails fear.
If necessity calls for it, then one must take a woman physician who is well versed in this: but this is seldom found.
But if that is not available, then seek a chaste and skilled physician and a present midwife who is well-learned in women's matters or a woman familiar with this art: make her present and particularly instruct her to do everything you command regarding the stone.
Firstly, that if she is a virgin, then one must look to see if there is a finger that can be inserted into her anus and search for the stone.
If it is found, then twist it with the finger and then instruct the midwife to insert her finger into the weak vagina and search for the stone after she has placed her left hand on the bladder and press it firmly.
If the stone is found, then one must gradually move it from the bladder opening towards the lower parts with all one's strength until it reaches the root of the hip.
Then, it is to be cut on the side of the half vagina near the root of the hip from any part that is prepared for it, and one feels the stone in that place: the finger should not be removed from the stone while twisting it under it; and the incision should be small initially. Then insert a probe over that cut.
Then insert a probe over that cut. If it feels the stone, then add to the cut according to the proportionate quantity as the stone comes out from there.
And know that the appearances of stones are many. From this it is small and large, smooth and rough, long and round having branches.
Know therefore its appearance, so that it may be shown to you regarding the thing which you wish.
If blood conquers you, then add at its place zege tritum and hold it for one hour until the blood is cut off.
Then return to your operation until the stone comes out: and do, so that you prepare yourself with the instruments, which I said for the removal of stones in men, to help you in your operation.
If blood conquers you and you know that the expulsion of blood is from an artery which is cut: then put powder over it and tighten it with thread suitable for ligation; and do not move it; and leave the stone and do not pull it out. Perhaps a weak woman may die. Then care for the wound.
When the sharpness of blood subsides after days and the place becomes putrid, then return to your operation until the stone comes out.
Chapter 62.
[Title: On the Section of a Watery Hernia.]
A watery hernia is not anything other than a gathering of moisture under the white membrane that contains the testicle: and it is called a sifac.
And at times it is in its own panniculus which nature has prepared for it in the part of the scrotum until it is considered as another egg, and it is between the white membrane of the testicle that we mentioned: and this does not happen often.
And indeed, the generation of this [abscess] in branches is due to weakness that occurs in testicles: therefore, this matter flows towards them. And sometimes it happens as a result of striking upon the testicles.
This moisture has many colors. Or it is of this moisture, which tends towards a citron-like yellow color, or red like blood, or foul like feces, or black, or watery white, and that is the most common one.
And signs by which it is known where there is an accumulation of water, are these. For if it is in the scrotum, which I have said, then the abscess is round and shorter than the figure of an owl; and the testicle is not apparent because moisture keeps it from every side.
And if the moisture is within its own bag [scrotum], then the abscess is round like part of an owl, and therefore a man will burst because it is another egg.
And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the scrotum [bag], then it falls down.
When one desires to know the color of the moisture, then test the color of the moisture on an abscess with a square probe, whose form has preceded. According to that which comes out in the track of the probe, judge about what is between it [the moisture and the probe].
Since we come to the cure with iron [lancet], then it is necessary that you first order the weak one to be bled if possible for him, and observe his body to be full.
Then he lies on his back on a low bed, and puts many cloths beneath him.
Then you sit on the left side of him, and command the servant to sit at his right, who stretches out his stick [lancet] to one side of two layers of skin of the testicles, and to the region of the groin [of the abdomen].
Then take a broad spatula, and cut the scrotal skin in the middle along its length, almost up to the ridge: and make the incision according to a straight line equidistant from the one that divides the scrotal skin, until you reach the white layer enclosing it: and scrape it off and observe it, or take care not to cut it off: and let your scraping be on the part that hangs down more with the egg: and scrutinize with subtlety according to the quantity, as much as possible.
Perform a wide opening of the spermatic sac with water, and drain out all the water.
Then separate the two lips of the incision with scissors and stretch the spermatic sac upward, without touching the skin enclosing the testicles: and cut the spermatic sac however it is possible for you to cut it, either entirely or partially, but especially the subtle side of it. For if you do not carefully examine, there is no certainty that water will not return through the incision.
If, however, an egg appears outside its sheath during your operation: then when you complete the incision of the spermatic sac, bring it back. Then attach the two lips of the scrotal skin with stitches.
Then treat it as other wounds until it heals.
If you find a rotten egg stained with blackness, then it is necessary to bind the vessels that support it, fearing bleeding.
Then remove the testicle with its supporting structure and drain the egg: afterwards treat it as I said.
If, however, water is gathered in two parts, then you will know that there are two branches: so cut the other part as you did with the other.
And if it appears to you that the operation should be one, then do it: afterwards cleanse the blood. And insert a linen thread immersed in oil or in rose oil inside the incision; and place an additional linen thread that you have soaked in wine and oil on its outside and expand it over both testicles, and search for the bowel opening; and place double cloths on top, they are poultices; and tie them up above with a ligament having six knots.

And sometimes this branch is artificially healed with cautery at the incision site using iron; it is to take a small, sharp cauterizing knife and cut the skin of the testicles; it is lit, as we have described; until the white sifac containing water is exposed; then take the cautery in this manner.
It is similar to the Greek letter.
Then pierce it with that and set it alight until all moisture comes out.
Then pull the sifac with tweezers and scorify it with a sharp heated cautery, cutting as much of it as possible until you have removed the entire thing.
And be careful not to let the fire touch it (the wound).
And know that this operation is safer, more distant from bleeding, and better than the operation with incision.
If the opposite happens to you during the hour of incision or cauterization, if an abscess forms, bleeding occurs, or something else; then it is necessary to treat what opposes you with the appropriate cure, as previously mentioned.
If the patient is timid and does not await this operation due to its horror, then administer perforation according to what I have told you, and it is.
When it is informed to you by what we have said about meanings that the branch is watery, then it must be done that the patient sits on an elevated seat.

On the treatment of Intestinal Worms.
The course (of treatment) for intestinal worms occurs from an incision that happens when the sifach of the abdomen is extended over the lower abdomen near the flank of the abdomen.
Why do the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles. And this rupture is either from the hernia or its extension.
And these two types (of rupture) happen for many reasons: either from a blow, or from jumping, or shouting, or lifting a heavy object and similar things.
And a sign that it is from the extension of the hernia. It occurs gradually over a long period of time and does not happen suddenly; it is an abscess that is turned around deep within; for this reason, because the hernia compresses the intestine.
And a sign of it when it is from the hernia incision, because it causes intense pain suddenly from its beginning; and it is an abscess different, appearing under the skin near; and that is because of the exit of the intestine, and the course of it to the outside of the hernia.
And sometimes it comes out with a worm (zirbum); and this is called the intestinal worm (Ramex intestinalis) and worm (zirbia); and sometimes it happens with diarrhea.
And sometimes it runs into the intestine with feces and remains there; and that is with danger for the sick, because it causes pain to worsen, especially when it is compressed.
And in the treatment of the types of this disease with iron there is fear; therefore one must be careful with the risks in it.
And the method of operation is to command the sick person to push his intestine back into the hollow with his hand if he obeys the return. Then he lies down on his neck upon your hands; and lift up his legs.
Extend the skin that follows the skin upward and cut the entire skin of the scrotum in length. Then bind the hooks of the incision to two lips of the incision, according as you need to open the incision with them; and the cut shall be according to the quantity, as much as is possible, so that the egg may come out from it.
Then scrape the sheep's-wool sac, and what is beneath the skin of the scrotum, until the white membrane of the sheep's-wool sac becomes hard from all parts; then insert your thumb into that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white membrane of the sheep's-wool sac, and between the folds, and without the adhesion which is on the back part of the egg.
Then with the right hand move towards the inner skin of the testicles; and with this stretch the white membrane of the sheep's-wool sac upwards with the left hand; and lift the egg from the sheep's-wool sac to the part of the incision, and command the attendant to stretch the egg upwards; and you dissolve the adhesion which is on the back part of the egg after the complete solution.
And search with your fingers whether there is nothing there from the intestine rolled up in the hard white sheep's-wool sac. If you find something of that, then push it down into the lower belly.
Then take the probe, in which is a thick thread, made of linen from ten threads; and insert it at the last part of the sheep's-wool sac, that is, the membrane, which follows the skin of the testicles after the incision; then cut the ends which project from the thread, until there are four threads. Then prepare something of them on top of something with a shape that is in the manner of a cross; and tie the egg-white membrane (alshifa), which we spoke of, because it is a strong ligament under the skin of the testicles, until no mucus, which nourishes them, can send anything to them; so that a hot abscess does not occur there. Place again the ligament second beyond the first ligament, distant from it by less than two fingers. After these two ligaments, let go of the sifach which is under the skin of the testicles, to the size of a finger; and cut the rest all around, and remove the egg from it.
Then, cut on the lower part of the skin of the testicles with a section where blood and pus run; as we said in what was mentioned before.
Then administer wool soaked in oil and place it in the wound; and administer the ligament as we said before. And sometimes burn the white sifach as was said, after its incision, fearing a flow of blood. For this often happens. Let go of the ligament until it falls by itself.
If the case delays, then boil with hot water; and place on top of it what was said before, until it falls by itself.
Then, care for the wound with the rest of the treatment for wounds, until healed.
Chapter LXVI.
Chapter on Windy Nose (Rhinorrhea).
In this windy nose, I have not seen anyone who dared to cure it with iron.
And first they said that it happens as was said in the windy nose that is with worms (infestation). That is to tie vessels after section above it with ease; then cut in the middle and care for later with what opens it itself, until the vessels fall out; and take care of the wound as we said before, until it heals.
Chapter LXVII.
Chapter on Disruptions that occur in the groins.
When there is a rupture in the groins as we said, and a place empties out, and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles; and if it descends, it is too little, and it returns in every hour; but if this condition continues with that time, a fissure is added to the sifach (epididymis), until the intestines descend into the sifach.
And it happens from the extension of sifach, which is in inguinibus, as we said. That is, because sifach extends: then it softens, and the place is opened, and it drains.
And its care is with cautionery, as its narrative preceded.
And at times it is cured with iron, according to this manner: and it is that the weak one lies on his back upon your hands. Then cut the place of the rupture and draining, cutting along the width, according to the quantity of three fingers.
Then tie down the alsihafak and what are under the skin, until the white sifach is exposed, which is below the skin following it.
Then take a probe and put it upon the draining from sifach, and press it to the depth of the abdomen.
Then two draining points are raised on the end of the radius from sifach, and tie them together with a stitch; then extract the end of the radius.
And do not cut the alsihafak at all, nor touch an egg, nor anything else, as I told you in the treatment of the intestines' branches.
Then care for it with the wound healing method. And when you make a cut, clean it, and restore the wound, until it hardens.
For sifach contracts and no additional draining is added to the rupture.
And cautionery is better in this place, because it is closer to salvation.
Chapter LXVIII.
Chapter on the softening of the scrotum skin.
The scrotum skin is frequently softened in some men, because the flesh between it becomes soft and its appearance is foul.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who is asked to treat him, that he makes the sick person lie down on his back, and cuts through the entire softened skin over the natural skin.
Then gather the two lips together with stitching: and if you wish, or first of all remove the excess softened skin with three or four stitches, and a firm stitch.
Then cut between the stitches.
Then take care of the treatment of the remaining wounds until they heal and the threads fall out.
Chapter LXIX.
[Section Title: Castration]
Know that castration is excommunicated in our law: and therefore it would be permissible for me not to remember it in my book: and its remembrance is not necessary, unless because of two methods.
One reason is that it should be in the knowledge of a physician when he is asked about it: and so that he may know the cure for him to whom it happens.
And the other reason is that we often need castration of some animals for our benefit through it, such as rams, gazelles, and cats, and similar ones among animals.
Therefore I say that castration is done according to two methods. Or by attrition. Or by a cut and section.
In that which is done by attrition, the method of operation is this: we make the animal sit in warm water until his testicles become softened and relaxed, and hang down: then rub them with your hand until they dissolve and are not noticeable under touch.
In castration by cut and section, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press the skin of his testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensorium, and cut through everything with one cut until when two eggs come out: then cut each after you have scoured it, and do not leave anything on them except sifak for the subtle part that is over the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than that by attrition because attrition may leave something from the testicles, which makes the animal desire copulation.
Then heal the wound until it heals.
Chapter 70.
[Section Title] On the care of hermaphrodites in two methods.
Hermaphroditus is from men according to two modes. One of them is that there appears in it the space following (?), or in the skin of the testicles, in what is between two testicles, a figure like that of a female womb, in which hairs are present: and sometimes urine flows out of that which is in the skin of the testicles.
In women there is one species, and it is a female womb above the comb (?), like the small testicles of a man, protruding to the exterior: one of them is like the prick of a man, and two like two testicles.
And the treatment of three species, two from men, and one from women, is: because it is necessary to cut the flesh added, until the impression escapes. Then treat them with the treatment of other wounds.
In the second species of men, from which urine flows out (?), which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor any treatment at all.
Chapter LXXI.
Chapter on the incision of tentigo and protruding flesh in women's ulcers.
A tentigo may be added on a natural matter, until it becomes filthy and ugly to look at; and sometimes it is magnified in certain women so much that it expands like in men, and reaches the point of intercourse.
Therefore, it is necessary to hold the excess of tentigo with the hand or with a hook, and to cut; and not at the end of the cutting, especially in the deep roots, so that there is no bleeding.
Then treat it with the treatment of wounds, until it heals.
The flesh that arises is the flesh that is born in the opening of the womb, until it fills itself; and perhaps it comes out to the outside like a tail, and because of this some people call the illness 'tailless'. Therefore, we should cut it as we would cut a tumor, and heal it until it is healed.
On the treatment of an unperforated female breast lump.
Chapter LXXII.
The vagina should be whole, not perforated, or have a small hole. It is either natural or accidental.
The accidental [condition] is that which precedes the illness; it itself arises either from added flesh, or thin tissue, or fat; and it occurs either in the depth of the womb, or in its sides, or on its surface, either upper or lower; and it prohibits coitus and conception, and parturition, and possibly menstruation.
And the knowledge of this [condition] is obtained through the examination by an obstetrician, if the membrane rupture is nearby apparent.
If it is not visible, then seek it with your fingers, or with a rod.
If the membrane rupture is from thin tissue and is near to two lips, then expel it, and tear it apart.
And place a piece of wool on top of the two lips.
Then place your fingers of both hands simultaneously, and let the woman lie down on her back with her legs spread open. Then stretch the two lips forcefully, until the thin tissue is torn apart and the membrane rupture is opened.
Then take linen, and soak it in oil, and place it on the spot; let the woman anoint this place every day to prevent the area from hardening with a scab.
If the thin tissue is thick and fatty, then it must be cut with a broad sharp-edged leaf of myrtle.
If the membrane rupture is from born flesh, then suspend it with hooks and cut it; have medicines with you which stop bleeding without causing pain, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and pitch mixed with sheep's milk fat.
Then administer a wide cannula made of lead to prevent the wound from hardening quickly; hold it for some days; then administer dried flaxseed, and then treat the rest with the usual treatment until it heals.
And sometimes is born in the matrix a birth of fleshes of another kind: it is therefore necessary that they are cut according to this manner: while it is not an apostema cancerous, for an apostema cancerous which is in the matrix, there should be no opposition with iron altogether.
Chapter LXXIII.
About the care of hemorrhoids, Athehelil and Bothor regarding red ones in women's veins.
Hemorrhoids indeed are an opening of veins' orifices, until much blood continuously flows out from them.
When hemorrhoids become chronic, they become thrombosed: and I have already said about their species and signs in the division of them; and here I will say what among them receives treatment, and what does not.
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the matrix and do not appear to the senses, then there is no treatment with iron for them.
But those among them which are on the opening of the matrix above which sensation falls, are those that can be treated.
It is therefore necessary to introduce a woman into a cold house. Then extend Athehelil with forceps or with rough cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then sprinkle powder over them near the flow of blood from one of the incisions without biting: such as ashes of incense, dragon's blood, thistle, and similar ones.
Then push his feet to the wall at hour one. Afterwards place her in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumach, and bark of pomegranates, and gallnuts, and similar ones.
Then take barley flour, and knead it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it over his back.
If blood is cut with it, good; and if not, make adhesive ointments (to stick) to the back (wound) of blisters, and nipples, without incision.
Then take wool and immerse it in the juice of tarathith, or the juice of arnoglosso, or the juice of branches of alaulat (aglanter), that is, fig tree leaves, Pontic wine, and make it sticky with beeswax.
When the abscess remains quiet, then take care of the place with ointments until it heals.
Albath is red and resembles al-hassa heads, and has a rough appearance.
Therefore it is necessary to cut what appears from it (the Albath), as I said earlier on the thighs equally; and take care of it until it heals.
Chapter LXXIV.
Chapter on Perforation of the Exitura that occurs in the womb (uterus).
In the womb (uterus) many kinds of abscesses occur, such as cancer, stone-like abscesses, sores, adubelas, alekilas (herpes), fistulas, hemorrhoids, ragadias, thelils, and hot abscesses.
And indeed I have already said all these diseases and their forms, and the signs of them, and their cures, divided; it is necessary that I say in this treatise about the hot abscess that occurs in the matrix, when it is one of the abscesses which collect pus, and you wish to know how its opening with iron is made.
Therefore, consider. If the pain of the abscess at its beginning is sharp with striking and flame, and fever; and you see it redden upon it; if pressure is applied to it, then do not perforate it; and treat it in that way which helps for maturation, until when quietness comes to the acuteness of the afflictions.
Then it is necessary that you make the woman sit on a chair with two armrests, and she reclines or lies on her back, and places her feet at the lower part of the belly; and let her hips be spread, and she puts her arms under her thighs, and ties both with a bandage fitting to it.
Then the midwife sits on the right side, and administers the tool for opening the womb's opening.
And it is necessary when you wish to administer this tool, that you perforate with the point of a deep probe the womb of the woman, so that what enters from the tool is not deeper than the womb, and does not harm the weak.
If the tool is too deep, then it is necessary that you place powder on top of the deep part of the womb; to prevent the entry of the whole tool into the depth of the womb; and it is necessary that you place a weight, which runs in the tool, on the upper side; and that you hold the tool, and turn the weight, until the deep part of the womb is opened.
When it appears to be excised and is touched with the hand and it is soft and yielding, then it is necessary to cut off that [thing] near its head with a broad lance.
When the pus is drained, then it is necessary to place a linen cloth soaked in rose oil or green oil that contains some resin on the wound: and lay the linen cloth, and draw out the incision deeply into the matrix.
Place [something] externally on the matrix and on the bone a clean wool cloth soaked in water in which wormwood has been boiled.
Then it shall be treated two days later with an ointment suitable for that, until it heals.
And sometimes the matrix and wound is washed so that it is cleansed with water and honey: then with water in which the root of the lily or Aristolochia longa has been boiled: then return to the ointment.
If the wound is hidden inside the matrix, then it is necessary to prohibit its treatment with iron: instead, treat it as I have said in the division [section].
Chapter LXXXVI (86).
Chapter on obstetrics, how to treat living fetuses that have left their normal position.
It is necessary for the obstetrician to know first the shape of a natural delivery.
Therefore, the signs of this [delivery] are as follows: when you see a woman pressing downward and desiring to smell air, and you apply pressure on her in the place of delivery, and she hastens the exit of the fetus: then know that this delivery is in its natural form, and it is an exit over the head of the fetus, and the second one with it: or suspended, or hanging from the navel.
When you see these signs, then it is necessary to press on her abdomen so that the fetus descends quickly.
When it [the surgical instrument] descends upon his head, it [the secondary one] also descends with it, and it should be purified from those superfluities by good cleansing.
However, that which is beyond this parturition, is unnatural, inadmissible.
For sometimes the fetus emerges with its feet first, and its body emerges before its head, and its feet, and one of its hands; or it emerges with its head and one hand; or it emerges with the umbilical cord, and perhaps it turns on its neck, and similar unadmissible figures.
Therefore, it is necessary for the obstetrician to be prudent, subtle in these matters, and to avoid error and deception; and I am showing all the figures from these, and how to understand them, and they are indicated by that, and they stand upon him.
When the fetus emerges with its head in its natural passage and it becomes difficult for him on the woman, and labor is strong, and you see his strength already weakened; then let her sit on a chair or women hold her; and let her drink warm water with fennel cooked in it, and with moist oils.
Then the obstetrician introduces a small spatula-like instrument between his fingers, and he finds with it the secondary one, and cuts it with his nail until what is in her from moisture runs out; and presses the woman's womb, until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then she must be cleansed with fennel mucilage, with oil of sesame.
Then command her after cleansing to be pressed; and make her sneeze with snuff, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour. The fetus shall immediately exit.
If two hands come out first from the fetus, then it is necessary to draw them back gently. If it does not obey in entering (the birth canal), then place the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up; then strike the chair upon the ground; and hold the woman so that she does not fall during the shock.
If the hands do not come out and the fetus dies, then cut them (the hands) off and take out the remaining fetus; bind its hand with cloth and take it out equally, for it will come out by itself.
The emergence of the embryo is on his feet. When the fetus emerges on his feet, then you should push them up; then turn the fetus gradually; afterwards straighten it equally.
Then take one of its feet and stretch it gradually.
When they (the legs) emerge up to the hips, then command him (the woman) to push and make her sneeze with a pinch; for it will come out if God wills.
And if it does not come out as we have said, then push the fetus back gently until you position it according to its natural form. For then it will come out easily with an easy delivery.
If it is forbidden as we have said (to perform the procedure), then take from althea mucilage, sesame oil and dissolved gum; grind it well in a mortar with good pounding; then anoint the woman's womb and below her belly with it. Then make her sit in warm water until she feels relief (from pain).
When you see that the lower parts of hers have become warm, then give her something made from myrrh and make her lie down. When then it holds an hour, then make her sit on a chair. Then make her sneeze: and bind her mouth and nose: and press the lower part of her abdomen with easy pressure. For feces will come out immediately.
Delivery over knees and hands. When it exits in this manner, then insert your hand gradually. Then the woman lies on her back, and let her feet hang downwards; and she lies down on the bed, and clasps her hands. Then press gently over her abdomen. Then take out what is under her feet from the pouches until it is prepared below. If the fetus does not come out, then take hold of her feet and move them with great movement. Then press gently what is above the pubis until the fetus rises to higher parts. Then insert your hand and press the fetus gradually; and tell the woman to hold her breath until the fetus is delivered.
Delivery of the fetus, hanging down broadly from the hands. Insert your hand in reducing her hand. If it cannot be reduced, then lift the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then let her lie down on the bed; and strike her legs with strong blows.
Then administer the ointment you have prepared from mucilages.
If she receives her delivery, then make her sit on a chair. Then strive to reduce the hand, and press the fetus according to its natural shape; and make her sneeze, and tell her to hold her breath until it is delivered.
Delivery of the fetus on its back, with spread hands, and its face to the mother's back. The obstetrician must hold the fetus and then turn it gradually with ease.
When it is evened [turned], then place upon its mouth as we have said from oil and mucilages.
Then command him to move slowly. When you have done that, then make her sit on a chair, and command her to lean towards the right side. Then command him to compress [the baby] and make her sneeze with powder.
The delivery of the fetus is prepared on the left side. When it descends to the mother's womb in this manner with the second membrane, then cut the second membrane with your nail until it is expelled by moisture.
If the fetus hangs over the face and its neck, then cut it from the navel so that it is not retained and dies.
Then push the fetus towards the interior until you place her as necessary; and command the woman to compress herself several times; for it will come out easily with an exit.
Delivery of twins or many fetuses. You should know that twins are often born; and sometimes three or four are born. However, this is an exception and rarely occurs.
But five is beyond nature and do not live completely; and it contains them, although they are multiplying, by a single second membrane; and they are separated by the siphac, distinguishing the tied one at each of their navels.
And sometimes they come out like a single fetus through the natural and easy exit, and they come out through an unnatural exit as we have said.
If some of them are difficult during childbirth and reach what we have said in the unnatural figures, then care for them as we have said: and let the midwife be subtle, and do what she does with ease and slowness, and invent every figure according to the one that is being prepared for him to save.
Recall that which forms in the womb from embryos, and they abort.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven and more than ten are formed in the womb: and it is already proven with me that a woman has expelled seven and another fifteen, all of them being formed.
What was done by the measurement of the glorious wise man.
Therefore, this entire matter should be in the knowledge of Obstetrics. Perhaps it may reach a similar one; therefore, confront it with that which is necessary.
Chapter LXXVI.
On the extraction of the dead fetus.
When you care for a dead fetus as I said in the division from medication, and it does not come out, and you will have to operate with your hand, then it is necessary that you consider.
If the woman is of good health and not with any accident from which it is feared for her loss: then it is necessary that the woman lies on the bed, on her back, and let her head be inclined downwards, and her legs lifted up; and the attendant holds her from both sides or tied to the bed, so that her body does not come out during the extraction of the fetus.
Then moisten the cervix of the womb with moist oils such as olive oil, almond oil, fenugreek and linseed.
Then the obstetrician wets his hand with these oils and mucilages; then he introduces it into the womb easily. Then he seeks a place where he can insert hooks on the fetus, and places that are suitable for it.
Therefore, consider then if the fetus is ready to descend upon its head; then insert hooks into its eyes, neck, mouth, palate itself, under its beard, in its collarbone, near the ribs, and below the hypochondriac regions.
If it is a descent (affecting) his feet, then make an incision in his breastbone and in the middle of his ribs.
And it is necessary that he holds a hook with his right hand; and places his wound on that which is between the fingers of his left hand; and introduces (his hand) with ease, and strikes the hook in one of those places which we have mentioned, until he reaches an empty space.
Then strike the hook another or third (time), if necessary; so that the constriction may be equal and not deviate to one side.
Then it is extended with an equal extension, and not an extension only in a straight line, but rather moved to all sides, so that the opening may be relieved; as it is done with a tooth during its extraction.
And it is necessary that in that place, the extension may be softened. If a part is held back from it (the wound), then it is necessary that the midwife joins some fingers with oil and introduces them from that side to turn what is held back.
If therefore a part of the fetus comes out, then hooks are changed to another higher place; do this until the entire fetus comes out.
If therefore a hand comes out before the other and it is not possible to return it because of its bending; then it is necessary that a cloth be wound over it. Then extract it (the hand) until when the entire one comes out; cut it at the joint of the ankle or elbow; and thus it is necessary that you do this in both hands and feet.
If the head of the fetus is large, or there is bending at its exit, or water has collected on it; then it is necessary that a pointed spatula be introduced between the fingers and pierce the head, and extract the water; or break it with an instrument called Almisdac, whose shape comes with the shapes of the other instruments in the chapter following this.
Similarly, perform [the procedure] if the fetus is large-headed by nature, then it is necessary to cut the hairs off [the fetus]; or pull it out with forceps, as we have said. Then pull out the bones with forceps.
If the head comes out and is stuck at the neck, then it is to be split until the moisture that is in the chest is released.
If it does not twist nor yield for an exit, then cut the head intermittently, as you are able.
If there is an abscess below the womb or it contains water (hydrops), then pierce it through until the moisture runs out from it.
If the fetus is large-footed, then its extraction is easy and its direction towards the bone of the womb is light.
If it is stuck in the belly or chest, then pull it out with a cloth that you have wrapped over your hand; and split the belly or chest until what is inside runs out from them.
If other members are torn away and the head returns, then the midwife should insert her left hand. If the bone of the womb is open, then insert your hand deep into the womb and search for the head with it, and pull it out with your fingers up to the bone of the womb; then insert a hook or hooks in it and pull it out with them.
If the bone of the womb is stuck due to a hot abscess that has happened to it, then it should not be pressed upon it, but rather administer warm liquids and oil; and apply poultices; and sit in waters that soften and moisturize.
If the fetus is on its side, then it can be turned; then administer what was said for a living fetus.
If it is not possible to do that, then it should be cut piecemeal and extracted.
And it is necessary that you do not leave anything inside the seconda at all.
Therefore, when you have completed your operation, then administer what we said regarding warm cauteries that occur in the wombs (uteri).
If there is a flow of blood, then it goes down in warm water and administer the remaining treatment.
I myself have seen a woman whose womb contained a dead fetus; then she became pregnant again with another one, and yet another stillborn fetus was found in her. After a long period of time, she developed an aposteme in the navel, which became swollen until it burst open and began to emit pus.
Therefore I was summoned for her treatment, and I treated her for a long time; but the wound did not heal.
So I put on it some strong adhesive plasters; and the bone came out of the place. Then after a few days, another bone came out. Therefore I was amazed when there was no bone in the womb.
Therefore, you thought that the dead fetuses were bones.
I asked about the wound and extracted many bones from her, while she was in good health; and she lived for a long time in this condition, and emitted little pus.
And I did not bind this foreign body here, except that it contains knowledge and help for what the skilled physician administers when healing with his hand.
Chapter LXXVII.
Section on the shapes of necessary instruments for extracting a fetus.
The form of the Spiral that opens the Matrix.
Here is the form of the Stricture Instrument, by which books are leveled; it has two equal spirals at each end of two pieces of wood. Nevertheless, this Spiral should be finer than the Stricture Instrument; and for this purpose, it may be made of ivory or boxwood.
And the width of all the wood should be about two fingers; and the edge of each of both is like one finger, and the length of each of them is a palm and half; and in the middle of two pieces of wood there are two additions made of the same kind of wood which have already been hardened on either side, whose length is half a palm and less; and the width of each of them is about two fingers or less.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the matrix, to open it when you turn the two spirals.
Another form similar to it but finer and lighter.
It should be made of ivory or boxwood, according to the resemblance of forceps. Nevertheless, at its end there should be two additions as you see here above; and the length of all the additions is like a palm; and the width of each of them is about two fingers.
When you wish to open the matrix with it, then have the woman sit on a bed, her legs being hanging down, and that which is between her thighs be opened. Then insert these two connected additions into the matrix; and you hold the end of the instrument lower between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument as you do with forceps, equally according to the amount you wish for the opening of the mouth of the matrix, until the midwife does what she wants.
Form of Dizziness Different Than That Which the Ancients Called Impetigo Fetus (Impulsive Presentation of the Fetus)
The form which breaks the large head: and it resembles a pair of forceps, having teeth at the end, as you see.
And sometimes it becomes wedge-shaped, as a pair of forceps according to this form, as you see, having teeth like the teeth of a saw, with which it is cut and crushed.
The form of the scissors having one spine.
The form of the scissors having two spines.
The form of the spatula having two ends for cutting off the head.
The form of two broad spatulas also.
All these instruments are used, and the more they multiply in variety, the more prepared they are by the craftsman, is quicker for its operation, and higher among men, because of their quantity.
Therefore do not despise one of these instruments, as if it were not prepared for you. For the necessity of them is inexcusable (inexorable).
Chapter 78.
Chapter on Second Extraction.
When the second is retained at birth, then it must be commanded to retain its breath. Then make her sneeze with powder: and press your hand on her mouth, and her own nostrils. If therefore it exits through this, it is good.
If not: then take the pot and pierce a hole in the covering; and place inside it herbs that open the cervix, such as calaminthe, root of ruta, anise, camomile, wood of senna, centaury, and linear cassia; take all these herbs or some of them, submerge them with water, and place them over fire.
Then place the infusion of rushes on the hole of the covering pot and another end into the cervix; hold it until the vapor reaches the concavity of the uterus.
Then make her sneeze, as we have said. For second birth it will exit easily.
If it remains after this treatment and does not exit: then order the midwife to submerge her hand in sesame oil or mallow gum. Then insert into the vagina and search for the second child. When she finds it, then take it and gradually stretch it out.
If it is attached deep in the uterus, then insert the hand as we have said until she finds the second child and extracts it gradually in a straight manner so that the matrix does not fall due to violent attraction; rather, it should be moved with ease to the right and left; then add more according to the strength of the attraction. It will obey then, and be saved, and exit from attachment.
If the cervix is constricted, as we have already said: treat it with sneezing and medicine from the pot with herbs.
If it does not exit with all that we have said, then beware not to tire her in the repetition of extraction.
It is necessary that what comes out from the matrix bone should be tied to the woman's hip. Then, enema her with the four-ingredient ointment. For it will corrupt and dissolve her after days, and will come out.
However, when it corrupts, raise a bad smell from her to the stomach and head, and injure that which is already weak. Therefore, it is necessary that appropriate fumigations be administered for this purpose.
Some of the ancients have already experimented with a fumigation of nasturtium and figs dried in the sun.
The shape of the instrument with which to fumigate the woman during the retention of the Second Stage and periods.
Make it similar to an alcamea vessel or a jar: and place the wide end over the fire: fumigation should be placed on plums: hold her while that fumigation is consumed: and repeat another one.
Chapter LXXIX.
Chapter on the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many boys are born, and the anuses of these babies are not perforated, which have already been opened by a sharp forceps. Therefore, the midwife must pierce it with her finger; and if she cannot, she must pierce it with a sharp spatula; and be careful not to touch the muscle.
Place upon it a cloth soaked in wine and oil. Then take care of it with ointments until it heals.
If one fears that it is obstructed, then put a lead tube into the opening and leave it for many days; and when the child wants to come out, it will be removed.
And now, obliteration of the anus also occurs due to healing of a wound or an abscess. Therefore, that consolidation must be cut off; then it should be treated as we have said before with the remedy and lead.
Chapter 80.
Chapter on the treatment of fistulas occurring in the lower part.
Fistulas that occur in the lower part are nodosity and swelling that occur near the anus outside; or in the space of one part; and it is a fistula or multiple fistulas.
When therefore that old knot is opened, watery white moistness or subtle pus flows out from it.
And at times these are penetrating fistulas. Therefore they are recognized by what comes out during discharge, and by wind when the sick person uses discharge; perhaps a worm comes out of them.
There are fistulas among these when they penetrate the space to the bladder and to the bowel of the penis. There are also penetrating ones that reach as far as the hip joint and the node of the tail.
From that which a penetrating fistula is recognized to the anus, it is also known from a fistula not penetrating, that you insert your index finger into the anus and insert a probe thin in the fistula made of metal or iron, without twisting, if there is no tortuosity.
If there is twisting [in the fistula], then insert a thin probe of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or the hair on your finger.
If you do not feel it to the bottom and nothing comes out from discharge or wind or worm as I said; then you will know that it is not penetrating, so approach for treatment.
And when a fistula is penetrating to the bladder or urethra; its sign is the outflow of urine from it and its prohibition from this, that the location be consolidated with medicines.
If it is penetrating to the hip joint or the hip bone; its sign is that a probe reaches up to there if there is no twisting up to the bone; and pain in the surrounding area, and that pus always comes out from it; and that medicine cannot be effective in it, nor does it consolidate with an ointment.
In these all penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all: and their cure is labor and futility to him, upon whom they are formed, from foolish physicians.
In that which is not penetrating and not old, healing is hoped for with the lancet: according to what I tell you, and I have already proven it: and there lies the sick one between your hands upon his back: and rub his legs up to his hips, and let his hips be inclined toward his own belly. Then introduce the lead or copper, if there is a winding in the fistula, until you know where the probe reaches.
If the sick one feels it near the anus, then it is necessary that your index finger be introduced into the anus.
If you therefore feel the probe penetrate by itself, which is detected on your finger and between your finger and the fistula or flesh: then you certainly know that it is penetrating; so do not labor in it, because there is no cure for it, as we have said.
They say that flesh heals in some men, and the remedy by which they hope for help is to burn cauterization as thin as the width of the fistula, as before, and to introduce the burning into the fistula until it reaches near the anus. Then do this twice or thrice until you know that all those added fatty tissues filtered, which are like the quills of a bird's feather, have been burnt.
Then care for it with linen cloths in butter until those burnt fats come out: then care for it with ointments generating and consolidating flesh.
If therefore it heals, it is good.
And if not, then it is never cured with any other treatment.
If it (the tumor) escapes and does not reach your finger which is inside the anus, and there is a thick layer of flesh or scrotum between it and the tumor, or if you see a fistula on what follows the surface of the skin, then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and you go cutting with the tumor that is in the fistula until you reach the point where the extension of the scrotum ends, and the scrotum is released and falls off.
Then clean those tissues which resemble the feathers of a bird's quill, so that nothing remains from them.
If blood prevails and breaks through between you and your operation, so that those tissues escape, then it is better and more speedy relief to cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
Because the cautery with fire produces good results by applying heat to those tissues, charring of those added tissues, stopping bleeding, and drying out moisture.
Then treat it with linens wrapped in butter or cooked leeks until the place emits pus, and those burnt tissues come out into the pus.
Then treat the wound with strengthening ointments that produce hard flesh; there are medicines containing styptics and drying agents.
For when it is restored, then it is cured; do not fear repetition.
If the fistula has already reached deep into the anus and is stretched out by the body's excess: then insert your finger into the anus, and examine it with it.
If you feel a tumor, and there is a layer of scrotum or flesh between it and yourself, which is close to penetrating: then there is no operation on that unless it is according to the path of trust and hope.
That is, because it is administered in him one of the three modes: either to cauterize it itself, as we said; or to excise it, until you reach its concavity, so that it is possible for you to insert a linen, and cure it from nearby. And do not proceed too much with the excision, lest you cut into the flesh containing the anus, and it happen by accident an unfortunate outcome of excretion without will. Then cure that with what I said.
For perhaps it will heal: or lengthen the same membrane and cleanse it after you have cut it up to near the anus, as we said, either with a probe or with another sharp tool. Then clean those fleshes filtered which are in the excision, as far as you can with examination.
Then strive for the healing of the whole wound with excision and superior opening where it heals; and the fistula remains open at the interior part of the anus, and it will be easier on the patient.
And sometimes the fistula is drained in this manner: and it is when you insert a probe into the fistula; and it is on the side of the anus near the surface of the body with skin and margin of the anus; then take the probe perforated at its end, which is like the awl (aleskef), that is, prepared with calfskin, in this form. And insert into it a thread wound around five strands and around thereabouts. Then insert the probe with a thread into the fistula until you reach its concavity.
If it penetrates into the margin of the anus internally, then pull out the thread from that opening; so that you can insert your finger into the anus and pull out the end of the thread, and bring together its two ends; and tie each one and let it remain for one or two days; and the more the thread cuts into the flesh, the better tie it, until the fleshes between the two ends of the thread fall off and drop away; then cure the wound, until it heals and is cured.
If, however, the opening of the Fistula is not penetrating: then make it penetrate by any means prepared for you, unless it is in great depth. For you, there is no need to do that (make an incision) so as not to cut the muscle itself.
Then do it as we said, until it is healed.
Make the spatula for the spiny fistula, whose sharpness is very acute on one side and not acute on the other so as not to cut what is unnecessary, as you can see.
Chapter LXXXI.
On sewing hemorrhoids from which blood runs after being cut; and on the treatment of fissures (fissure in ano).
There are hemorrhoids according to two modes. Either they are inside the anus, similar to coal lumps or prunes; or like grains of wheat themselves. And from these there are small ones and large ones; blood always runs from them, and there is one, and there are many. And they are outside the anus, and at its extremities.
However, those which are outside the anus, are for the most part few in moisture, from which runs either lemon water or a little blood with constant flow; and they are according to the color of the body.
And the treatment of those which are inside the anus is to order the patient to sit on hot water, and it is expressed until it appears outside the anus and appears to you as athelia. Therefore, also hang them with hooks; or hold them with your nail. Then cut them at their roots.
If they are not held by hooks due to their moisture and their own softening: then take them with a rough cloth or a glove made of double wool and remove them with your fingers. Then cut them (the vessels), and sprinkle some warm powders over them after the incision for them to remain in place of the cautery. Either cauterize them according to what preceded in the chapter on cauterization. Then take care of them with the rest of the treatment until they heal.
If the anus does not obey to evacuation, then enema should be administered with a slight purgative, so that the sick person is cleansed with what is in the anus, and the evacuation is quick when the sick person releases it.
If the faeces are outside the anus, then their condition is light and easy; it is good to grasp them with your nail or to grasp them with a tweezers, and cut them. Then take care of them with what I said before, until they heal.
And if the wound resists cutting with an iron, then it is necessary to apply suture to them in this way. Take a thread rolled up and insert it into the point. Then pull the faeces towards the top and make it penetrate with the point on its root from the other side; and wind up the ends of the thread around the point and let them be broad; and tie the faeces tightly with a strong knot. Then tie the thread, and pull out the point.
Do this with all faeces and leave one; do not leave yourself, so that excess of blood flows out from it.
Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil or pitch over the anus and place it on the anus; and order the sick person to rest. Then let him be until he falls asleep.
When the faeces fall, take care of them with ointments and the rest of the treatment until they heal.
On treating fissures (or cuts). For they often happen due to the removal of feces and constriction of nature.
When they have become chronic and medicine is not effective on them: then it is necessary that you shave with a spatula or with your nail until they become moist, and the superficial layer which prevents their healing should be removed. Then care for them until they heal as required.
If they do not heal: then treat them more forcefully than the first time, until they bleed much, and after that care for them until they are healed.
On treating an anus that is not right (or abnormal), and one that is normal: and about ulcers (Athelil) and scabies (Formicae).
Chapter LXXXII.
Know that Almirmar is only a round swelling similar to the head of a nail, colored like the body, and it occurs throughout the body, particularly in the lower parts of the feet and fingers; and pain occurs during walking from it.
It is necessary that the part on the nail-like swelling be cut off and held with forceps or a nail, and it should be removed from its root.
Then care for that, and if you wish, cauterize it as described in the previous chapter.
From ulcers (Athelil), one is a small elevation, rough, filtered, round on the surface of the body. And they often occur in children's hands.
The treatment is to spread the ulcer (Athelil), and cut or prick it; or stitch it with silk thread; or pluck out the hair until it falls off. If you wish, cauterize it with fire or with sharp medicine; and now the abnormal ulcers (Athelil) and normal ones are removed with a tool that I will describe.
The translation of the sentence is: "Formica (ant) is also a small prominent filtrate, thick, on the surface of the body, penetrating deeply: and when it is found, it feels like a bite from an ant all over the body, and it mostly occurs in the hands.
The treatment of it is to take a cannula from a goose feather, or strong vulture feather: and place the cannula over the formica, until the circle of the cannula contains its parts. Then rotate your hand with the cannula until it separates what is around the formica: and place it deep into the flesh, and pull out the formica from its root.
And if you wish, do this with an iron or brass cannula in this manner.
Let the upper part of the cannula be bent upwards, pulling a mute roll towards it, to be relieved by its grip and rotation itself.
And if you wish to cauterize the formica as mentioned before in the chapter on cauterization in Athelil's text.
Chapter LXXXIII.
Chapter on the tools for fumigations applied to diseases of the anus, and solutions of the stomach, and colic.
Whence the clisteria is made of silver, gold, brass melted or hammered.
And sometimes these instruments are small and large, according to those in whom they are used.
Therefore, that which is administered in the treatment of small children should be small: and for weak or painful anuses, so also the suppositories.
Large suppository.
The cannula's upper part where it is tied to the uterus should be wide according to this method: and it should have a distinct portion to be tied to the uterus as you see, and its lower end which is inserted into the anus, should be closed, that is, not open, soft, very fine, drawing towards subtlety: and on one of its sides there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
And let the size of the hole be according to the thickness of rods, not too thick and not too thin, and let the uterus in which the medicines are placed be made from the bladder of an animal or from a sheep's parchment, shaped like a small asafetida bag, whose root is one palm.
And it should be perforated with many holes as is common, and the space between each hole should be the thickness of a finger. Then insert into those holes a thread, perhaps made from raw linen, which should be about ten threads or approximately that amount, and gather it with the uterus like an asafetida bag. When this is placed inside it, the upper part of the suppository should be tightly bound with two distinct parts by a strong constriction. Then apply the suppository with it.
And this is the circular form depicted here, and the holes.
The quality of making the suppository with it is as follows: fill the uterus or bladder with medicine that has been heated according to the tolerance of the sick person: and be careful not for it to be too hot or too cold.
Then the sick person lies down on his back, and lifts his legs upwards: and place beneath him something soft, that is, hide or linen.
Then anoint the extremity of Clisteris with oil, or with white goose fat, or with mucilage of fenugreek, or something similar. Then introduce it into the anus with ease. Then let the attendant receive the bladder with both his hands at once, and squeeze it with violence, until all that is in the Clisteris passes into the intestines.
Then remove the Clisteris, and the sick person lifts his legs upwards to the wall.
If medicine forces him to evacuate, then hold him as much as possible. And if he sleeps the whole night with it, it is more of a cure.
If you clisterize him with diseases of the abdomen and his evacuation is hurried: then clisterize again until he is cured.
If there are hemorrhoids or painful sores in the anus, then let it be very subtle and soft, mild, from the Clisteris with which boys are clisterized.
And this is the form of a soft Clisteris on which the skin is stretched tightly.
Chapter LXXXXIV.
I have already said in the division of treating wounds that it belonged to a book, and I will say here the treatment with hands, and with medications according to the supplement.
Therefore, wounds are distinguished according to how they are made, and according to the place where the wound falls.
Therefore, wounds made in this way are like being struck by a stone: or cut with a sword or knife: or pierced with a lance, or log, or arrow: and similar things from many other objects.
Wounds that occur according to the parts of the body are such as a wound falling on the head, neck, chest, abdomen or back; and similar ones from these members.
And I am telling the cures of some wounds, so that I may place the reasoning and rule over the rest of the wounds.
And I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the recollection of compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say. If it happens that there is a simple wound on the head and no bone fracture has occurred; consider then if it is due to a blow of a stone or similar object, and only the skin has been broken; and the wound is large, and you fear an imminent abscess of hot pus; then act quickly, and make a venesection of the head at once; and do not delay that; and draw out from him according to the potency of blood as much as possible, unless something forbids phlebotomy, especially if the blood flowing out of the wound is scant. Let the venesection be on the opposite side of the wounded part.
Let the venesection be on the opposite side of the wounded part. And let him be careful not to fill himself with food and heavy drinks.
If something prevents reduction, then reduce the food, but avoid meat and wine.
And put on the wound if there is a hot abscess, warm infusion of cooked food in rose oil only, or with wine containing saltpeter.
If you are free from a hot abscess, then put on the wound if it is recent with its own blood and has not changed air; and if the air has already changed, then put something over it as I will tell later; and if it has already changed air, then put some ointments on it until it heals.
If the wound is large, or it is from a sword cut and similar ones: and its edges are not brought together by pimples, then bring them together with sutures, as I will explain regarding the wounds of the abdomen in the matter of their suturing.
If the wound is already exposed from bone and hangs, and there is no retention of it unless in a small suspender: then cut it (the hanging part). Then take care of the wound with medicines, and restore hard flesh to it where there is skin deficiency, and instruct the sick man to eat foods with bulk, such as heads (of animals) and cooked wheat, until it becomes soft; and similar foods.
If you find putrefaction in the skin and it does not adhere to the bone: then cut out the putrefied part, and throw it away; then take care of it (the remaining wound).
If however, in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows and it cannot be cut off by medicines: then probe for the artery (or vein). If you find it uncut, then cut it with a spatula, or tie it up (with sutures). If necessity compels and you cannot do what was said, then cauterize it (the artery or vein) until the blood separates.
If however, these wounds are small and simple: then the matter is easy and light; so that you sprinkle this powder on them, because it solidifies them before air changes (their state).
Chapter on the Powder for Consolidation. Prepare one part of olibanum (frankincense), two parts of dragon's blood (a red resin used as a medicine), and three parts of unburnt lime: grind it thoroughly and sieve it; fill the wound with it, compress it well, until it adheres well on top, and coagulate it with blood.
Then bind it above with sutures, and let it be, do not release it until it remains so that it does not come apart. The medicine is not to be removed from him until he is healed.
And at times plaster alone does it when there is no olibanum and the blood of a dragon also does the same operation in many large wounds when it is suitable to be placed on them and they are bound, and the wounds are recent with their own blood, which has not been altered by air.
If the air has already changed it by some alteration, especially when it is in summer time, then there is no use for this powder: therefore take care of it with what I said, put some digestive ointments over it or make poultices from barley flour mixed with water and honey until pus is emitted. Then care for the rest of the healing until they are healed.
But if a fracture occurs in the bone with the wound and it is small, then extract it with trepan; and now I will speak of the treatment of skull fractures that will follow.
[Section on neck wounds]
If a wound occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple wound of the head.
If the nerve of the neck or the artery is already cut: if it is a nerve, there is no skill in treating it except to turn the treatment towards avoiding violent stiffness, such as ziniar and zegi and similar things. Because they hurt nerves, and contract them.
And do not place anything cold on the wound at all: because the substance of nerves is cold and its continuation is with the brain, which is above the organs; therefore that which is to be treated should be made from soft medicines such as lime plaster mixed with sweet water several times infused with oil or rose oil, or pitch when washed even with sweet water; and other mineral stones in this manner, and moist unguents.
If the wound is large, then administer suture: or sew its edges with threads. Then care for it until it heals.
If the wound is deep or if a sinus has gathered pus at its lower part, then puncture it at a more depressed place.
If an artery has already been cut in the wound and bleeding has occurred, then separate or sever it and tie it; or cauterize it if there is a need for that.
If the windpipe has already been cut, either entirely or partially, and the trachea has been saved: then sew the lips of the skin over a reed for the windpipe, and do not touch the windpipe itself; on the contrary, support it and reduce it to its natural shape. Then bind it with a suitable bandage and let it rest for some days. Then, care for yourself with ointments that contain styptic and astringent properties until you are healed.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then examine it. If there are fragments of bone in it, remove all of them or what can be removed: leave what cannot be prepared until the wound rots and separates, and the discharge subsides.
If the wound is recent, then sprinkle powder over it as I have described. If there appears to be bone in the wound and a fistula is formed: then care for it as described in its own chapter.
Chapter on Wounds Treated with Spatulas.
If it is a wound caused by a lance or knife and you see its depth, then consider the following. If gas is discharging from the wound when the sick person is breathing heavily, then know that the wound is fatal.
If the wound is not deep and is recent with blood, then do not apply powder to it immediately or press on it so that the blood does not remain in its depth and return to the heart and kill the sick person: instead, place an attracting ointment on it and dissolve it twice a day.
If an attracting ointment is not available to you, then place a dry old cotton wool on the wound's opening to absorb what discharges from it due to moisture: make sure the sick person sleeps over the wound so that what collects there can heal.
If three or more days have passed since the wound occurred and there is no spasm, no bad heart tremor, no narrowing of breathing, and you see that the other signs are good: then know that the wound is healed. Cure yourself and with linen cloths, and the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
If the healing opens again, and it always opens up, then you should know that it has become a Fistula. Therefore, cure it from its root.
And if the wound is from a sword cut or knife, and it is simple on the chest or back surface: then treat it with the suture that preceded it, if it is large: or with powder, if it is small.
But if it has already made an indentation on the bone and cut off fragments from it: then examine the wound, and hurry to pull out those fragments, if they are separated. But if they are not separated, then leave them until the wound rots, for the extraction of those will heal the wound.
As for other wounds caused by accidents on other limbs, the judgement of treatment is as we said.
Chapter on abdominal wounds and the passage of the intestine, and their discharge.
A rupture that occurs in the abdomen can be great, medium, or small.
From a great rupture, at times the intestine or number of intestines comes out.
Therefore, insertion and suturing of those is required, being more violent and difficult.
A small rupture can also be difficult in another way. Therefore it is more difficult to reduce it if you do not hurry in its insertion to its place immediately, because it swells, opens up and becomes enlarged, making the entrance difficult.
Therefore, a medium rupture is better because with it the reduction of the intestine is not difficult, as it is with these two types.
Know that suture of the vein is according to four modes.
Two commons [types of] sutures converge in the suture of the abdomen, and in the suture of other wounds of the body; and two other types of sutures specifically communicate with the remaining wounds. However, they are more proper with the suture of the abdomen; and I tell you one by one, along with its exposure and explanation.
Therefore, when the wound is small and something comes out from the intestine, and it becomes difficult to return it; then that is due to one of the two modes. Or because of the smallness of the rupture, as we said; or because there is distension in the intestine due to cold air.
When that is the case, then one should heat it thus, by immersing a sponge or a damp cloth in warm water alone. Or boil in water leeks, cumin, dill, and ginger with the intestine, until the distension is resolved.
Sometimes it does wine where there is stricture; and that is better than water alone for the resolution of distension.
When you see the distension is already resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which ale or mead has been boiled. For through that the opening of it (the intestine) may be eased with a small thing.
If the return of it (the intestine) is expelled after this treatment, then close the rupture with a little bit, using an instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut.
And the first treatment is better when it is prepared, than the cutting; and it is not to be forced for cutting after necessity and lack of instruments.
Let one part of it (the instrument for the treatment) be twisted, sharp, and another part not sharp, and the tip should not be fine like the point of a needle, rather it should be a little blunt; and that is similar to a lancet, as you see.
When a wound is enlarged and enters the intestine, it is then necessary that its reduction should be according to its own natural form in its proper place, if possible over it; because it is better.
When the wound is wide in the lower part of the abdomen, then it is necessary that you make him lie on his back and place his legs higher than his head. And if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then place his head and his chest higher than his lower parts.
And similarly if the wound is in one of the two parts of the abdomen, then direct your attention and consideration always in this way, so that the part where the wound is is higher than the other part.
Therefore, it must be applied in large wounds and in middle wounds.
In small wounds, place it as it is prepared for you.
Then make sure that a devoted servant is present between your hands who holds the wound with his whole hand and sews the edges together. Then, cut some thread for the one who follows to stitch; and this is the common method of sewing one together.
And it is, that you take a needle or a number of needles according to the size of the wound. Then release a quantity of finger width from the end of the wound, that is, of the doctor; and fix one needle beyond which you insert the thread into both edges of the skin, with both edges of the flesh that are under the skin from inside, until you make it penetrate from the other side, and you have already sewn together the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the flesh; and they become four rows.
Then sew together with thread twice around the needle several times from both sides until the edges of the wound are sewn together properly.
