Then release the thickness of the finger also, and sew in them another awl; afterwards draw it straight with thread, as you did with the first awl. Do not stop doing that with the awls you require until you complete the contraction of the whole wound.
Let the awls be of medium size between thickness and delicacy; for delicate awls pierce the flesh too quickly, and large ones have a difficult entrance into the skin; therefore it is necessary that they be of medium size in delicacy and thickness.
It is not necessary that the awl be sewn at both ends of the skin close together; so as not to pierce the flesh too quickly, and open the wound before its consolidation, nor should they extend even with suturing, lest the wound be prevented from consolidating.
Then cut the end of the awl so as not to injure the weak person while asleep; and place little woolen balls on both ends of the awl from every side, which will hold the end of the awl; and release them when you know that the wound has already consolidated.
And this kind of suturing with awls is more suitable for small wounds. Because one or two needles, or around them, are sufficient for their suturing.
The second suturing is common, that you gather the ends of four: the ends of the skin, two, and the ends of the stitching thread, two, or in place of one, with an awl containing equal thread in delicacy and thickness.
Then when you pierce with the awl these four ends, withdraw the awl from the side where it entered, so that the thread tied above the wound falls; so that the suturing will be like that of cloth when they are sewn together, and place between every suture a quantity equal to the thickness of the little finger.
Men know this suture.
And with this suture, I sewed up the wound of my man which had occurred within his belly, who had been wounded with a knife, and the wound was larger than one palm: and out had come from the intestines about two palms from the middle intestine, and there was a rupture in the middle of the abdomen.
I therefore returned it (the protruding organ) after the intestine of his had been outside the wound for twenty-four hours.
The wound had healed in the space which was about fifteen days: and I cured him, and he recovered: and he lived after that for many years, turned back to his duties.
And the physicians judged that it would not heal (get better).
And it was a miracle that I did not cure it with ointment. Because I was in a place where no ointment could be found, nor any medicine. I therefore put on the wound old dough twice a day, and attended to its cleansing with water of honey, until it healed.
I shall now speak of two kinds of sutures according to the narrative of speech.
And it begins with a sharp suture: and you insert the point from outside to inside.
When the point penetrates the skin, and along its length and width throughout the whole body: release the end of the suture at the side where you inserted the point, and make it penetrate to the other end from the inner part to the outside at the opposite extremity.
When you have made it penetrate, then make it penetrate thus in the same extremity from outside to inside: and release the end of the suture at the side where you are inserting the point, and make the point penetrate to the other end from the inner part to the outside, and make it penetrate with your penetration as you do it, until it penetrates completely.
Then also begin from the same side, and extract the point itself with its extremity, which is from the back on the other side, and pull out the tip that penetrated through the skin.
Then bring it back into the same skin, and extract its extremity from the other side with this extremity (the point), and pull it out from the skin on that side, and do it this way once, and then the other, alternating: and do it this way after the other, until you have extracted all of it according to that example.
The sum of this suture is that your sutures for the skin should be smaller than the skin itself: in such a way that you sew the points (the knots) of one side of the skin with one part of the extremity of the skin: and that you release it with the other part on the other side, until you have completed it.
The second species (type) of suture proper, as Galen said.
This discourse is told to you as it is done by some healers in the way that they gather all parts fitting each other according to nature: and apply the point of one side of the skin to the other side's point, and the point of the back (mirach) to the other side's point. And this is done as I tell you.
You must make the tip of the back (mirach) stick out at the extremity of the skin close to you on the outside, and let it penetrate only to the inside there: and release both points (extremities) of the skin. Then turn the tip, and let it penetrate from the outside to the inside into both points (extremities) of the skin, namely on both sides.
Then turn both, and let both penetrate from the inside to the outside, into the opposite points (tips) of the back (mirach), which are on the other side.
This method of stitching is better than common stitching and is a stitch which recalls remembrance.
Thus is the speech of Galen also.
And they said thus: The stitch of the abdomen is straightened with two hooks. The thread is introduced into each of them (the abdominal wounds) with one filament: and begin with the introduction of the hook from the part which is with you, and make it pass evenly along the skin stitches.
And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen: then the stitching of this (rupture) is more difficult than the rest of the places in the abdomen.
The judgment of the treatment of the wound is the judgment of other wounds.
The fact is that when you come upon a fresh wound with its own blood, before it changes by the air: and if you bring out the intestine, and wash it, and make it fit: then place it on powder of burnt flesh (or incarnate).
If the air has already altered the wound: then place some ointments on it which are present with you, until they make pus; and let threads fall (on the wound) and be pressed down with mullein leaves and myrrh. Then treat that as the treatment of other wounds until it heals.
If there are no medications present with you, then immediately place on it that which begins to emit pus, old cottons; and change it twice a day as I have taught you until it heals.
For you do not need another medication for the most part when the wounds are simple.
If you fear that the wound may communicate to the main members in the injury, then it is necessary for you to immerse a soft wool in oil of temperate warmth or rose oil: and place it in the region around the groins, and under the armpits.
If it feels pain or punctures, or rottenness in its own intestines (for this often happens), then clisterize him with warm wine of pitch, black: particularly if the rot has already reached the intestine and an opening has been made penetrating to the depths of its concavity.
And know that what is from the large intestine is easier to heal; and what is from the small intestines is harder to heal.
The intestine called Jejunum does not receive healing from a wound that occurs in it at all: and this is because of the multitude of its veins, and their size, and the subtlety of its body, and its proximity to the nature of nerves.
If however what comes from the wound is yellowish and you seize it fresh: bring it back according to your reduction, by which you reduce the intestines equally.
If however it has passed a space, and is already greenish or black: then it is necessary that you tie it with thread above the place which has darkened from it, so that there is no bleeding. For in yellowish there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligament and place two ends of the thread hanging from below on the lower part of the wound outside it: so as to alleviate its attraction towards you, and the extraction of the yellowish at the site of the wound, and the emission of pus from the wound.
Memory of the wound that occurs in the intestine.
When there is a rupture in the intestine and it is small, it is possible that it can be restored in some people: because I have seen one who was wounded in his belly with a lance thrust and the wound was from the right side of the stomach, and it was an old wound: and a fistula was made, and it exuded purulent discharge.
I therefore left the treatment, until I was not confident in its healing; neither did I cease to probe it, until it was healed, and the place had been consolidated.
When I saw the place already consolidated, I feared an accident happening to the sick person in his belly; and no such accident happened to him from it. And he remained in better dispositions of himself, eating and drinking, urinating, and bathed, and exercised in his diet.
And some experimenters said that when an injury happens in the Intestine and is small, then it should be tied according to this method. And there is a way for you to capture ants with large heads. Then gather two lips of the wound and place one ant with an open mouth over the two lips of the wound. When its head is on them, and it closes its mouth, cut off its head, for it will stick to them and cannot be loosened.
Then place another ant near the first one and do not stop doing that until the ant matches the size of the entire wound.
Then return it [the ant] to its place, and close the wound. For those heads remain attached to the Intestine until it is eaten away and healed, and no harm comes to the sick person completely.
And now it is possible to tie the Intestine even with a fine thread; which has been taken out from the animal's Intestine and attached after it has been introduced into the point.
And there is a way to capture the end of this thread from the Intestine, and it should be scraped a lot. Then tie a fine linen thread at its end. Then insert the thread into the point and close the Intestine with it. Then reduce it to a dissection.
This method of suturing with worms and intestines, is not except by way of trust and hope.
Know that a large wound, especially if it is on one of the slender intestines, then there is no skill except refinement, and its healing is not possible at all.
Chapter on the care of the bladder, and fistulas.
Know that every wound or boil when it becomes old and decrepit, turns into an ulcer, does not consolidate, and always emits pus, and is not cut off: then it is called universally in whatever member it is, Fistula, and we call it Zuchemen.
And Fistula indeed is a hard, white knot filtered, without pain, which has the hollow of a bird's feather: and because of this some call it Risa, that is, the feather.
And there are some hours when it is moist, which emits pus. And perhaps the moisture is cut off at certain hours. And sometimes this moisture is much and it is little; and it is thick and it is refined.
And I have already mentioned in division, when I said wounds, that every ulcer which does not heal, nor flesh is born in it, it is not this for any one of nine causes.
Of which one is either due to the scarcity of blood in the body; or because it is malicious; or because there is hard flesh between it and its surrounding area preventing the growth of flesh; or because it is full of dirt and filth; or because the ulcer itself is putrid, and the matter that is sent to it is of bad quality; or because the medicine is inconvenient for its cure; or because corruption falling in the region is a kind of plague, as happens in Caesaraugusta: where digestion of illnesses is difficult and healing of boils is delayed by nature; or because there is one bone, or the number of bones.
I have already shown you all those causes and their signs, as well as the treatments for them with medicines in division. Here it is necessary that I make you know the treatment for Fistula and Strangulated Hernia, which is made through the way of surgery with the hand.
Know then, that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body. For these are the fistulas that reach to large veins and arteries, or nerves, or ligaments; or intestines, or bladder, or some of the ribs; or some of the vertebrae in the back, or some of the joints; such as hands, and feet: and these are those that approach the proximity of the main member and similar ones.
Which of these fistulas is according to this manner, is according to difficult healing and does not receive treatment, and the occupation with it is labor and ignorance.
If there is any fistula of which the depth does not reach to the places I have said: and you hope, and trust in its treatment, and wish to reach the knowledge of it, then take a probe of iron or copper, if the fistula points in the straight direction, and examine it with it.
If there is a twisting in the fistula, then investigate it with a thin probe of lead. Since lead, with its softness, is easily worn away and bent around twisting.
If the fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to sign over it with a probe. Cleanse then one opening from among its own openings.
For the moisture with which you cleanse it, goes towards the other openings and runs out of them.
Then examine and investigate according to the way that is possible for you: so that you may know if there is a bone or nerve, and the fistula's concavity is deep or near; or it is a single fistula with many openings, and stands over all of it, with the strength of your own questioning, by which you question the weak, and inquiring pain under pressure with your hand on the place, and similar signs and incidents.
When you stand over all these matters in a true position, then proceed to treatment with confidence. It is necessary for you at this time to consider whether it is a Fistula that appears near [the affected area], or in a safe distant place away from the junction, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or one of the places that I told you about: then cut the Fistula according to what has been mentioned in my account, and remove whatever is inside it through filtration, and the corruption of flesh that grows in its opening, or pus, and similar things. Care for [the area] until it heals.
If the Fistula is deep, and it is straight: then it should be cut as deeply as possible for you. Then cleanse [the area] from all corrupted flesh of it.
Then administer a linen cloth wrapped in sharp medicines and insert it into the concavity of the Fistula that you have seized with iron: do this repeatedly until the sharp medicine corrodes all that remains in the concavity of the Fistula due to corruption.
Then restore [the area] with unguents that promote healthy flesh until it heals.
If it does not heal through this, then cauterize [the area] as we have mentioned before.
If the cause of the Fistula is bone and it has been confirmed for you: then ask about it, and cut the bone according to what I told you. If nothing prevents you from doing so in a vein, or nerve, or major limb, as we have said before.
If a bone is revealed to you and there is some corruption or blackening in it: then scrape it until the corruption is completely removed. Then care for [the bone] with that which promotes healing until it heals.
If it does not heal and discharges pus as it was doing: then you know that you have not reached complete eradication of the corruption.
Excise therefore over it again, and inquire about its reason and cleanse it with all your strength.
Then restore it. If it heals, that is good; if not, then know that the corruption is in a deep part of the body which you have not reached. You therefore do not have skill in it, except to leave it to nature.
If the corrupted bone is small and it is possible for you, draw it out with fine forceps that fit to it.
If there are many bones, then inquire about their removal one by one, and do not leave any of them with your strength.
If it happens to you that something prevents you from any of the humidities and there is no fear or mistake in making an incision of them: then incise those humidities and flesh, if they are there, and free the bones.
If you do not have the preparation for removing bones from your time, then place on the wound what causes it to rot itself and leave it until it rots what is around those bones from the flesh and humidities.
And keep the wound so that it does not consolidate. And tighten the incision which you made in your operation. Or place on it, if you are afraid, hot cottons soaked in ground sulfur with oil; or hot cottons soaked in Egyptian ointment, or any green ointments.
For when those (humidities) rot certainly and the bones are separated from them, the removal of them is alleviated, and their drawing out.
If a single large bone, such as the bone of the leg or hipbone, and similar to them, has been corrupted, and what is from it is a large part: then shave it with the final rasp until that blackness and corruption are removed. Then restore the wound.
If what is corrupted in it is a large part and the corruption has already reached the bone marrow, then it must be sawn and cut through entirely until the point where corruption stops: then care for it until it heals.
And I tell you a case that occurs to a man in his leg: place it as an example and aid for your operation.
There was a young man about thirty years of age, who had pain in his leg, from a cause that moved upon him within the body, that is, from inside, until the matter reached the leg, and an abscess was made by an abscess, and it was not an external cause.
Then passed the time with him while the error of physicians occurred, until the abscess was opened, and many substances gathered with him. And his treatment was delayed until the leg became fistulous and many openings were made in it: which all emitted pus and moisture of the body.
Then a multitude of physicians cared for him about two years and there was no wise man in the art of hand in it until I was called upon, and saw his leg and the substances that were flowing from those openings at a large pace: even all the body of the man was already swollen, and his color was yellow.
I therefore inserted a probe into one of the openings and the probe reached the bone.
Then I examined all the openings: and found them to reach one another from every part of the leg.
I therefore made an incision over one of the openings, until I exposed a part of the bone; and I found it corrupt: which was already rotten, decayed, putrefied, perforated, until it had penetrated up to the marrow.
I therefore cut out what was exposed to me, and prepared it from the rotten bone.
And I removed, that there was nothing in the bone except that corruption, which I cut away. And I have already uprooted it.
Then I placed a dressing on the wound with consolidating medicines for a long space. And it was not consolidated.
Then I tried again, and exposed over the bone second above the first opening; and found a continuous corruption with the bone: and cut away what appeared to me also from that corruption.
Then I attempted to dress it. And it was not dressed.
Therefore I exposed again, and did not cease to cut the bone piece by piece, and attempt to dress it; and it was not dressed, until I cut from the bone about one palm's breadth, and extracted that with its marrow.
Then I dressed it with medicines, and it was quickly consolidated and healed; and this repetition was not necessary in the operation of his and the section of his, except for the disposition of his weakness, and the scarcity of his tolerance, and my fear over him of death; since it happened to him at all hours from an excess of evacuations with bad fainting spells.
Therefore he was completely healed; and there grew strong flesh on the site of the bone, and good arrangements were made in his body, and his strength returned; and he turned to his own dispositions; and he did no harm at all to him in walking.
If the prominent bone in the body is already fractured, then it is necessary that you grasp it in this manner: and it is as follows: to take a ligament, and tighten it at the end of the prominent bone; and command someone to stretch it upwards; and place another thicker ligament from wool on the first one. Then bind it to the flesh that surrounds the bone; extend its end so you can pull the flesh towards the lower parts; and you shall peel back the flesh over the place where you want to cut, so it doesn't get cut by the saw.
Place a wooden board or a table underneath the bone below; because when you do that, it is not forbidden to cut corrupted flesh.
It is necessary that the saw be slightly above the corrupted place, so that corruption is not in the concavity of the bone; and it should not appear to the senses in its view, and make another part serve as a substitute for the sawing.
If the bone is corrupted and not prominent, but rather continuous with another part, and corruption is in the middle or some part of it; then peel back the flesh from all its parts. Then place a wooden board underneath.
Then saw it from the first part where the corruption is, until the sawing is completed on the other side; and let the saw be slightly above the corruption, as we said before.
If the corruption is at a joint, cut the corrupted joint and saw the bone where it joins from the other side.
If, however, the corruption is between two joints, then there is no remedy but abrasion.
If the corruption is at the beak of the hand or foot, then it presents a very difficult situation. Nevertheless, you must find out what the nature of the corruption looks like to you. And file (or grind) her and clean her as well as possible for you, and when it is corrected by any means, it does not cause opposition to the Vein or Nerve for you.
And know that there are many cutting (instruments) and saws for cutting these bones according to the position of the bones, their preparation, their thickness, their thinness, their size, their smallness, their hardness, and their rarity. Therefore, it is necessary that the tool should be suitable for every kind of operation.
And know that these operations indicate to you according to the type of instrument that you need when your study is lengthy. And the knowledge of the methods of this art is a sign of the modes of diseases; then you will find for yourself what suits it from the instruments for every disease.
And I am confirming for you at the end of this chapter the number of instruments, which you will place as examples on which you cut, and the test by which you try it on others.
The form of another saw.
The form of a rasp for joints. Let the head of this rasp be shaped like the head of a star-headed nail; and its points should be shaped according to the form of the points of a file.
And it does not suit unless it is rubbed with it when the heads of the joints are broken, or if a large and thick bone is present.
Form of a larger razor.
Form of a broad razor.
Form of a razor with a concavity (convexity).
Form of another fine razor.
Form of another razor with a curved tip.
Form of a small, fine, bent razor.
This resembles a drill and its tip is similar to a saw: it is used at many places due to the reason of bones.
The form of a razor that fits for the purpose of cutting through bones.
Its tip is triangular and its angles are sharp.
It comes from India. And likewise it is necessary that all those things which I have said be made of razors, and chisels, and saws.
Section on the incising of extremities, and serration (cutting) of bones.
Extremities become rotten either due to external causes or internal causes.
Since you have treated the corruption with medication and it does not help, and you see that the corruption is spreading in a limb that nothing seems to affect: then it is necessary that you incise (cut) the limb up until where the corruption ends, so that the weakened part may escape death or the greater evil which is a defect of the limb.
And the sign for this is that the limb darkens (becomes black) until it seems to be dead; or the heat has burned it, or it becomes rotten after turning black: until the rot is cut through up until where it follows the limb and creeps throughout the entire body.
Therefore when you make the incision and likewise if the cause of the corruption is from the sting of certain venomous creatures such as marine scorpions, weasels, hedgehogs, and similar animals.
If therefore corruption or injury is at the extremity of a finger, then cut off the finger and do not leave space for corruption to spread, until it reaches the rest of the hand.
And similarly if it happens in the hand, then cut it off from the root of the wrist, and do not leave space for corruption to spread, until it reaches the arm's bone.
And if it invades it (the bone), then cut off the arm at the elbow joint.
If however corruption passes beyond (the arm) and you see it about the elbow: then there is the death of a weak man. And over that (the dead arm), administration of remedy is its amount of virtue.
And similarly do with the foot, when corruption invades a toe, then cut it off at one of the joints: and if it reaches the heel of the foot, then cut off the entire foot. And if it ascends to the knee, then cut off the leg at the joint of the knee.
If corruption has already reached above the knee, then there is no skill in it except to let it go and abandon the weak man to death.
And the method of cutting a member or sewing it is that you tighten the tendon below where you wish to cut, and tighten another tendon above the place. And stretch one of the tendons downwards, and stretch another tendon upwards towards the top. And you separate the flesh that is between two tendons with a broad knife until all the flesh is exposed. Then it is cut or sewn up.
And it is necessary that you place a linen cloth over all parts and not let the knife touch any healthy part; and an additional injury occurs to the weak man, and a hot abscess.
If however internal bleeding occurs while you are working on it, then quickly cauterize the place; or put some absorbing powders over it to stop the blood flow. Then return to your treatment until it is completed.
Then bind the wounded limb with a suitable ligament and care for it until it heals.
And I tell you what happened to a man on his foot, the same thing happening to him as I told you.
This is what happened to him, because his foot turned black due to a burn similar to fire burning it; the decay started with his toe and eventually spread throughout the entire foot.
Therefore, the man cut himself off from himself when he saw the decay spreading through his limb with great pain and burns; he cut himself at the joint, and healed.
And after a long time passed, the same decay occurred in the tip of his thumb on his own hand.
Therefore, he came to me and I tried to regain the loss with the remedy that I placed on his hand after cleansing his body; however, the loss did not stop, instead it spread to another finger, until decay started affecting his entire hand.
Therefore he called for me to cut off his hand; but I refused, hoping to cure the loss; and I also feared death for him during the cutting of his hand. Because the man was above his loss.
And since he had given up on me, he returned to his own land; and then he came back to me because he was afraid of dying and cut off his entire hand; and he healed.
And I did not bring this narrative except as an aid for that which falls under the genus of this illness; and to show what is signified by it, and according to how it should be done.
[Title] On caring for bladder stones and the quality of enema with medications.
When a boil occurs in some fleshy parts and the space of the boil extends until it makes collection of pus: then it bursts or is perforated and what is in it comes out as pus, and there remains an empty place like a vessel: and the skin that is above it has become thin like a cloth that has already been softened: and it does not reach the final corruption nor presses on bone, nerve, or ligament: it deserves to be called Sinus: and it is not called Fistula: however, if the space of it extends until corruption presses into one of these parts, then it is called Fistula, or ulcer.
And the care of this [fistula or sinus] is that you cut the entire skin as it is rolled up: and especially when it has become thin like a cloth: and trust that it will not adhere to the place because of its corruption.
If you hope that the skin will adhere and the ultimate corruption does not follow from this: and if there is a thickness in the skin due to flesh, then treat it with Clisterium: and it is to be considered as a sinus.
Then if it is large and the pus that is emitted from it has a foul odor: then clisterize it with a medicine from Egypt, which is vinegar, oil, and zinziber, parts receiving equal amounts, mixed together in a vessel: and boil it over fire, until the medicine turns red: and let it become thick like honey.
Then take from it whatever is necessary for you: and dissolve it with water and honey, and clisterize the sinus with it: and tie up its opening, and let the medicine remain in it for two hours.
Then remove it by pressing: do this for days until the sinus is purified and the foul smell is removed.
And at times, one cleanses with water and ashes when this medicine is not present to you; and it is to be known that you receive the ashes of vinewood or ashes from holm oaks; and you throw water upon it. Then wash her, and cleanse with it until you are confident that the sinus is already cleaned.
If the patient cannot bear Egyptian medicine or water and ashes, then cleanse him with water and honey, to which something from crushed wine lees has already been added. Or cleanse him with honey and wine mixed together, because the property of honey is to purify and cleanse; and wine makes the sinus adhere, especially when there is an excess of stiffness and dryness in the wine.
When you do that several times and are confident that the corruption of the sinus has been removed, then cleanse him with it which causes flesh to grow in it.
And it is to be known that you receive from the plaster diaphanicon; and you dissolve it with rose oil and stiptic wine; or cleanse him with certain medicines and other unguents whose properties I have written about in the treatise on ointments.
If the opening of the sinus is narrow and cannot take a cannula for cleansing; then expand it slightly with iron; or place linen wound around an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment inside it until it expands.
And similarly, if the opening is also wide, then bring together the edges with a suture; and allow the quantity of cleansing solution to enter it without addition.
And similarly, if the opening from which pus flows is elevated above; then cut it in a lower place within it so that the pus runs out below; because pus when obstructed in the depth of the sinus prevents flesh from growing in it.
If it is not possible for you to cut the bladder lower than you wish: then try, so that you prepare the member with a preparation by which pus runs out from it easily according to your preparation. Try not to retain anything from pus within it: and take the consolidating medicines that are placed upon the sign, suitable for what you wish. Spread them over a linen cloth. And let the cloth be of such quantity that there may be communication throughout the bladder. Then cut with scissors directly into the bladder opening, larger than the bladder opening by a little bit. Then spread ointments gently over another cloth, according to the size of the opening: and place it on top, at a distance from the bladder opening, in order to promote the outflow of pus from it: and do not remove the large cloth unless after several days, one by one.
He who is on top of the bladder opening, he is the one you remove at every hour, so that what collects in it from pus may come out: and know that, whether what flows out from it is much or little, digested or undigested.
And with this, again consider the place of the bladder itself, whether its master feels pain there or not, and whether there is an abscess there or not.
When your medicine is thus applied and you see the material that flows out from the bladder opening, then know that the bladder has already adhered or approaches adhesion: then dissolve it in the morning, or on the third day: and when you dissolve the wound, then change the cloth, and renew the ointment.
If pus flows out from the bladder after a long time with a subtle smell, then do not despair of its adhesion, for healing is approaching, since there are some people who slow down the regeneration of flesh in their wounds, and there are those who act contrary to this.
If however it comes out from the Sinus for many days as a putrid boil, then you shall know that the sinus is not adhered.
If the adhering sinus delays and its matter prolongs, then you shall add humid medicines with dry properties to it, as the doctors do; but they should be medicines that are moist in substance and dry in power, like dyafinicon ointment, when superfluous addition is added to it from zegi.
And from the last [part] that is treated, it is that you shall receive dyafinicon ointment, and let it be dissolved with rose oil, and rub over it aged wine equal in substance.
Then mix it with that and use it.
And now make one similar to this action, when you do not have dyafinicon ointment at hand, honey; when you boil it until it thickens, and use it. Or take myrrh, aloes, and olibanum; grind the whole thing and powder it over honey while it is on fire. Then lay a cloth over it and bind it to the sinus; and anoint with the honey you boiled until thickened, and powder its shape, and place it over the cloth and bind it.
And sometimes administered to him is long aristolochia, and the roots of celestial lily, and it is lily; and wheat flour, and knotgrass. Use them singly or combined, grind them and sift the powder; and sprinkle it over the honey I told you about, and use it.
If the matter of the sinus prolongs and does not heal with this treatment, then you shall know that there is corruption in its depth; or it has already made an impression on the bones or hard members or ligaments; then treat it with fistula cure, as mentioned before.
On the treatment of Panaritis and a worn nail, and the incision of a finger, and a section.
Aposteme which occurs under the nail of the thumb or big toe of the hand or foot; perhaps it also arises in other fingers.
When the matter of this (Panaritis) is prolonged and neglected, it becomes an aposteme that is treated with heat; it may rot and discharge pus until it corrodes the root of the nail; perhaps it rots completely, and the corruption reaches the bone, so that there is a foul smell; and the end of the finger becomes wide and darkens.
When you treat it (the affected part), and your treatment does not improve it: then it is necessary to cut with the iron the entire excess that remains from the nail. Cauterize the wound after that. For cautery is very beneficial.
If the bone is healthy and the nail also is healthy, and the hollow additions of the nail already press the flesh towards the inside and begin to pierce it and harm it: then it is necessary that you place subtle radium under the corner of the nail which pierces the flesh, and push it up: and cut the flesh easily, and place on top of what remains of the flesh from medicines burning, corrosive ones, until all of it is removed. Then heal it with ointments, until it heals.
If the corruption already presses on the bone, then it is necessary to cut that bone and extract it; for a corrupted bone never heals while it remains in there.
If you see corrosion and corruption advancing on the finger, then cut it at one joint, according to what was previously mentioned about its memory (anatomy). Then heal it, until it heals.
If there is wear or injury of the nail, and a violent pain occurs in it: then it is necessary to use leeches first. Then cut the nail with a sharp spatula cut crosswise from above to below.
And keep, so that the cut does not reach the flesh which is under the nail, for you will cause a very violent pain to occur above it, and it will be a cause for the growth of additional flesh in that place.
Then heal the place with what soothes the pains.
A finger which is born in some human hands, perhaps it is entirely fleshy; and perhaps there are bones in some of them, and perhaps there is a nail in it: and some of them are born at the joint of the root, or its birthplace is in some joints of the finger. He who is born in certain knots of the finger, is not moved; and he who is born near the junction of the finger, perhaps moves.
The flesh that grows from them is easily divided. It should be cut at its root with a broad spatula.
But the treatment of one born at the junction of the root is difficult. Therefore, refrain from cutting it.
However, in the one born on the finger at the end of the knots, then it is necessary to cut its flesh with a round incision up to the bone. Then saw the bone with one of those saws suitable for that. Then care for it until it heals.
The consolidation that happens between the fingers occurs frequently either from human birth, that is, being born with it, or from a wound consolidation, or burning by fire, and similar things.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut the consolidated part until the fingers return to their natural shape. Then place a cloth or linen soaked in rose oil between them to prevent them from consolidating quickly and separate them; or place a thin lead plate between them until the location is healed as needed.
And similarly, if consolidation happens with some fingers at the palm, then cut the consolidated part as needed and conform to the shape of the member.
Chapter on the defect in incisions.
The veins are twisted, thick, full of melancholic excesses that occur in various parts of the body; and most frequently they occur in the legs, especially those who travel and work hard, and those who carry heavy loads.
It is necessary that you administer the lancing of the body from black choler several times by a strong lancing.
Then, phlebotomy (bloodletting) of the patient's basilic vein.
The treatment (of these things) with iron (lancet), is according to two methods. One method is to score it (the affected area) and to draw out black blood. And another method is to elevate the Vein and extract it entirely.
The incision of this [vein] is according to this method. Irrigate the leg first with much hot water until the thick, foul blood dissolves. Then bind the weak leg from the upper part of the hip of that [leg], up to the lower part of the thigh with a bandage. Then cut the vein at one, or two, or three wide sections.
Then lift (eleua), that is, draw blood from the lower part of the leg towards the upper part, and it should first be done by the leech for the weak [patient]. Then cut the nail with what is below it (down to its base): until the quantity of blood that you see is sufficient, and what strength the weak [patient] can bear.
Then bind (it), and command him to abstain from foods that cause black bile; and repeat the evacuation and leeching when the veins are full, for it may harm the weak [patient].
The lifting (eleuatio) of this [vein] is according to this method. Scrape the weak leg if there are many hairs in it. Then immerse it [the leg] in a bath, or irrigate it in the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; or exercise it with strong movements if there is no bath present for him, until the limb becomes warm.
Then make an incision along the direction of the vein in length: or at the end [of the vein] near the knee, or at the lower part of it near the heel.
Then open the skin with the scalpel and scrape off the vein from all sides until it is felt: and at its appearance, it will turn from red to blackish-blue. When it comes from the skin, it appears white as if it were a cord.
Then insert the Radium under it until it is raised and comes out of the skin; suspend it with a blind hook, soft.
Then cut another section near that section with three fingers. Then peel the skin from above the vein until it appears. Then lift it up with the radii as you did before, and suspend it with another hook as you did at first.
Then cut another section or several sections if necessary for that one. Then peel it and cut the last section at the heel.
Then extract from the section above that one.
Do this until you extract it from the upper or highest section, or all sections until it comes out completely; then cut it.
If it does not obey you to be extracted and lifted; then insert a lancet with a strong thread twice, tie it and extract it yourself or insert the radii under it and turn your hand over all parts until it comes out. And be careful not to cut it. For if it is cut, it will become very difficult for you to lift it up and it may enter into the wound from that causing harm.
When you have extracted it completely; then place a linen cloth soaked in wine and rose oil or olive oil over the wound site and take care of it until it heals.
If the vein is contracted having a winding with coiling to parts and it is not as we said according to the straightness; then you should make an incision over all its winding parts and the sites of its coiling.
Then suspend it with hooks until you lift it up completely; and be careful at your incision site not to cut the vein or wound; for it will become very difficult for you to lift or extract it. Preserve therefore your prudence.
The method by which a vine is healed (or treated).
The shape of the blind man's (catheter) cup.
It is not narrow like other catheters nor has a sharp tip that would injure the vein; rather it is rounded and flexible because if it were too fine, it would pierce the vein with its fineness; on the contrary, it should have excess roundness, as we said.
On the extraction of a leg vein.
This vein is generated in the legs of warm lands, such as Alizegi and Arabia, and in dry, warm lands of little softness, that is, where no plant or tree grows.
And perhaps it is also generated in other parts of the body besides the legs.
And indeed its generation is from the putrefaction that occurs under the skin, such as happens within snake and ascaris worms, and worms generated between the skin and flesh.
And a sign of the beginning of this vein's occurrence is a violent inflammation in the leg. Then the area is blistered. Then the vein begins to come out from that blistered area, as if it were a root of a plant or an animal. This is followed by a series of further instructions on how to safely extract the vein, including using hot irons and cauterizing the surrounding tissue. The translation ends
When its end appears, then wrap a piece of lead weighing one keil dram around it, up to two and a half drams; and let the suspended lead hang from the leg. This is part of instructions on how to safely extract the vein by wrapping it with lead to prevent it from collapsing or breaking during the extraction process.
Whenever something comes out of it towards the exterior, wrap it in lead and tie it up. This instruction is likely meant to prevent infection during the extraction process by keeping the vein covered and contained. The translation ends here. If it extends too much, then cut off that part and turn up the remaining part. Do not cut it at the root before it has emerged completely. Because if you cut it, it contracts and enters into the flesh; it causes an abscess to appear, and pus at the site, and a bad ulcer.
Therefore, it should be treated gently and drawn out slowly until it has emerged entirely from its end, and nothing is left in the body from it: and this vein emerges from some humans that is as long as five palms and ten. And now it has come to me, because it has emerged from a man of twenty palms.
If it is cut during your treatment time: then insert a ray into its opening and pierce it with a long hole along with the body until everything that is in it from matter has been evacuated; and administer the rotting of the place with medicines for several days. Then cure it with treatment for abscesses.
This vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself; and holes occur in it, and a branch comes out from every hole.
Therefore, take care of it as we said in the division, and with what was mentioned earlier.
Section on worms generated under the skin, and this is called Bouina's disease.
This disease is called Bouina's disease in a certain land among us; because it often occurs in cows, and there is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh.
And it travels through the body, moving up and down; and it is detected by the senses during walking of a limb to another, until it bursts anywhere that it bursts on the skin, and comes out.
And its generation is from the corruption of certain humors. As it happens with worms and snakes, that is, earthworms and roundworms in the abdomen.
And feared from its malignancy. Because when it moves in the body and is raised to the head and reaches the place: then perhaps it opens there, and goes out, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Therefore, in order to cure it and remove it, this is not done except during its movement, and the perception of it by the senses.
Therefore, one should tighten what is above it and what is below it with a strong ligature. Then cut above it and remove it.
If it penetrates into the flesh, and you do not find it: then place a cautery over the spot with fire until it dies.
And what is feared more, is its corruption, which corrupts the eye, as we have said.
If, however, you see it already having reached the head near the eye, then tighten under it with a good ligature above the eyebrow. Then cut above it and remove it.
And the sick person should use cleanliness of his body, with medicines dissolving corrupting bad humors.
And let him avoid foods that cause corruption.
Chapter on the incision for the disease of Nakir.
This disease is called in our land Nakir; it is a pain that occurs in certain members, and then changes from member to member.
And I myself have seen this, as I am telling you. I was called to a sick woman in certain villages. And she extended her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
And when an hour had passed, I saw a swelling move with a rod, as a worm moves, quickly ascending to the man's shoulder: it was like living silver running from place to place.
Therefore, pain left that place and was fixed in the shoulder.
After an hour it ran through the rest of the body until it reached another arm.
Then he told me that it was rotating throughout its entire body, as I had seen.
Therefore, I was amazed at the swiftness of the change from limb to limb. And indeed, before that, I had never seen this sickness appear to my eyes in such a way. However, I saw many who found the pain change from limb to limb; and I did not see it with my own eyes as I did in a woman.
And I do not think that it was anything other than the fact that she was from those who are dry of body vessels; hence, this appears to indicate a windiness changed.
And it is necessary that it does not appear in those who are sweet-smelling and moist bodies of concealed veins.
Therefore, when you wish to cure it and the patient feels that pain; then if it is apparent to you, as we said, then press on it quickly and below it; cut above it until that windiness pressed out; and cauterize the place.
If however you do not see it with your eyes; then cure it by expelling the body and that which expels windiness; and crush them with foul pills and pills of myrrh and similar substances.
Chapter on Extraction of Arrows.
Arrows are differentiated according to their types and the places where they fall on the body.
However, the diversity of ears is as follows: because among them are those with large tips and small ones; and concave ones, and those without openings. And among them are those with three corners. And among them are those with tongues (projectile points). And among them are those with stars (points with multiple prongs).
But those which fall on the limbs, are according to two types. Or the limbs are hollow, like the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs. When therefore it falls in one of these members, and signs of death appear to you, which I tell you afterwards, then it is necessary that you devote extraction of that arrow from them, for death follows it in whom it is, in many dispositions. And when these signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not hidden deep within the member, then extract it, and take care of the wound.
From the signs of the brain when an arrow falls into it and penetrates a bone, and exits above the brain, are: since sudden headaches occur from this, and blindness, and dizziness, and redness in the eyes, and swelling, and redness of the tongue, and spasms, and confusion of intellect, and vomiting of cholera. And perhaps blood comes out from the nose, or ears. And perhaps speech is cut off, and the voice is destroyed. And moisture comes out from the wound's place, white like plaster. And it comes out of it resembling a meaty fluid.
If therefore these signs appear to you, then refrain from treatment, and extract the arrow if it does not come out by itself.
The signs of the arrow when it falls on the heart are: that it is close to the left nipple, and one feels as if it were fixed in a hard object, not in an empty one. And perhaps the arrow's movement is similar to a pulse movement, and black blood runs from the wound. And it follows that coldness of the limbs, and cold sweat, and fainting occur. Know therefore, that death is descending without doubt.
And the sign of an arrow wounding the lung is the exit of foamy blood from the wound, and the vessels that follow the neck are to be cut off, and the color of the sick is to be changed. And it exhales a large, deep breath and seeks attraction of cold air.
If an arrow falls into the lung, which is in the chest; then it is near to small ribs: and a great panting with intense pain, with sigh, occurs; and all limbs of shoulders move.
And if an arrow falls into the stomach, then perhaps something undigested comes out through the wound from food.
And if an arrow falls into the abdomen and pierces it: something of feces comes out through the wound, or pus, or an intestine that is already ruptured. Therefore there is no hope for his cure, nor for the removal of the arrow.
If an arrow falls into the bladder and passes urine: and something passes out from it to the outside, and the pain is stronger upon the sick; then you know that it is fatal.
Remaining members, such as the face, neck, throat, spatula, aid, dorsal spine, fork, hip, leg, and similar limbs are saved according to several arrangements: when the arrow does not hit an artery or a nerve; and the arrow is not venomous.
And I tell you what I have seen of these arrows, to indicate to you by that on your cure.
That is, because a man had an arrow fall into his eye socket near the root of his nose. Therefore I removed it myself from the other side, under the cheek of his ear; and he was cured, and no harm came to his eye.
I also removed another arrow from a Jew that had fallen on his eye under the lower eyelid; and the arrow was already hidden, and I did not get hold of it except for its small end, with which it adhered to its wood; and the arrow was large among arrows of Turkish bows, with soft iron, in which there are no ears.
The Jew has been healed, and no accidental evil has happened to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from the throat of a Christian.
The arrow was Arabic, and it belonged to those with ears [i.e., humans]. So I cut through him on top of two windpipes; and by now he was drowned within his throat. I was sharpened with that [instrument], until I extracted it; and the Christian was healed.
I extracted another arrow from a man who had fallen into his abdomen; and we thought he would die because of it.
After thirty days had passed and nothing changed in his condition, I made an incision over the arrow; I sharpened myself upon it and extracted it; and he was healed, and no accidental evil happened to him.
And I saw a man who had an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound was healed over it. After seven years it came out [of the body] from the root of his hipbone.
I saw a woman who had an arrow lodged in her abdomen, and the wound was healed over it; but the arrow remained within her, and nothing changed in her condition or caused her any harm in her natural operations.
I saw another man who had an arrow lodged in his face; the wound healed over it, and there was little pain for him; and similar things happened to many others.
I extracted an arrow from a nobleman of the King who had fallen into the middle of his nose and had already deviated slightly towards the right; but the entire arrow was hidden.
I was called to treat him after the fall of the arrow for three days. I found therefore a wound of an arrow very tightly closed.
I probed it with delicate tweezers and did not feel it: and himself he found a puncture and pain on his right side of the ear. I hoped therefore that it was this puncture from the tip of the arrow.
I applied a plaster to the place with a drawing ointment having an attracting and dissolving property, trusting that the spot would open and show me the sign of the arrow so that I might cut above it: and it did not happen at the place where it should have happened, showing that the arrow had passed through.
I stayed with the plaster over him for many days: and it did not happen as expected, and the wound hardened in the meantime: and he remained weak from the extraction of it for a space of many days, until he felt the arrow one day within his nose. And he told me that.
And he told me that. I placed over the wound medicine that was sharp and corrosive for many days until it opened: and when I probed it with delicate tweezers, I felt the fine tip of the arrow sticking to the wood.
Then I added to the opening of the wound with this sharp medicine until the tip of the arrow appeared clearly to us: and it passed me with that space of time about four months.
Then when the wound had swollen and it was possible for me to insert forceps into it, and move it, it did not obey to come out: then I did not stop probing, and devising on it with means of ingenuity, until I began one day with correctly made forceps according to the form that they will take at the end of the chapter, until I extracted it. Then I healed the wound.
And physicians indeed judge, that the nasal cartilage does not restore. I therefore restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient recovered with complete health; nothing at all harmed him.
And I tell you the quality of extraction of some arrows: that you may place that rule and meaning on what I did not say.
Because the parts and distinctions of this art are not comprehended with the narrative; nor does that book contain it, and a wise craftsman compares little with much; and with what is present, concerning what is absent; and finds a new operation, and a new instrument in the descent of foreign matters of this art when they occur.
Therefore I say that arrows do not exit from the members to which they are fixed, unless according to two modes. Or by attraction from the place from whence it entered. Or in reverse direction of another part.
And that which goes out from whence it entered is an arrow proceeding into a soft place; and it is attracted and exits.
If it does not obey for an exit from the hour at which it falls: then it is necessary that you leave it for some days, until the flesh which is around it rots away; and the attraction of it will cease, and its exit.
And similarly if it strikes a bone, and does not obey you for an exit, then leave it also for some days; and move it with attraction and motion every day until it comes out.
If it does not obey you for an exit after days, then it is necessary that you bore around the arrow in the bone on every side with a subtle chisel until the arrows swell. Then attract it and draw out the arrow.
If the arrow is already hidden within the body and concealed from sensation, then search for it with a probe. If you feel it (the arrow), then attract it using certain instruments suitable for the task.
If you cannot reach the arrow due to the constriction of the wound and the length of the arrow being deep; and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in that area: then pierce it (the arrow) and wait for the wound to expand so that it becomes possible to extract the arrow.
If there are ears that hold the arrow fast on all sides: then free the fixed flesh from them by any means you can; and if you cannot lift the flesh due to a fracture of the ears or twisting of them, wait until it breaks out.
And when you administer the extraction of the arrow in any location, then use the twisting of your hand with pliers for all parts; until it breaks out: and with great subtlety to avoid breaking the arrow, making its attraction difficult and the extraction itself.
If you cannot reach it (the arrow) for an hour: then leave it for some days until the things around it rot away. Then probe it again; for the wound will close itself, but if it causes blood flow contrary to you: then administer what I have said in its treatment in its chapter; and protect your strength from cutting a vein, nerve, or tendon.
And administer your art in every way possible to the removal of an arrow: and let it be with ease, calmness, slowness or firmness as I told you.
And it is necessary that when you pull out the arrow, it should be weakened according to the form (shape) by which it was lodged inside (the wound). Because it is more helpful (for the patient's recovery). If however, that is not possible for you, then administer what is possible according to shapes (arrowheads or arrows of different types).
The arrow that comes out from the opposite side of the other part or has already proceeded outwards, or makes a hump at the end of the arrow by a sensation on the upper part of the skin nearby, and you see it protruding: therefore, cut above it, and let the incision be according to the quantity that forceps can grasp in it.
Then pull it out: for it becomes easy to come out by itself.
If however it is retained in the bone, then turn your hand according to its roundness, until the arrow presses against the bone and widens itself: then pull it out.
And if it does not (come out): let it be for some days; then try again until it comes out.
If the shaft of the arrow is in it (the wound), then push it out with the shaft.
If however the shaft has fallen out, and you wish to administer a push: then insert an instrument with a hollow (concave) end into it so that it enters the concavity of the arrowhead; then push it out with the same (instrument).
If however the arrow is concave, then push it out with the instrument inserted into it. For the arrow will be loosened by that (method).
If the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to excavate all the flesh in which the poison is, if that is possible for you. Then care for her as is fitting until that point.
If an arrow is falling into the chest, or into the belly, or into the bladder, or into the side: and it is near by what you touch with the probe, and it can be cut through it: then cut through it, and be careful not to cut a vein, or a nerve, and pull it out.
Then suture the wound, if you see it, and care for it until it heals.
And this is the shape of the forceps with which arrows are pulled out.
The ends should be shaped like a bird's beak, made of iron: when they grasp the arrow, they do not let go of it.
And they are made in many shapes: large, small, and medium-sized, according to the size of the arrow, and its thinness, and the width of the wound, and its narrowness.
The shape of the impeller is concave.
And the shape of the impeller is deaf.
This is a deaf end like a radius, so that its entrance into the concave arrowhead is relieved, and it is driven with it.
Chapter on venous bleeding.
Veins for bleeding, whose custom has run in the body, are thirty.
In the head there are sixteen: two pulsating veins that are behind the ears, called two herbs; and two arteries, appearing in two temples; and two veins which are in the two tear ducts of both eyes, called "Aspicientes"; and a prepared vein in the middle of the forehead; and a vein at the end of the nose. And two jugular veins, which are in the neck. And two veins that are in the upper lip of the mouth. And two veins that are in the lower lip. And these are the veins called Algecherich. And two veins that are under the tongue.
However, the veins that are bled in arms are five in every arm.
One of them is Cephalic and it is from the forest side; and the common people call it vein of the head. And Fusca. And it is the middle vein, and it is composed of a branch of the basilica, and a branch of the cephalica; and they call it the vein of the body in common speech. And Basilica, and it is placed on the domestic side; and it is also called Titillicaris. And the common people call it the vein of the belly. And [it is] the arm vein, and it is placed on the fork: and this is where phlebotomy is performed, and this is that which appears above the thumb by a manifest protrusion.
And the little Saviour: and it is the vein which is between the anular and the cube [bone]: and there are to it two branches.
And in the leg and in the foot, there are three veins. One of them is that which is under the bend of the thumb from the side of the little finger. And the second is the saphenous vein: and its place is at the heel from the domestic side. And the vein of Nessus: and its place is at the heel from the side of the forest.
And in another leg, there are three veins similar to these.
Chapter on phlebotomy of two veins after the ears.
The phlebotomy of two veins which are after the ears, is helpful for old catarrhs, and hemiheadache, and scrofulas, and old sores on the head.
And the quality of [the procedure] is according to what I have said [before]. And it is, that the head of the sick person should be shaved: and the nape of his head should be rubbed in the place of two veins with a rough cloth rubbing good. Then the sick person should tighten his neck with a bandage until the two veins appear. And their places are behind the ears, in two depressed places of the head. So seek them with your finger, and where you feel their pulsations under your finger, mark that place with the branding iron.
Then take a phlebotomy knife, and this is called the Incisor. Then insert it under the vein into the flesh, until the phlebotomist reaches the bone. Then, extend your hand with the vein and skin towards above, and cut the vein with an incision that includes the skin. And let the length of the incision be the size of two joined fingers, or about that: and let out as much blood as you want.
Then, tie it with sutures and release it until it heals.
And now, the excision and cauterization of these (vessels) begins at the start of the book.
The phlebotomy of the two arteries which are in two times is helpful for an old hemigraine: and for a painful sciatica, and for a constant headache: and for the flow of superfluous fluids that are sharp towards the eyes.
And the quality of phlebotomy (phlebotomizing) them is as I tell you. Let the sick person tighten his neck much until two veins appear clearly to the sense through visible manifestation: and let the pulsation of them be shown under your finger. Then, (make) signs with the cauterizing iron.
Then, extend the skin above the vein towards above with your index finger and insert the lancet from below: and extend the vein towards above. Then, cut it as you did with two other veins: and let out blood according to your need.
Then, loosen the constriction of the sick person, and place your finger on the vein at the hour position. Then, place a linen cloth over it and sutures: and tie it tightly above with strong constriction: and release it until it heals.
And now, the reminder of them, and their excision, and their extraction begins at the start of the book.
Remedy for phlebotomy of the front vein is after phlebotomy in the head, for old facial diseases: and for migraine, and redness: and for foul ulcers.
And the quality of its phlebotomy is as I tell you. Tie the sick man's neck with a bandage until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "Fossorium".
Place the prominent tip at the end of the Fossorium on the vein and strike it with a peck or with another tool in that manner, and let the blood flow according to the amount you wish. Then dissolve the wound of the sick man and tie it until it heals.
And sometimes it opens with a wide phlebotomy. However, the phlebotomist should not be sharp-pointed as the other phlebotomists, rather it should be wide-mouthed. And the phlebotomy should be made across [the vein], since the bone is nearby; and perhaps the phlebotomist will break it when it is sharp.
Remedy for the two veins that are in the two tear ducts of both eyes is for an eye with a scab or redness: and for swelling in the eye, and facial diseases.
And the quality of its phlebotomy is that the sick man ties his neck with a bandage. Then phlebotomize them [the veins]: and you stand over his head.
And let phlebotomy be performed across [the vein], to a length less than usual, when phlebotomising little, incise slightly wider, for there is no flesh in that place. If one who phlebotomises is subtle at the end [of the vein], perhaps it will be broken.
Then make run out as much blood as it is necessary for you. And place a bandage over them, and tie them up at night, and loosen them.
The veins of the nose are phlebotomized to treat acute fever, and severe swelling, and diseases of the face, such as hemigraine and redness that occurs on the face; especially when it is old.
And the quality of its phlebotomy is that it tightens a weak neck [of a person]. Then hold the nose of that person with your left hand, and take a subtle, long lancet; and place it in the middle of the nasal cavity, between that which separates the nose according to its correct alignment. Because the vein does not appear to the sense there, and because blood begins to flow immediately.
And it is necessary that your hand be at the end with the lancet slightly; and make out as much blood as it is necessary for you. Then tie it up at night. For it recovers quickly itself.
The phlebotomy of the two veins in the back (of the head) has two beneficial effects: it helps to constrict coughing and the beginning of leprosy, and diseases of melancholy, and impetigo, and bad ulcers, and those that are corroding, i.e., herpetic sores or eruptions.
The quality of phlebotomy is that it binds the sick person under each neck with a ligature; and the craftsman should stand over the head of the sick, and the sick person should be sitting on a seat.
Then phlebotomy vein to the length of phlebotomy wide a little shorter. Then draw out an appropriate amount of blood, or according to what you see is necessary for that purpose. Then do the same with another vein.
Then release the ligature and bind two veins together tightly: so that the sick person does not faint. And let it be until morning. A wound heals.
Chapter on the veins of Albucasis. The veins of Algeberich are helpful for phlebotomy because they contribute to alcohol in the mouth and corruption of gums, and ulcers, and fissures in lips, and ulcers, even those that are in the nose and around it.
The quality of phlebotomy is that you should have the sick person sit before you: and bind his neck with a bandage. Then roll back his lip and look at two veins; one of which is on the right side of the lip, and the second on its left side: and the demonstration of each is evident through their blueness. And it is true that around them are small veins, black. Therefore cut both with an incision.
If there is doubt about you and you do not know which of them it is: then direct your attention to the larger incision, and that will be clearer.
And do the same with two veins that are in the upper lip; and it is most common to use this procedure: and cut the two veins in the lower lip.
On phlebotomy: vein under the tongue after cephalic phlebotomy. For the two veins that are under the tongue, phlebotomy is beneficial: it is because cephalic phlebotomy is for conditions in the throat and sickness of the windpipe, and sicknesses of the mouth.
And the quality of phlebotomizing them is that the sick person should be seated in front of you with his hand on the sun: and loosen his tongue, and look under the tongue on one side for a vein, and on the other side for another vein: and the color of both declines towards blackness.
Therefore, phlebotomize each one: and be careful not to injure your hand while phlebotomizing them. For under it are the arteries, and possibly there may be a flow of blood from these arteries.
The three veins that are phlebotomized in the elbow, these are the ones for whose phlebotomy there is a custom among all men.
And phlebotomy of them is done according to two modes. Or pricking with a broad phlebotome made of myrtle: or letting it open to the subtle point of decline: or cutting with a sharp phlebotome, and this is called Alnesil. And this is its form.
And from these there are wide and thin forms according to the width and tightness of the veins. The shape of the phlebotome made of myrtle should be wide, as you can see. And it fits for opening veins that are hollow, full, proceeding, appearing, thick, and those that contain thick, turbid blood.
And this phlebotome is of smaller width and more subtle in cutting.
It is appropriate for phlebotomy of subtle veins that contain delicate lemon-yellow blood.
Phlebotomy of the basilica is helpful for one of these three veins' phlebotomy. Because it drains blood from ailments that are under the throat and neck, following the chest and abdomen; therefore, the phlebotomist should be careful with it, since an artery is beneath it. If, however, the phlebotomist makes a mistake and adds in the puncture, he will cut the artery, and there will be blood flow. Therefore, the phlebotomist should not puncture it; rather, it should be cut by Alnesil.
If the basilica does not appear with a manifest appearance, then it is necessary that you exchange it for another or seek one of its branches; or you replace it with the vein of the arm, the phlebotomist. It is itself obvious and cut it when Anesil the phlebotomist does so, as we have said.
If, however, you wish to perform phlebotomy on this same one, then it is necessary before the tightening of the arm, that you touch the place, until you recognize the pulsed place. Then mark the place with a sign using hot wax, afterwards the arm; and cut the vein with a concave incision, the phlebotomist Alnesil, as we have said. And be careful that the puncture does not fall into the space from the location of the artery.
And when you see, as you tighten the bandage, an inflammation at the place that you have marked with hot wax; then that inflammation is inflation of the artery; therefore, avoid it.
If you see blood rise during phlebotomy, like the urine of a boy, and it is thin, red: then you will know that it is from the blood of an artery. Then draw back and place your finger over the spot at a distance, then remove your finger. If the blood is cut off (for it is often cut off), then bind the arm and let it be; let the weak one avoid moving it; and there should be fear of it.
And do not move it for a few days until it heals.
But if the blood does not flow off and binds you, and there is no medicine present at your moment, then cut the artery, if it appears to you. For its ends contract, and the blood flows off.
Or take the bark of a fig tree, cut it and take one half, bind it over the place where the vein is constricted with a string and bandages until another day.
Then if the blood flows off, it is good. And if it does not: then care for it with the remembrance of that place from where powder is removed to cause blood flow, and removal of the blood from that vein is not difficult in many positions due to the small size of the wound and the possibility of binding from the arm.
The phlebotomy of the Blue Vein is helpful because it draws blood from the upper part of the head and the lower body; therefore, since it is composed of a branch of Basilica and a branch of Cephalica, as we have said.
And it is fitting for the phlebotomist that it should be feared from its phlebotomy, because under it is a nerve. If a nerve is struck during phlebotomy puncture, and it causes fainting, the healing process becomes difficult, and perhaps it may not heal completely.
And this nerve appears to sensation often. If it is concealed in some individuals and is subtle and not evident: then you must place your lancet where that vein is, along with a small incision and avoid the nerve with all your strength.
If the vein is between two nerves, then find the vein along its length.
Chapter on the Vein of the Head. The assistance of phlebotomy for the Vein of the Head is because it draws blood from the head and contributes to eye ailments.
And it is proper in this vein that if you wish, the lancet should be anointed with olive oil or myrtle oil before pricking, because it is safer than all the veins, since it is not near an artery nor a nerve.
However, it is suitable for you in phlebotomy that you avoid the head and arm only, and seek a more comfortable location: and it does no harm if it is not found at the first prick, but you may return to it several times with the lancet.
However, perhaps an abscess may form in some individuals when it is not pricked at the first prick, but it does no harm to that abscess in any case.
Chapter on the Usefulness of Phlebotomy and the Cautions Observed in It. The nature and accidents of phlebotomy, which you must consider for its correction.
First of all, you should know that phlebotomy is not administered except in the conservation of health and its persistence, and with caution to avoid illnesses.
And it shall be done venesection on one of the three veins that are on the elbow, namely, Cephalica, Fusca, and Basilica. And it shall be done venesection at the beginning of Spring after fasting, in truth, and summer; in autumn, and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear.
Venesection shall be done on the first or third day, after three hours have passed from the previous day.
Venesection which is administered in diseases does not have a specific hour; but when the need and appropriateness for it arises, it can be done at night or day, and at any hour, and at any time.
It is not necessary to perform venesection on boys until they reach fourteen years of age. Venesection shall not be performed on pregnant women except from the fourth month up to the seventh. Venesection shall not be performed on the elderly who have already passed sixty years.
When someone wants to perform venesection for any reason, it is necessary to clean the intestines before venesection with a soft enema, if there is much fecal matter retained in them; so that during venesection, the veins are not attracted by putrid waste from the intestines harmful to the main organs.
Venesection shall not be performed on the patient who is intoxicated, that is, suffering from sickness of satiety or nausea; nor on one drunk or vomiting due to drunkenness until it has passed from them. Venesection shall not be performed on a patient with dropsy.
It should be avoided to perform venesection again after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, multiplication of coitus, labor, exercise, sleeplessness, fasting, or anything that dissolves the strength from the body or an animal.
Then consider in fineness of humors before that, if blood is thick with foods and drinks, and medications: if it is possible for him to do that.
Then enter the bath, unless it is forbidden by something: or exercise in some way, so that blood may be made more subtle.
And place phlebotomy on his chest, on the third day, as we have said: and endeavor that his chest is evacuated of all evils that day: such as pain, anger, fear: and of all bodily ailments, such as labor, punishment, excess, and similar things.
And let him have present the things that are used in custom among men from their fragrance, and scent, and joy, and similar things, according to the quantity possible for him.
Then let the phlebotomist sit on a stool higher than the stool for phlebotomy: afterwards he will draw out his arm and rub it with his hand two or three times. Then bind the ligature with a cord, and wind it around twice.
And let the ligature be moderated, because if the ligature is unequal or excessive in the ligature, then it prevents the flow of blood: or in softening, it also prevents the flow of blood.
Then after tying, it is necessary that the person being bled rub his hands together until the veins swell and are felt.
Then the phlebotomist cleans the puncture point with a little oil, an old one properly.
Then he shall place his index finger of the left hand on that vein at the place where he wants to make a puncture, slightly: so that the vein does not escape and the blow is not wasted. Because it is from the vein as you find it, similar to a fleeing cord, during phlebotomy; and from these there is what is full of windiness; and when you place the phlebotomy instrument upon it, it contracts under the phlebotomy instrument, and deceives the phlebotomator, and the phlebotomist does not open the vein; and if he opens it, it is tightened: therefore, for this reason, the phlebotomator should be firm, and careful in all these matters.
Draw or incise the phlebotomy instrument away from the vein. If the vein is opened by one cut, then it is good. And if not, then make another cut a little below or above the same place with haste; but if it is not possible to make another incision.
If it cannot be made another incision or the weak person faints, then leave him for a day, or two days; and do not tighten the bandage. Perhaps the abscess will attract heat. Do not enter the bath.
Then make another incision if necessary.
If the opening is small or blood runs subtly, then be afraid that not enough blood will come out; then make another incision in the same hole according to the straight line, and add a little more in the procedure.
And do this quickly before the abscess is removed, for the place of the abscess is in many people during small operations.
If you see that the abscess has already been removed, then do not go over it at all, for it does not cleanse anything in your hands. And put something of olive oil over it, because it eases the flow of blood. And it is better in this place than olive oil itself and other oils.
And similarly administer oil faeces in every phlebotomy of yours, where phlebotomies veins are against the prohibition of blood circulation; and they do this by Tyriac Albaharik, and sagzenea, when it is placed over one of them.
Blood is made subtle and dissolved, when it is thick.
If it happens in the place of phlebotomy a large abscess, for it often happens, especially to those who are not phlebotomists except at that time, or there is a small opening of vein; then hasten and put over the place a sponge soaked in water and salt, heated slightly; and tighten it for an hour, because it dissolves.
And it is necessary that you do this after the blood leaves from that vein itself, when its completion, or from another vein.
