If something remains in the place after several days of blackness or greenness, it does not hurt it; and if you wish, put over it something of aloe, or myrrh dissolved; or something from mint juice, that is, camphor or similar to it.
Often abscesses and protuberances happen at the phlebotomy of the Basilica.
Put then your hand over it; if you find softness under the pressure of your hand on it, then that protuberance is bad. Be careful to put over it something from what I said. For perhaps blood from an artery flows out of it.
But make a plaster to it with what is there for the swelling, so that the place becomes hardened. Then care for it with the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
And it is necessary that you draw blood from every man according to the amount of its virtue. And what appears due to a color prevailing over blood.
If the blood is black, then let it come out until it turns red; similarly, if you see it thick, let it go until it becomes subtle; and similarly, if it is sharp, let it be removed until its sharpness disappears.
It is necessary for him who is full, strong and in need of bloodletting with one vein to be amplified, and the bloodletter should be on the side; and it should be contrary for him who is weak.
It is necessary that it be drawn from the veins and that there be a narrow opening; and it is better that which is administered in bloodletting through the vein be a cross-section rather than a puncture.
This method of bloodletting is safe from the flow of blood and from the cutting of nerves; and it is more praiseworthy and safer than bloodletting through breadth and length.
And to whom this is accustomed to come upon bloodletting syncope, it is necessary that he eat before bloodletting with a little bread soaked in water of muscatel grapes or dried if heated; and draw out from his blood in three veins, or four.

Whoever wishes to amputate his arm and let out blood in the second [stage]: it is necessary for him whose phlebotomy is for evacuation of much, and the strength of whose phlebotomy is weak, to let out blood gradually by the quantity of strength in continuous days.
Whoever wants to amputate his arm and let out blood in the second [stage], and it is his body (i.e., he is doing it voluntarily): then he should do that after seven or nine hours from his first phlebotomy.
Whoever wants to draw blood from his body towards the opposite part that it flows to: it is necessary for him that it be let out on the second day or third day.
In whose body there is much blood already heated and sharpened, and causes a fever to come on: it is necessary for the blood to be let out in a single instance, and a large quantity drawn: and the opening should be widened until there occurs fainting: after you have observed all the conditions of phlebotomy: and so that you place your hand upon his pulse near the flow of blood, so that death does not occur from the fainting. For often it happens when the phlebotomist is unaware, and falls through carelessness.
And it is not necessary when you wish to amputate the arm and let out blood in the second [stage], if the opening of the vein is already closed, and the exit of blood becomes difficult, that you press on it violently and the area around it be quickly extended. For this is very bad indeed, rather let it alone until the second [stage of] phlebotomy.
Or remove with the sharpness of the phlebotomy that which has coagulated from blood in the vein opening, and place something dissolved salt in water on top of it. Place something made from turiyakh alfarokh or sagzena on top of it, and apply gentle pressure until the blood comes out.
If the vein has already been cut, then leave it alone, and do not cover it, until the boil settles down.

But if it is during the summer days, then you are excused from immersing your hand in hot water. Above all, the flow of blood into hot water is recommended during wintertime.
The venesection of this vein is healthier than all other veins because it is not a pulsating vein and there is no nerve under it.
Venesection of the Saluatella in the right hand is beneficial for liver diseases.
The manner of venesection is to tie a ligature around the thumb with a bandage or your hand, after you immerse it in hot water until the vein swells and becomes very sensitive. Then make an incision across the vein (phlebotomy). And if you cut it completely, it will not harm her in any way.

The remedy for the saphenous vein phlebotomy is for diseases that are in the lower part of the body such as female diseases (menstrual problems), kidney diseases, old sores on hips and legs, and similar diseases.

Therefore, perform the phlebotomy on a larger branch of it or near the heel in its cluster; because it is better and safer.

On Ventosection and its Quality of Use.
They are made from horns, copper, and glass.
Ventosection is indeed performed in two ways. With incision and bloodletting; and the other is ventosection without incision.
And this ventosection which is without incision, is performed in two ways. Or it is with fire. Or it is without fire.
And the places of ventosection which are administered with incision and bloodletting are fourteen on the body. One of them is Ventosection of Alnocrates, and it is the last on the head; Alkehel, and it is in the middle of the neck; ventosections of Alhagdahim, and they are two plates on the neck from both sides at once; ventosections of the brain, and it is under the jaw in the lower part of the mouth; ventosections of two spatulas; ventosection of Alachosos above the tail end; ventosections of two foci, and they are in the middle of two arms; ventosections of two legs; ventosections of two knees.
And ventosection does not draw blood from small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore its virtue does not fall out of them, as is the case with phlebotomy. It is not necessary that ventosection be administered either with fire or without it in any disease caused by congestion until the entire body is evacuated.
If necessity arises for ventosection due to disease or habit, it is administered at any hour during the beginning of the month, at its end, and in the middle, and at any time whatsoever.
That is, because there is one of men who, when multiplied within him the blood, until it needs drawing out through ventilation, finds in his head a swelling and sores.
And there is one of them who finds repletion and redness on his face, his head, and his neck. And there is one of them who finds itching on his face and forehead, and darkness and dullness in his eyes.
And there is one of them who scratches the place of his ventilation. And there is one of them whose laughter is multiplied. And there is one of them who finds the taste of blood in his mouth: or the tongue is spitted out and the blood is spat out. And there is one of them whose sleep is multiplied. And there is one of them who sees in his sleep blood and redness, and the dead, and wounds, and things similar to those.
When we therefore see something of these, and properly if it is in the third month: we command then ventilation to be made, after two or three hours have passed.
The remedy for ventilation of the neck is: because it brings about heaviness in the head, and what is expelled goes to the eyes. But it should be that this is after the evacuation of the whole body.
And this ventilation is in place of a cephalic phlebotomy.
And it should not be used by one who is of cold temperament, or in whom there is catarrh. Because it brings him great harm.
And for that reason it should not be used by the elderly, and in whose head there are cold diseases.
But he who does this frequently generates forgetfulness over him.
And therefore, you should instruct the Anesthetist to place his hand momentarily towards the lower part when letting go, fearing from forgetfulness due to generation.
Anesthesia or Alkehel, is in place of phlebotomy Fusca, and phlebotomy Basilica, and because of this it causes sneezing, constriction of breath, breathlessness of instruments, cough, and filling.
It is necessary that the anesthetist Alkehel should be pushed momentarily, because if it is placed lower, it generates weakness in the heart and stomach.
But anesthesia alhagdahim causes headaches, attacks, migraines, and perforation; and it is in place of phlebotomy Basilica.
And you should instruct the anesthetist not to press his hand during scarification; so as not to cut the artery and cause bleeding.
But anesthesia below the chin causes alcohol in the mouth, decay of the gums, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is instead of phlebotomy aleherich, which are on the two lips.
But anesthesia with spatulas causes toothache, which occurs from pressing and heating.
But anesthesia of the internal parts of two kidneys causes help for phlebotomy of three veins, Basilica, Fusca, and Cephalica; because it attracts blood from all those small veins that are in the flesh; and these small veins draw blood from larger veins until the attraction reaches to veins three.
And you should instruct the anesthetist not to proceed too far during scarification; because the area is exposed with flesh, and under it are nerves and arteries.
The ventosa that inflates over the alchausos is beneficial for hemorrhoids of the anus and lower ulcers.
And it is necessary to advise the Ventosator that the ventosa should be large and made of air: since the place requires strong suction and perhaps fine ventoses may break; and let it be cut with a deep incision.
The ventoses of the legs diminish by a manifest reduction: since they draw blood from the whole body and they contribute to ancient pains in kidneys, womb, and bladder; they provoke menstruation, and contribute to bloating and dropsy; and they are in place of phlebotomy of two saphenous veins and alhorcobeni.
However, they weaken the body much, and cause fainting in many men.
And the help of the ventoses for alhorcobeni is near the help of the ventoses of the two legs.
The quality of the positioning of the ventoses is that you should place the ventosa first in an empty place and perform a moderate suction; and do not prolong the position of the ventoses, but place them quickly and remove them quickly, so that the humors come to the place at equal speed: and do not stop repeating this and continuing until you see the place already redden and inflame, and the redness appears to be blood; then scarify, and repeat suction slowly. Then consider in the arrangement of bodies.
For if a man is of soft flesh and few pores, it is necessary to scarify him only once, not more, so that the place does not become ulcerated.
And advise the Ventosator to expand the scarification and make it shallow; and moderate the suction in ease, speed, and gentle motion.
If there is a swelling in the blood, then it is necessary to lance it twice. In the first instance, an opening is made for the subtlety of the blood and its thinning; in the second instance, a thorough examination is made for the extraction of the thickened blood.
If the blood is very impure, then lancing should be done a third time: to achieve the final result.
And finally, when we wish to extract blood gradually or in small amounts, a single lancing is sufficient for us. If we wish to make multiple extractions of the blood, we should perform multiple lancings.
And if we measure that the blood is thick, then it is necessary to perform a deep lancing; and the depth of the lancing, equal to the end, is the depth of the skin.
[Paragraph] What should be administered from the oils when in the position of the Ventosas (Venetians), and what one should avoid with the Ventosando.
In the case where the skin is thick, hard, dark, and its pores are constricted, it should be anointed with the Ventosas places using open, soothing, resolving oils: if it is during the summer season, as alkali oil, or olive oil, or oil from sweet almonds, or cucumber seed oil.
And if it is in winter time, then use oil of narcissus, or oil of lily, or oil of chamomile, or sulphur: and similar things.
If there is excessive fat that is cold, then use oil of amaracus, or oil of balm of Gilead, or oil of almond, or oil of dittany: and similar things.
If there is a windy discharge of large pores, soft flesh: then it should be prohibited from using oil, and the places of the windings should be washed with rose water, or cold water, or salt water, or water of squash, or water of purslane: and similar things.
But for him whose blood is abundant with moisture, wash the windings with vinegar, or water of myrtle, and sumac: and similar things.
For him whose excesses are thick, wash the windings with old wine, or sage water, or anise decoction, or chamomile: and similar things.
And it should be careful not to wash the windings in a bath, or in the foot of a bath, but rather it should be administered after leaving the bath for an hour, or for two hours.
And it is not good if anyone sleeps after washing.
What should be used to control the windy discharge, or the blood-letter before washing?
And after that, it should be considered first: if the patient is windy or blood-let, and his acuity and inflammation are choleric: then it should be given cooling things, such as grapes juice: also a bladder with vinegar and lettuce, and roasted onions, and yolk: and similar things.
Place his food before the chickens, and cook the mutton pieces, and set prepared food with herbs: and similar things for them.
If it is a cold complexion, let him drink syrup made from honey, or from almiua, or ale made from seeds; and let him drink moderately strong wine, which is between old and new; and let it be prescribed that he should eat sparingly. Place his food before the chickens and dogs; and let him have small birds, that is, little birds; and let the pigeon chicks be crushed.
It is necessary that the drink on the day of venesection and bloodletting should be more than food; and it must be given in certain men at hours tyriaca or alfaroch, or a medicine made from musk (muscata), or ale of elderberry (alesselithe) before venesection; and before or after: to strengthen the main limbs, and to make the blood subtile. And it is not necessary that they should drink it in a hot drink.
Chapter on venesection without scarification. Venesections without scarification are those which are applied on the liver, spleen, foot-affliction, and on the abdomen, umbilicus, places of kidneys, and on the ankle; because these limbs cannot endure scarification upon them.
And by these there is no search for anything, except that it draws blood from one limb to another; as we place the venesection on the breasts in the affliction of nosebleed. And we use them to dissolve the venosity of an unwanted cold in a limb; as we place the venesection on the abdomen and umbilicus. For it makes the limb rarefied, warms it up, and removes pain for this reason; because it has dissolved that venosity.
Also, it is placed on the kidney when there occurs an ulceration or stone in them. By virtue of its attracting power, perhaps it opens the ulcer, or expels the stone from its place.
Similarly, when it is placed on the liver and spleen for the treatment of windiness in both cases.
These are administered empty with a mere incision only. And sometimes they are administered with fire.
And sometimes they are administered with warm water in cases of pleurisy: this is to fill the Ventosa and make it large, only with warm water, or water in which certain suitable herbs have been boiled.
Form of the Ventosa administered with fire.
The diameter of its opening should be two fingers apart, as we have made it; and the depth should be half the size of a palm; and on its side there should be a small hole, according to the quantity that enters into it with an awl; it should be made of copper, tin, leather, or linen, equal thickness, cleansed; so as not to harm the body during its placement upon it; and in its middle there should be a crossbar transverse from copper or iron, where the candle is placed with fire.
And now it becomes this swollen one large, greater than we said before, and yet not much smaller than that (swelling), according to the illnesses and age of the one who uses it.
Swellings in children are different from swellings in men, and those of larger bodies.
The quality of placing this swollen one with fire on a limb is to ignite linen with fire from flax or a small candle from wax: and place it on the middle of the crossbar which is in the middle of the swelling: so that the fire may be kindled below the swelling, not to burn the body of the weak one.
Then it is to be placed on a limb, and the finger shall be on the hole which I said, as long as we hold the swelling: when we need it, we remove the finger, and the vapor comes out through that hole, and the swelling is immediately relieved.
Then linen with fire according to its manner, and repeat it if you need it.
In the swelling administered for the illness of pleurisy with water, there is no crossbar nor hole: it is not administered unless it is filled with water and placed on a limb only.
And this is its form.
And this swelling, the larger it is, so as to hold more water, is better.
Chapter on Suspension of Sanguisugums.
Sanguisugae are not administered in many places except where the position of swellings is not possible due to their smallness, such as the lips, gums, and similar parts. Or in a bare member, such as fingers or nose, and similar parts.
And the quality of using them is that you come from Sanguisugis which are in sweet waters, clean from putrefaction.
Then they should be let for day and night in sweet water until they are hungry, and nothing remains in their stomachs. The body is first evacuated with venesection, and with emetics. Then the sick limb should be washed until it turns red. They are then placed on top of it.
When they are filled and fall, and it is possible to suck the place with a syringe, then it is more helpful; if not, then clean the place with vinegar. Then it should be washed with much water, rubbed, and squeezed out.
If the course of blood is prolonged after bleeding from leeches, and it becomes draining; then soak a linen cloth in cold water, place it on top, until the drainage stops.
If there is an increase in blood, then sprinkle on it powdered alum, gall nuts, and similar things from the poppy; until the bleeding stops.
Or pieces of stripped beans can be placed on the place; and they are left until the beans stick to the place, for the blood is stopped.
And it is necessary that if leeches need to be repeated, when possible, to change them.
If leeches are forbidden from being hung up, then clean the place with fresh blood. Or stick a needle into the places until something comes out of the blood. Then they are placed, for when they feel something from the blood, they will stick immediately.
When you want them to fall, sprinkle something from powdered aloes, salt, or ashes over them; and they will fall immediately.
This chapter is also often necessary in the art of Medicine, and it is the restoration of a fracture, and dislocation of accidents in bones.
Know ye, O sons, that many foolish doctors and the ignorant boast of this chapter, and those who have never examined an ancient book nor read from it a letter.
And for this reason it happens that this method is lacking among the skilled [people] in our land. And I have not encountered it [the method] at all in good form, and I have not obtained it from it anything except what I obtained due to the length of reading ancient books and diligence over understanding them, until I extracted that knowledge from them.
Then I adhered by experience and diligent study throughout my life.
Now I have described to you from that [method] in this chapter all that my knowledge contains: and beyond what my experience has exceeded, after I have abbreviated it for you, and have freed it from the occupation of abbreviation, and have abbreviated it at the point of abbreviation, and have shown it at the point of declination: and I have formed many shapes from the forms of the instruments that are used in it, since it is by addition of declination, as I did in the two preceding chapters.
Title II.
It is necessary that we say in the prologue of this chapter the main points, and chapters, to which understanding is first required of the craftsman at his station over their truth: namely that you, and those ready for it, know or learn this noble art, and others from you.
I say therefore, that when a fracture, dislocation, twist or fall occurs to someone, then it is necessary, firstly, to hurry towards bleeding him and loosening him, or both at the same time: unless something forbids it, such as weakness of strength; or it happens to a child or an old weak person; or it is a time of intense heat or extreme cold.
Then let him be content with his food, cold vegetables, beans and heads; and forbid wine, heavy meats, and being filled with any food or anything that fills the veins with blood. Until he is safe from a hot fever and does not fear the outflow of matter to the limb; then let the sick one return first to his usual regimen with which his custom was accustomed.
When the fractured bone begins to heal, then it is necessary that the sick one eat nourishing foods in large quantities, thick, heavy, in which there is viscosity; such as food made from cooked wheat with water, rice, heads and feet, entrails of cows, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things. And with this regimen, the healing of the fracture is done more quickly and better.
And know that broken bones, when they are in men who are in the first old age and decrepit, it is not possible for them to be joined and consolidated according to their nature always, because of the drying of their limbs; and the bones which are from these are consolidated and united at the end of gentleness, like the bones of small children.
Nevertheless, nature connects something similar to glue around the broken bone from all sides, in which there is thickness, with which it adheres and tightens it until they are consolidated against each other, and tied together until it comes to the end of strength and firmness, as it was at first, until it does not forbid it something because of its operations; and because of this cause, it is necessary that you put the food of the sick in heavy foods, with thickness and viscosity, as we have said.
And know that the types of fractures are diverse, according to the differences of the limbs; since a fracture of the leg is different from a fracture of the head bone; and a fracture of the chest bone is different from a fracture of the backbone; and similarly all other members are different from each other; and I come with the reminder of all types of fractures exposed in their respective chapters distinct from one another. The species of fractures themselves are also diverse.
Since a fracture occurs curved, except when stars appear in it. And sometimes a fracture occurs along the length of the bone; and there are its splinters, that is, stars, and additions proceeding from them, as are found in a pen when it is sharpened for writing with a knife. And not proceeding; and there is a fracture with wound and rupture at the head; and there is a small fissure fracture.
And to each type there is a skill or specific tool for its restoration, according to which its memory will come, distinguished in their respective places.
And from that which is known about a bone fracture, it is its crookedness and prominence; its appearance to the senses; and its sound when you press it with your hand.
When therefore no crookedness appears in the place, nor does a sound occur to your touch when you press the bone with movement, nor does it cause great pain; then there is no fracture at that place, indeed it may be a crookedness or small fissure; therefore it is not necessary to move it with the hand and complete compression, but rather place medicines over it, whose memory comes after the time appropriate for the place; then a bandage is tightened with a fine string.
And know that when the place is bent and divided, except for what happens in it as satagiae, nevertheless remove all parts from their comparison: then it is necessary for you to begin from your hour for its correction, equating it before hot ulcer occurs.
If a hot ulcer occurs, then let it be for some days until the ulcer subsides. Then equal it according to whatever method is possible with gentleness and skill.
And know that the restoration of it and its equating is easier than bones, where satagia occurs.
Then tighten it, according to what comes to your recollection of it.
If satagia occurs in a bone, then extension of this broken member is necessary from two parts, if it is the hand or foot: or with your hand, if the member is small: or with two ropes, or with a rope and your hand.
And let your position be that in which you place the member over an equal place, according to its natural shape, until when the parts of the broken member extend: then try to make those additions with all skill and according to whatever method you can in their places: and take care according to your strength, so that pain does not occur to the weak due to your operation or injury: and try according to your strength to apply one of two bones with its partner, according to the best forms.
It is necessary at that time for you to test and touch it with your hand. If therefore you see something different there, correct it and equalize it according to the quantity of your strength.
And avoid a violent extension and a strong compression, as many foolish people do. For often they cause a hot ulcer or constriction in the member through their operation, as we have already seen from their operations many times.
Then attach after the incision, and proper surgical procedure, and the compression of that member, and peace, and calmness: and warn the sick person about it. And let him be careful not to move it during the hour of his watch, and sleep, at its revolution, and agitation, and at its discharge, and all movements during the last strength of his power. And let him be careful that the position of the member is not one that follows pain. This is because when he feels pain or injury in the position of the member, then it is necessary that he moves himself to another position from which he does not feel pain.
And be careful that his position is equal and straight: so that no curvature occurs in the member when it heals.
And the quality of the compression for a broken member is as I have said.
Know that fractured members differ according to their size, and their magnitude, and their shape.
Those that are small, such as the arm, finger, club, and similar to them, then it is necessary for there to be a soft, subtle wrapping of cloth. But those that are large, such as the thigh and leg, it is necessary for there to be a wide, firm wrapping of cloth.
Because a broad bandage connects a large member and compresses it from every side with equal compression so that no spot is left bare.
Then after your evacuation, place the suitable linen on it from the incision, on a soft cushion above the fracture site. Then begin to wrap the bandage over the fracture site three or four times, according to how deserving the member is: and compress your hand slightly with the bandage.
Then go with him to the upper part from the place of the break, and tie less than your previous binding, which you bound the broken place with. Then draw out a little further from the place of the break, and soften the binding slowly until you take a large amount from a healthy place.
Then take another plaster, and apply it again to the broken place with bandages. Then go downwards with the bandage towards the lower part from the break. And let your work be in binding and softening of the bandage, and in the manner as I said in the first bandaging above.
Then place between the bandages pieces of soft flax or cloth, equal to the curvature of the break if there is any curvature in it; and if not, do not put anything in it.
Then apply another plaster over it. Then place stars evenly spaced immediately above these bandages, if there is no swelling or hot abscess in that place.
But if there is swelling or an abscess there, then place that which sits on the abscess and remove the swelling; and let it be for several days. Then bind those stars over it.
And let the stars be made from the middle parts of thick reeds, shaved and skillfully formed; or let them be made of wood from which cribra are made, which are made from pine, yew, palm tree branches or calingi; and let the width of each star be according to this form and this same shape.
However, the star that is placed over the trace should be a little larger and wider than the other stars; and the length of the star should be according to what is allowed by the member in terms of size and smallness.
Then bind over the Star with another ointment, according to the first binding. Then bind firmly with threads, as we have said concerning binding; and it should be that your binding is stronger over the place of the break, and the farther it is from the break, the less the binding should be.
The threads must be of moderate thickness and fineness, and made of soft linen.
Since if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the operation of fools placing their own twisted cords of rough linen, it is a great error; since the binding falls off with them beyond quality.
And thin threads again do not suit; because you will not achieve with them through the binding what you want.
It is not necessary that there be less than a finger's breadth between one star and another.
If the sick person is hurt by the extremities of the stars after binding in healthy places: then place under them soft wool or camlet, until nothing is hurt from that.
But when there is a break with a wound, and rupture occurs in the skin, I will come back to it with its own discussion in the second chapter.
And know that not every broken member needs to be bound with stars from the first day. That is because when a member is large, it is not necessary to place stars on top of it unless after five days, or seven, or more, according to your safety from the occurrence of cold abscess.
And this is the method of plasters that the ancients used, which are placed on a break and displacement.
The common method of plaster, restoring a break, suitable for many constitutions, especially women and children; since it is from that which heat does not overcome nor cold.
And it is that you receive from mill-dust, and it is the marrow of flour which hangs on the walls of the mill near the movement of the millstone: and you shall make it as such, except that sieves it with egg white: and place its mixture not thick, nor subtle. Then use it.
Another method of plaster, for the healing of a fracture, dislocation and twisting. Take almess, laudanum, acacia, enula and mugath: and macerate all with ten parts of myrrh, five parts of both aloes and twenty parts of alethil. All should be crushed and sifted, and mixed with water of alethil, or with egg white if the plaster is applied to a weak person who is heated. Then use this plaster. For it is a good composition, it quickly heals broken bones and helps many people.
Another method of plaster, which also helps for fractures and twisting. Take mugath, mess, white alteae, all with ten parts of myrrh, five parts of both aloes and six parts of acacia, a pound of Armenian bolus twenty times, all should be crushed and sifted, and made with water or egg white: and administer them.
Another method of plaster for joining bones and those separated from their places: it soothes the pain that occurs to them, and the separation of a bone, and a fracture. Wool juice is taken, and it is immersed in vinegar and boiled oil: and it is placed on the place.
And indeed, this plaster does not have the virtue of healing, but it is good for the soothing of a hot boil: and it expels pains properly.
Method for applying a plaster, which restores a broken bone. Take leaves of the fig tree that is deaf and leaves of wild parsnip: grind all of them, and make a plaster from both.
Method for a speedy application of a plaster for the restoration of a broken bone, and when you want to dissolve the remnants of an abscess. Take equal parts of the root of althea, chamomile, marigold flowers, herb flour, all in one part: grind all of them, and make a decoction with wine if the member is not heated.
If it is heated, then make it with coriander water or with water and use it.
Another method for a stronger plaster in the resolution, stronger than the first, when a hard abscess occurs during the restoration of a member. Take equal parts of the root of althea, flax seeds, boxwood, licorice root, sampsucke, marigold flowers, chamomile, all in one part: grind all of them and make a decoction with willow water or sweet water or wine. Apply it according to the heat of the member and the calmness of its warmth.
Hippocrates himself did not say in his book that anything should be placed on a broken member during its restoration except a preparation made from wax and oil; nothing else. And he said it should be of a medium between thickness and subtlety.
Galenus, however, thought that things should be placed on a broken member during its restoration which have the heating property, such as myrrh and aloe and frankincense, and similar things from those mentioned before.
Method for a plaster that promotes injury and pain. Make a paste of equal parts of ground chickpea, human hair or goose feather, and althea (marshmallow root), along with salt: grind and sift it; then make an ointment from this mixture.
The amount required to make the bandage remain in place is such that if there is no pain or itching, nor does the bone move from its place, then do not dissolve it for many days. If itchiness, distressing pain, or swelling occurs at the site, then hasten and dissolve it within an hour, remove the ointment from there; take a soft cloth or seawater sponge, moistened; immerse it in warm water and wash the area until the itch subsides and the pain is alleviated.
If itchiness, distressing pain, or swelling occurs at the site, then hasten and dissolve it within an hour, remove the ointment from there; take a soft cloth or seawater sponge, moistened; immerse it in warm water and wash the area until the itch subsides and the pain is alleviated. Then let the limb rest for an hour. Then place on it (the limb) wool soaked in vinegar and oil, or rose oil; tie it over it at night until you are free from the danger of hot infection, and let the swelling of the limb subside and the pain be alleviated.
Then repeat the same process for a delicate binding and a small amount of ointment; do not bind it tightly with your first bandage or with a delicate one until it is healed.
If you see that the abscess, redness, pain, swelling and all other symptoms have been completely removed, and you require an ointment and binding, then repeat the same procedure as before equally.
If nothing of what was mentioned happens to the limb, then do not dissolve it before three days, or four, or five, or seven. And when it is permitted after twenty days according to the appearance of the dissolution of the limb, as we have said, until the fracture adheres and the coagulation of the flesh near it; add also more binding in your bandage than your first one completely; and also increase the intake of food for the sick person, as much as the memory of the previous advice suggests.
If you see that the place of fracture is already drying out and shrinking too much: then you will know that nourishment is prevented from reaching it. Therefore, anoint the area with warm oil and water at every spot where you dissolve it, and let it be for all three days, and apply a little softening agent to relax it slightly.
By this procedure, nourishment flows to the member, and it heals quickly.
What foolish restorers do instead of restoring the fractured member by what is proper, when they do not restore it first as required, and restore it according to its curvature, is an error in their procedure, and there is great fear: and if it were correct, the ancients would have said so in their books, and they would have operated with it.
And I have not seen any trace of theirs whatsoever in that matter, and it is better not to do that.
Chapter on the making of a fracture in the head.
Types of fractures are diverse, and their shapes are numerous; causes of the same are distinguished.
For the fracture that occurs from a blow with a sword: the blow removes the bone completely until it reaches the siphac, which is below the bone, just as an ax cuts through wood: and for this reason, the species of fracture is called Axial.
Or the sword cuts something of the bone and cuts its face, but does not penetrate through to the end of it: and this type of fracture is called Kalan, that is, Absolute Lever.
And a wound from two types of fractures, either great or small.
And the fracture that is crushing or grinding: and its cause is a blow with a stone or falling on a stone, or similar things.
This fracture is also penetrating, which is approaching the padding that is under bone: or it is on the face of the bone: and this wound belongs to these two kinds of fractures, whether small or large.
This fracture is hidden within the bone in the subtlety of hair: and it is a small crack, for which reason this type of fracture is named Capillary Fracture.
Among these [types of fractures] is a fracture that occurs due to an accident or being struck by a stone, and these cause the bone layer to enter into the interior, forming a hollow: as it happens with the crucibles of metal, when they are struck and a part of them enters into the interior.
This is most often found in the moist bones of the head, such as those of children.
All these kinds of fractures are set separately, and I will return with the explanation of this [entire matter] in its proper place.
We know all these kinds of fractures through examination of it, and investigation of them with probes, and removal of the corrupted flesh that is over them.
The Capillary type is known through this: that it is revealed on the bone, scraped, and lined up on top of it with pitch: for the fracture appears black.
In the treatment of a fracture, first consider the condition of the patient: then if you see signs from his condition that indicate fearfulness, such as vomiting cholera, extension, loss of intellect, loss of voice, fainting, acute fever, eye problems, redness of eyes and similar signs in many other conditions, without a doubt it will not heal: and if you see the patient's conditions are not terrifying to you, and hope for recovery: then begin its treatment.
If a wounded person comes to you in the first instance and is wounded: and it happens during winter days, then it is necessary that you study bone excision before the fourteenth day according to every arrangement.
If it is during the summer days, then it is necessary that you hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, before it becomes rotten under the bone from the tissue, and such accidents occur as we have mentioned.
If the bone fracture has already reached the tissue touching the brain and is accompanied by pieces and pulling: then it is necessary that you cut the broken and smoothed parts according to what I have told you.
It is necessary that you shave the head of the wounded person and scrape over the bone as much as possible for you, according to the shape of the wound and what is light over the weak.
If it happens to you during the scraping of the bone a flow of blood or a hot abscess: then put what is necessary against it. And it is necessary that you fill the place with soaked cloths in wine and rose oil, and let the wound rest until the abscess settles, and be secure from blood flow. Then begin the healing of the bone, and the removal of it.
And this is done according to one of two methods.
The first method is to cut the bone with a knife having a narrow blade: and this is its form.
And administer another knife wider than the previous one a little: and this is its form.
Then also administer another knife even wider than the second one.
And the second method is that there should be a number of knives of different sizes among you; some of which are wider than others and some shorter than others: and they should be at the end of sharpness extremities, and made of Indian iron or copper, and use them with ease in striking the knife so as not to strike the head and hurt it.
If the bone is hard and tough: then it is necessary that you perforate around its circumference before you administer Incisoria, with Terebris which are called Terebra not penetrating deeply; and they are not so named except because they do not pass through the bone's flesh to what is beyond it; therefore, because the Terebra has a rounded end above that which is beneath its head, and a small circle prevents submerging, and passing through the bone's thickness.
And it is necessary for you to take a great number of these Terebris, one of which suits the thickness of the bone, until there is for you all the Terebra that fits the skull; whose sharp end's size in length and width should be according to the thickness of the skull.
And this is the form of three kinds of Terebris or Trepans.
The quality of perforating the bone's circumference after it is broken, is that you place the Terebra on the bone and rotate it with your fingers until you know that the bone has already been penetrated. Then change the position of the Terebra to another place, and put in its place what is equal to the size of a finger or approximately that.
Then cut with Incisoria what is between every hole in the bone; and do it more delicately than you can on the top of it, as we have said, until you excavate the bone, either with your hand or with some other tools which you have prepared for that purpose: such as tenaliae and delicate forpices.
And you must be careful with all caution, lest the Terebra or any Incisoria touch something from the skull.
When you perforate the bone and it has been separated from the skull, if it is continuous with it and you extract it, then it is necessary to scrape and make equal the end that remains in the bone with another tool similar to an Incisoria. It is necessary that it be thin and delicate more than other incisors.
If something remains of the small bones and cartilage, then take it with ease, along with what is at hand from your instruments. Then care for the wound after that with linen cloths and unguents as we said before.
Another method of operation is easy, completely distant from fear; which Galen said and praised greatly; and this is his saying. First, you must begin to expose the bone piece from the place where the fracture is more violent and clear; until when you have exposed that part and placed under it the end of this concave incisor, which has this form.
The concave part does not cut anything; and the sharp part of it facing in both directions along its length, as you see; so that the concave part is attached to the bone, with the sharp part incident on the bone.
Then strike on the incisor from one side with a small hammer, until you cut the whole bone with ease, as it is turned; and be careful that no cloth (panniculo) from you happens to fall into what is happening, which you fear completely.
And if the physician were not more foolish than men and ignorant of this, nor was he sleeping, then if something remained attached to the bone from the cloths in some places, he would cut it off with the end of the concave incisor itself and release it easily. It is released from it without harm and without fear.
If the bone fracture does not penetrate to the cloth, and what is cut off from the bone is its face, and roughness and delicate cartilage remain in it; then it is necessary that you grind down the roughness, and dig out the delicate cartilages with fine rasps, which you have prepared of various sizes, so that it is possible for you to apply them more suitable and correct ones in every place according to what leads you the operation, and the fractured bone itself, and its shape. It is necessary that you administer [the operation] according to your own judgment, firstly cutting the bone, more widely than those who scrape it off. Then use a finer tool after that.
It is necessary that you administer [the operation] according to your own judgment, firstly cutting the bone, more widely than those who scrape it off. Then use a finer tool after that. And do not stop doing it continuously until you reach the point of administering it more thinly and finer than all of them.
In every one of the remaining small fissures and a fine fracture, it is necessary to administer care, according to that which leads to its correction.
And there is a matter that does not hide over all, to whomever has any interest in this art, and it stands on what we have written and shown in large fractures.
If a membrane is found to be retained when you remove the bone: then it is necessary that you take linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and immerse it in rose oil, and place it over the opening of the wound. Then take another doubled or tripled cloth, immerse it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth: and do that as easily as possible on top of it, so that it is not burdened by moisture.
Then administer a broad ligament over it: and do not tighten it, unless for the amount that holds the wound only: and release it with this care for one day or two days, until you are certain about the hot inflammation. Then dissolve it, and administer afterwards medicines with which excess dryness is needed: such as the roots of garlic, and wheat flour, and frankincense powder, and aristolochia, and similar things: and there is, that you make from these medicines a powder, which is dusted over the wound like dry ones.
And universally administer all medicine in it of the nature that cleans and does not bite. "And be careful according to your virtue, so that the wound may be clean during your treatment: there should not be dirt from ointment, nor dirtiness.
"And be careful according to your virtue, so that the wound may be clean during your treatment: there should not be dirt from ointment, nor dirtiness. "Do not allow pus to accumulate at all: since when pus accumulates on the brain tissue, it corrodes and rots it, causing great harm to the sick person afterwards; and this has already happened with the skull, when the bone is being cleaned by him, especially when care for it is neglected. A blackness appears on its surface.
"Therefore, if the conditions that I mentioned occur in the sick person, know that it is surely fatal.
"And if blackness does not occur, except from the medicine applied to him and it is effective in its action so that it makes this blackness: then one should take a portion of honey, three portions of rose oil, and anoint with them a cloth. "Then place it on the skull; afterwards take care of him with the means of healing that are appropriate, until he is healed.
"On the restoration of a broken nose.
"Know that the nose is not broken except when both of its upper parts are broken at once or only one of them: because it consists of two bones; since below it is cartilaginous and does not break, but only becomes bruised, distorted, and crooked.
"If one of the two parts is broken, then one should insert a small finger into the nose and push the fracture back with the index and thumb to its normal shape; this should be done skillfully. "And be careful that pain does not occur in the sick person during your operation.
If the fracture is in the upper part of the nose and does not reach it with the finger: then, it is necessary to align the extremity of the radius, where there should be a small swelling.
If the fracture is in two parts, then make it similar to that one: and bring together with its restoration on the first day of the fracture, if possible. And if not, then after the seventh or tenth day, at rest with the cauterization of warm lard.
Then insert a piece of flax from linen cloth into the end of the nose if the fracture is in one part: or insert two pieces of flax if the fracture is in two parts: and let there be a swelling on the flax of such size that it fills the nostril opening.
And some of the old restorers said, that the flax should be soaked in butter and changed every day. But this does not seem to me, rather it is necessary that the flax should be soaked in egg white, made with flour mill powder. Then release the flax when the bone hardens and the cartilage hardens.
And sometimes a feather of the goose is inserted into the nose in place of flax after it has been covered with soft cloth: and this makes it so that the feather holds the fracture of the nose more firmly, and so as not to prevent the weak from breathing.
And this is not necessary. If you want, do it: if you want, do it with flax.
If the nose again forms an abscess while treating it with warm cautery, apply a nasal plaster with pitch, or with pitch soaked in rose oil, or a little with balsam of Mecca.
But if no abscess forms with the warm cautery, then it is necessary to apply plasters made of sesame flour and incense powder mixed with egg white. Then place a soft cloth upon it (the wound), and do not tie the nose with anything at all.
If however the nasal bones are broken or crushed, then it is necessary that you make an incision over them and extract them with instruments suitable for the purpose. Then apply a suture and take care of it with that which causes it to heal, using ointments or plasters suitable for the purpose.
If a wound occurs between the nose, then it is necessary that you treat it with linen and administer a lead cannula until it heals.
Chapter on the restoration of the lower jaw when it is fractured.
When the lower jaw is fractured and the fracture is not accompanied by a wound: then observe whether the fracture is only on the outside and is not broken into two pieces, and bends inward: then its diagnosis is easy.
Therefore, if the fracture is on the right side, insert your left index finger into the weak jaw: similarly, if the fracture is in the left lower jaw, then insert your right index finger: and press with it the protrusion of the fracture from inside to outside with ease using your other hand from the inner part of the bone correctly, and equalize it.
If the fracture of the lower jaw has already separated into two pieces, then administer traction from both sides according to straightness: until it is possible to equalize it.
If however a loosening or displacement of the teeth has already occurred, then tie them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk. Then place a soft cushion on the fractured lower jaw. Then place a double cloth on the fractured lower jaw, and place over it a large star-shaped cushion made properly: or an equal piece of skin from a sandal in length to the jaw bone.
Then bind it up from above, according to how you prepare its ligature, and let it rest until it is healed: and instruct the patient to be at peace and rest: and put for his food softened meals.
If however you think that something is changing in the figure by any means: then be quick, and dissolve it on the third day. Then correct whatever has been changed from it, and apply plaster made of milled flour with egg white, or with sifted wheat flour, after you have removed the scabs: and place soft wool on top of the plaster.
While that plaster remains attached to it and the bone arrangement does not change, let it be, without removing it, until it is healed: or bind the fracture. This fracture is bound many times in three weeks.
If however a warm abscess occurs in the meantime: then administer what I said many times for its reduction, until the abscess is removed.
And if the fracture is with a wound, consider it. For if a piece of bone is separated, or from a sawing: then be subtle in this, to remove those pieces of sawing with what suits you for the removal of them from the instruments.
If however the wound opening is narrow: then enlarge it with a leech according to your needs.
Then when you remove the sawing, and nothing remains of them: or if the wound opening is wide: and if not, place on it from plasters that suit for this, and let it heal until it is healed.
Chapter on the restoration of a Fork, when it breaks.
The fork is broken most often from the front part from the shoulder, and its fracture is made according to one of three modes.
For it is broken and separated into two, except that there occur in it suppurations: and it is more easily restored to its state.
For such as occur in the bone, suppurations: and it is more difficult to restore.
For such as is a fracture with a wound.
And the operation in it when there is a fracture without a wound, is that you make two assistants present, one of whom holds the splintered furcula, and the other stretches the neck towards the opposite side.
Then equalize the fracture with your fingers until its form is made, according to what is required: and let there be neither prominence nor hollowing in it.
If you need more extension, then it is necessary that you place under the neck of the weak one a sphere made from cloth or wool: and let its size be according to your need: and stretch, lift, and squeeze the sphere with your hand until you equalize the fracture, according to what is required.
If you cannot pull the end of the furcula outwards because it has reached deep: then it is necessary that the weak one lies down on his neck: and place under his shoulder a beam in size, and press the minister under his arm towards the lower part, until the bone of the furcula which is deep is lifted upwards: and then correct the fracture, and equalize it with your fingers.
If, however, you feel a suppuration from the furcula and it moves: then it is necessary that you make an incision over it, and extract the suppuration easily.
If it remains in the bone, then make a handle on the incision of it with one of the Incisorium which you have prepared for that purpose, after you place under the furcula an instrument which saves the saw: and it is an instrument made from wood or iron. This is its form.
It resembles a snail shell without a concavity.
And let its width be according to the need of that bone's size and proportions. The length of it as much as possible for your operation.
And have two extremities, as you see; and one extremity be wide, and the other narrow.
If the wound rupture which you split when extracting satheiatum bone is wide, and your cauterizing iron is hot, then gather two lips of the wound with suture.
And if the rupture is small, or fear hot cauterizing iron; then fill the wound with cloths and wool, according to the amount of the wound's cut.
If it happens that hot cauterizing iron occurs, then pour oil of roses on the cloth, vinegar, and wine, and place it on top of it.
But the fixation of bone without a wound and without cutting is, to place plaster on the bone made from flour milled with egg white. And put soft wool on top of it. Then place a sphere under the wound if it is needed. Then take a leech, that is, the roll which the Saracens hold, which is very long; and its width should be as wide as one palm, or approximately that. Then place a double piece of wool on top of the soft wool and plaster. Then take a needle from fine wood, whose width is three fingers, and similarly in length. Then thread the needle with cloth. Then thread the cloth with the needle in the place of the leech which falls on the fracture and the wound. Then place the leech on the fracture as it is rolled, and thread it over its neck, and under the healthy wound, and under the sick wound; and return it over all parts, and so that the fixation holds the fracture properly; and this is what must not be hidden from you, and completely, so that the needle does not move over the broken bone. It is necessary to observe the sick person every day. Whenever the ligament becomes soft and you see the knot being removed, then correct it and tighten the ligament.
Then place the sick man's sleep on his back and place a small pill under his pillow at night so that when he wakes up, his aid may be raised from his side. Therefore, raise the fracture of the collarbone by elevating the shoulder.
Either bind his arm to his neck and do not loosen the bandage unless it happens in a place that is swollen due to itching or from an abscess, for twelve days.
Then renew the plaster if you see his face turning towards it. And add to the constriction and release it until it is restored and healed.
The fracture of the collarbone is bound and supported for up to twenty days; it may be less in some people.
Chapter on the restoration of the Fractured Spatula (Scapula).
The scapula rarely breaks in a wide place; it does not break except at its edges.
When it breaks from there, and breaks in the middle of it, and it is not known unless by touch, then make the preparation according to the shape of the fracture. And reduce it to its natural shape in every way possible for you.
Then place flour of milling with egg white and soft wool over it and put a pillow made of double cloth on top. Then place the wide knot under it from a thin board according to the size of the scapula or larger but not too much.
If there is a concavity under the knot at some place on the scapula, then fill it with soft wool until the knot descends to the same level.
Then apply a tourniquet above with sufficient tightness and firmness, until it is no longer moved from its place.
And consider the bandage daily. Whenever therefore the bandage becomes soft, tighten it, and equalize the pressure if it is moved from its place: let the weak side lie upon the healthy one.
The spatula is restored in twenty or thirty days.
When this number is completed, then loosen the bandage: and be safe. For it is from bones whose fracture is not feared nor their separation.
If however it protrudes from the bone and punctures under the skin: then cut above it, and remove it. And do as I have said in the treatment of a fracture of the neck of the femur by hot poultice, if anything occurs from it.
Chapter on the restoration of a breastbone fracture.
The chest is sometimes broken in the middle, and this happens rarely. However, its extremities are broken and crushed more frequently due to accidents of it.
When the middle of it is broken, which inclines towards the lower part, and a violent pain occurs in it, and difficulty in breathing, and coughing; and perhaps blood vomiting occurs, and the hollow in the fractured bone is evident to the sense, and not covered: the restoration of this is that the weak side lies upon its back: and place between its spatulas a cushion.
Then press the shoulders and join the ribs from both sides or flanks with hands: and grind it evenly, according to every way in which this can be done and fits together, until the figure of the bone returns, as required.
Then place on top of it an ointment and a powder, and place on top of that a thin star-shaped piece made from willow or boxwood, or similar materials, after you have rolled it up in a cloth. Then wrap it around the broken bone, so that it is not removed: and go with the bandage following the roundness to the back several times, and bind it tightly enough.
Then consider the bandage at every hour and whenever it becomes soft, tighten it; and if its necessity causes it to dissolve due to itching or corrosion that occurs in the place, or pain, or abscess: then hurry, and loosen it, remove the ointment, and correct what happened with the treatment method.
Then reduce the ointment if you see it going to that face; and join a tight bandage until healed.
Chapter on Restoring Costal Bones, when they break.
Know that a costal bone fracture does not occur except in large areas that follow the back and from their extremities on the front side. And it is not caused by friction, unless because they are cartilaginous. And the detection of this is not concealed from touch during examination with fingers.
And the restoration of this is done so that the break can be aligned with fingers to the best possible extent until it matches the shape as required. Then apply an ointment and bind the broken bone with a star-shaped piece if necessary.
If the costal bone fracture is towards the interior: then it causes a strong painful sensation, and puncture, like the puncture that occurs in pleurisy; because the bone pierces the membrane, and also there is difficulty breathing, and coughing, and vomiting of blood many times; this is difficult to treat.
And the ancients have already devised that remedy with many devices: and among them are those who say to put foods for the sick which generate inflammation and gas, so that the stomach is inflamed, and it is stretched and driven outward in order to heal a fracture from outside.
We reject, that it should not be caused quickly to make a hot abscess, unless it happens. If it has already happened, then add it (the treatment) into it (the wound).
And some of them said: place a windy substance on the place, then apply suction with force, and it is similar to reasoning. However, there is fear that windy substances will attract excess into the place, due to its weakened condition.
And some of them said: the place should be covered with wool which has already been soaked in hot oil: and lice (puluilli) should be placed between the ribs until it is filled: so that the bandage is equal when you wind it around according to its roundness.
Then the sick person is treated with a remedy for pleurisy from food and medicine.
If the affliction presses too hard on the sick person and hurts him with a sharp instrument, piercing his flesh by wounding it, then we fear for the sick man: then it is necessary that we cut through the place and expose the broken rib. Then we will place on it (the wound) an instrument that heals a sifac, whose name has been mentioned before: and we will cut the bone with ease, and we will cut it (the sifac).
Then we will join together two lips of the wound, if it is large with suture: and we will treat it with plasters until it heals.
If a hot abscess should happen meanwhile, then hurry and pour lice into rose oil, and place it on the spot: and the sick person is treated with what is suitable for treating an abscess.
The patient should also lie on the opposite side until he is cured.
On the Restoration of a Fracture of the Spine and Neck.
Fracture sometimes occurs in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that they are rubbed [against each other]: and similarly with the spondyles of the back. If this happens to someone and one desires to know whether it can be healed or not: then examine [the case]. For if you see the hands already softened, stunned, and dead; and it cannot move them, nor extend them, nor contract them; and when you press them with your fingers and prick them with a needle, it does not feel this or pain in them: then know that it will not heal, and in many cases it is mortal.
If it moves them and feels the pressure with your fingers and the prick: then know that the neck bone is sound, and that the weak one will heal with treatment.
If it happens with the spondyles of the back similarly to this case, and one desires to know whether it can be healed or not: then examine his feet; then if you see that they are softened and this happens in them as it happened in the hands; then when he lies on his back, he expels wind and faeces involuntarily; and when he lies on his abdomen, he expels faeces involuntarily; and when he lies on his back again and wishes to urinate, but cannot: then know that it is mortal. Therefore do not labor in treating it.
But if nothing of this happens to him, it is lighter [in nature].
And the treatment for this is to apply heat with a mustard plaster [to the affected spondyle]: so that you place oil of rose over the rubbed spondyle alone; or with hog's lard heated.
Place it on that place several times a day until the hot abscess is assuaged; then place one of the strengthening, drying, and binding plasters over it, and bind it with a ligament; and order the sick person to rest quietly and in peace. He shall not sleep on the part where he found pain, until it is healed.
If it happens due to the rubbing of a bone (sathaim), or something that is already separated from it: then it is necessary for him to cut across the skin and remove it. Then gather together two lips of the wound, if it is large, with suturing. Then care for himself with some soft dressing, from ointments, until he is healed.
If however the last bone (alhaws) of the shin splint is broken and it is the end of the heel: then it is necessary to insert the thumb of the left hand into the anus, and with the other hand to align the broken bone as much as possible, according to what is possible, and in a second alignment.
Then place him on it (the bone), and remove it; and care for the wound with the treatment that preceded it, until it is healed.
Chapter on the restoration of anus (Anca).
Chapter 11.
Fractures of the bones of the ankles are rare. If they are fractured, then the fracture is not anything except comminution at their extremities; and they are divided lengthwise, and slant towards the inside; and there occurs pain in that place, and puncturing; and the leg that was fractured becomes numb.
And its restoration is, that you extend your hand over it, until you stand over the fracture as its figure is.
If the fracture is only at its extremities, then equalize that fracture, according to what you prepare yourself from the equation, until it resembles its natural figure.
If however the fracture is in its length, or it already turns towards the inside: then make the weak one lie on his belly, until the restoration of that fracture is prepared for you. When you have equalized it, place a plaster on it; then place an astel (a splint) made of wood or hide over it and tie a suture on it where you are not afraid of altering the fracture or removing the splint.
And equal the concavity of them with what fills it until the suture takes it in accordance with the equality; and command the weak one to sleep on his back or on a healthy side.
If a hot abscess occurs to him: then stop extending it and its restoration until the hot abscess settles; and place whatever is beneath it on it, according to what has passed, then return to its restoration; and tie it as needed.
If however it happens to the bone that it swells or breaks out: extract it.
Chapter on the Restoration of Fractures.
The helper (tool) is that which is between the elbow and head of the spatula.
If it breaks, then its restoration is according to one of two methods.
One of these methods is: that you receive a flat wooden board of medium thickness, in the following shape.
And two ligaments are to be tied at both ends.
Then it is suspended from a raised place, and the weak one shall sit on the seat. Then he should throw his broken arm over a log until he reaches the notch of that log, where the break of the log is attached.
Then let something heavy be placed upon him from above, so that the servant may stretch him towards the lower parts. Then the physician shall set the fracture with his hands until it returns to its proper position.
And another method is that the weak one lies on his neck; and let his hand hang from his neck with a bandage. Then command two servants that one holds what is above the fracture with his hands; and let another hold below it, and each one of them stretches to his side.
And if you wish the extension to be stronger, then bind below the fracture with a bandage, and above it with another bandage; and let each of the two servants stretch to his own sides.
If therefore the fracture is close to the shoulder end, then it is necessary that one bandage be placed under the notch and another under the fracture towards the elbow.
And similarly if the fracture is close to the elbow, then it is necessary that a bandage be placed above that place and above the elbow itself.
Then set the fracture easily without difficulty, until it is level according to what is necessary, and applied correctly; then bind it if no warm abscess occurs.
But if a warm abscess occurs, then release the binding for seven days. Place linen that has been soaked in vinegar and rose oil on it until the abscess subsides; then bind it: and the method of binding is to place a plaster over the fracture.
Then place the inversion from new cloth over the plaster. Then gather the arm onto the support itself, and put his open hand on his own shoulder.
Place the cloth and bind it over the support so that the arm remains in place like a star: if something does not prevent you from doing this, nor will anything move due to a broken bone.
If you are afraid that something will move due to a broken bone, then use a star: and there is one, by which you place the larger and stronger star over the fracture itself. And place the width of each star equal to a digit: and let the length of the stars be according to the fracture, with an addition of three digits from every side.
Then bind over the stars with the bandage as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
And your binding should be tighter than the fracture site. And as the fracture extends more, let the binding be less.
If you see the position of the stars and the binding as we have said, then do it at the hour when you restore the limb immediately: but if you fear a hot abscess, then let go of the binding and the stars until the seventh day, as we have said.
Then consider the binding in all three days, so that it does not happen in the place of itching, or swelling, or food is prevented from reaching the limb because of the excess binding. Correct therefore everything as we have said.
If you are confident that nothing will happen from this: then do not loosen the binding, unless after three days or more.
Let the weak person sleep on his back and place his hand on his stomach: and put woolen socks full of wool equally under the support.
Consider at every hour of the night or day, so that the figure of the broken member is not loosened, nor is the ligament softened. Correct it entirely with your power.
Place food for the sick according to the order we have given you, so that it is a subtle food first, until the bone begins to bind; then it is necessary, that you increase his food.
For the custom of help and the member is to bind for forty days; then it is necessary, that it be loosened, and a bath be given, and it be treated with ointments which correct it.
If the fracture is foul, scrape it; then do not loosen from it the ligament and splints for fifty days, and until two months.
Chapter on the restoration of the broken arm.
The arm is composed of two bones, which are called two humeruses.
One of them is small; and it follows the thumb. And the other one is large, and it is placed below the small one from the lower part.
Perhaps only the large humerus breaks, or perhaps both break at once.
When therefore the small humerus above breaks, then its restoration is easy, and its healing is easier.
And when the large humerus below breaks, the fracture is bad, and the healing is difficult.
And it is worse when both bones break at once.
If the bone that breaks is the small humerus above, then it is fitting for the physician at its restoration, to place a sling smaller with ease until it equals itself.
If however the large humerus is the one that is broken: then it is necessary to place a strong splint very tightly.
It is necessary that [the figure] of the hand be placed at its restoration, and its [full] extension extended over the pulley. The thumb shall be higher than all the fingers, and the lower joint (of the thumb) shall be higher than all the digits or the rest: and the weakened square one resting on itself, and there shall be a pulley before it or directly in front of it, at its level, so that the weakened does not fall into labor.
Then let the attendant stretch the arm from its lower part with his hand or with a ligature. And another attendant shall stretch likewise from above.
Then the physician sets the bone until he brings it back to its best shape possible.
If there are pus-filled cavities (sinuses) in the bone fracture, then strive to replace every splinter in its place with your strength.
But if it appears separated and pustular (abscessed) and penetrating the skin and there is no hope of restoration for it: then incise over it, and excise it according to the manner which was previously mentioned.
But if there is a fracture with a wound, I have already written a separate chapter on this matter, so take care of it from that point.
If at the beginning of your restoration an abscess arises that is hot, then apply a linen cloth prepared with wax made from rose oil, white wax, and medium thickness: and bind the cloth over it tightly with a narrow ligature until when the abscess subsides: then remove the wax, and place an ointment prepared from flour mill powder and egg whites. Then place pins, and the pin that is placed over the fracture should be slightly larger and stronger.
And know that the number of pins for the arm is six in most cases: whether the fracture occurs in one splint or two splints at once.
Then place your bandage stronger and more forceful over the stronger and more prominent part of the fracture, and a little further towards its upper or lower parts: or place a softer bandage around it according to what was previously remembered at the beginning of the chapter.
The wrappings to be used on the fracture should be soft, moist: and they should not be hard, rough. And let the thread for binding be of linen, middle between fine and coarse, as we have said.
Consider the limb and ligament after several days. If anything happens which requires correction, such as itching on the limb: then it is necessary that you apply embrocation to the limb with warm water until the itching stops, and leave the limb unbound until it calms down; then repeat the bandaging.
If the bandage has already been softened and the bone removed, and similar things have happened: then correct that completely with your skill, and consider again.
If nutrition is prevented from reaching the limb due to excessive bandaging, then it is necessary to soften it slightly, and leave it for some days until it reaches the nutrition; then bind it again.
But if nothing of what has been said happens to the sick person, then it is not necessary to loosen him, unless after twenty days or thereabouts.
Then the hand of the sick person is suspended at his neck. And let his neck be straight, and keep it protected from violent movements. Make him sleep on his back.
And know that this fracture is healed within thirty or forty days; and perhaps it is healed within twenty-eight days. All of that depends on the temperaments and dispositions of humors and virtues.
Restoration of broken hands.
Know that the hand comb and finger knots rarely occur a fracture. It does not happen to him, unless it is rubbed many times.
When a foot fracture occurs or is rubbed, then it is necessary that the patient sits on a low stool, and before him there should be a seat equal in height. Then put his hand upon it extended.
Then the servant spreads out the broken bones, and the doctor aligns them until they are joined with a good union.
Then it is necessary to place plaster and wool, unless there occurs a hot abscess. Then put a splint on top according to the size of the place: and you have already wound it in linen cloth.
If the fracture is below about the belly of the foot, then make a similar sphere from cloth: and command the patient to bend over it with his broken foot: then tie it with long cloth.
And let the splint be of parchment, in which there is softness, so that it can be applied to the skin of the sole: and tie it as necessary.
If the fracture is on the outside, then it is necessary to place a splint on top and another one below on the foot: and keep the hand open and straight. Then put a bandage, as the hand is rolled up: and extend between the fingers with a ligament.
If there occurs a fracture in any finger knot, then if it is the thumb, align it as necessary. Then tie with the foot: and if there are any more, place a straight splint, smaller, to lift the fracture and not move it.
If the fracture is in the remaining fingers, such as the middle, index, little finger or ring finger, then align it and tie it with the healthy finger that follows it: or tie all of them according to continuity: and it is better. Place a small awl upon it [the part], as we have said in the thumb.
And consider in your restoration, and after the arrangement of the amputation of heat, and set against it what is required, when something happens from that [object], according to its repeated narrative.
Chapter on the repair of a broken Hip.
The thigh bone is often broken and revealed to the senses because it turns towards the inner and posterior part.
And its repair is done by tightening a ligament above the break, and another ligament below the break. The sick person stretches himself upon his face.
Then extend all the ligaments serving its part equally; and this when the break is in the middle of the bone.
If however the break is close to the root of the hip, then let there be a ligament for the neck part, so that the extension falls upward; and another ligament below the break.
And similarly if the break is close to the knee, then let there be a ligament near the knee, so that the extension falls towards the lower parts.
Then the physician adjusts the bone with both hands until he reduces it to its original shape; and the bone unites by a good union.
Then it is necessary that you apply plaster and a tight bandage if no abscess occurs in the limb. If an abscess should occur there: then let it be left for several days until the abscess becomes hot; then return to your treatment.
The bandage of this [limb] should therefore be as follows. It is necessary to wind a hard plaster around the break, that is, bandage; and double it twice or three times; and there remains an excess of it. Then wind the leg until the heel reaches the root of the natural joint.
Insert a long thread between the hip and the leg near the knee towards the lower parts, and let the ends of the thread come from the upper parts of the two areas. Then roll up (the skin) over the leg and hip what remains from the incision.
Next, place stars (splints or bandages) on the hip in the location of the fracture, and place one star on the bone of the leg.
Then fill the voids between the leg and hip with soft cloths so that it matches the tightness (of the wound).
Then begin with a strong suture from the middle above the location of the fracture with three or four revolutions. And as you lengthen the suture from the location of the fracture, let your stitch be smaller, softer, and looser.
Next, aim for the ends of the thread which you inserted between the hip and leg. Then bind three stars (splints or bandages) on both sides (of the wound). Next, follow the ends of the thread to the lower parts until you reach the ankle. And with both sides bind also the ends of the stars so that the suture is not moved from its place.
